Chapter 13pro


The night was cold as Zara trudged forward, her back aching with every step. A trickle of blood ran down her right arm, staining the tattered sleeve of her suit. Some flakes, that reminded her of Snow, fell silently from the sky, dusting the ground in a still, unsettling silence.
She had crash-landed on an unknown planet.
Her gaze flicked toward the wreckage—the twisted remains of the ship that was supposed to carry her safely through the stars. Smoke still rose from the debris, curling into the darkness above. How?
There had been no asteroids. No signs of mechanical failure. The engineers had assured her the ship was perfectly intact before launch. And yet…
She was here. Alone.
The air held oxygen—thankfully—but it felt strange. Heavy. Almost alive.
She’d managed to breathe upon impact, but something about the atmosphere felt off. Dense. Pulsing in a way she couldn’t quite place. She didn’t have time to dwell on it now—she needed shelter.
Spotting a darkened cave, she stumbled toward it and collapsed inside. Drawing her knees to her chest, Zara pressed her forehead against them, trying to steady her shaking breath. She wanted to cry, but the tears refused to fall.
Her mind drifted—Flora.
Her sister’s hazel eyes, bright and fearless, paired with that shimmering red hair. How often had Zara imagined the day Flora would finally make it to Space School? How had she seemed when she left—excited? Scared?
And Nathan. Her brother. The quiet observer with piercing blue eyes and black hair. They, but he was family all the same.
Had they heard what happened? Did they know? Were they safe?
Zara squeezed her eyes shut, whispering a silent prayer for their protection.
But as the words left her lips, a thought crept in—an unsettling presence lurking at the edge of her mind.
She had made enemies at Space School. Not everyone had welcomed her plans, her discoveries, her existence.
Would they do something like this? Sabotage the ship?
She hoped—prayed—that wasn’t true.
But deep down, she feared the answer wasn’t the one she wanted.


Chapter 1
**Zara Footsteps**
**Flora P. O. V**
Flora walked down the space school hallway, each step echoing with the weight of Zara’s absence. The scientists’ words still haunted her—no wreckage, no signal, no way to find her sister’s body. Just silence.
Her sister was dead, and her friends vanished, Nova, Amika, everyone.
She clutched her books tighter, steadying her breath. She and Zara had always been different—Flora, quiet and observant, with curly red hair and blue eyes; Zara, taller, bolder, with straight hair and a smile that could melt tension in a room. Opposites, but inseparable.
Colten—her adopted father—had said Zeb, her boyfriend, would pick her up after class. Flora wasn’t sure what to expect. She hadn’t seen him since the crash, and just the thought of facing him made her chest tighten, a wave of emotions threatening to overwhelm her.


In that moment, the memory pierced through the shadows of her mind, bringing both comfort and heartache.
She saw Zara again, sitting with her in their dimly lit room. Her sister’s eyes were bright, yet shadowed with an unspoken understanding.
“One day,” Zara had said, her voice steady but tinged with urgency, “you will walk the same halls I walked. You’re going to need to know how to be strong, how to keep your eyes on the Lord, especially when everything feels like it’s falling apart.”
Flora’s heart had ached. “I get it… But you’ll be with me on my first day, right?”
Zara sighed and shook her head slowly, as if the weight of the world rested on her shoulders. “The day I finally get to fly, V78, is happening this week; yours is a week after that. I will be far out in outer space. Remember that?”
“But why can’t you just… try?” Flora pleaded, fragile hope flickering in her chest.
Zara’s response came soft yet firm. “As much as I long to be there with you, you know I can’t.”
Zara smiled. “And as much I would like for you and Zeb to come with me, I know that can't happen.”
The pain in her eyes mirrored Flora’s own. Their shared dreams had faded like echoes against the stark walls of reality.
She missed her with everything she had. Why would a good God let her sister perish in such a way?
The voices around them echoed off the polished surfaces of the space school’s main corridor, low, scattered conversations mingling with the hum of boots against the cold metal flooring.
Laughter erupted occasionally among the students, a haunting reminder of what should have been. Flora felt a weight as she inhaled the faint scent, which reminded her of Zara. The school had it. Each breath she took was a reminder that Zara would never be there to share it with. Leaving Flora to navigate the halls alone, forever changed by the past.


Flora moved through the crowd like a ghost, clutching her books close. She didn’t know what the whispers were saying—didn’t want to. Her presence felt too loud, too visible, like grief had marked her in a way everyone could see.
Then two girls broke from the flow of students and strode toward her.
“Hey, look who dropped in. A newbie?” said the first, her brown hair pulled tight, dark eyes sharp with something that wasn’t curiosity.
The girl beside her looked similar—same angular features, but paler, more hesitant. She lingered a step behind.
Flora offered a small smile, trying to keep her voice steady. “Nice to meet you. I’m Flora.”
The first girl scoffed. “No one asked for your name.”
Flora sighed. Her first day, of course, each school had to have one of these ignorant people. Her movement is calm, she will stay calm, not feel threatened, like the movies.
The second girl shifted, uneasy. “Nalie, she’s Flora. You know what hap—”
“I don’t care who she is,” Nalie snapped, cutting her off. Her voice was louder now, drawing a few glances from nearby students.
Nalie's eyes suddenly changed; what was once a scoff now looked terrified.
Her tone changed—sweet, sudden, and false. “Hi, Alfred. We were just talking.”
Flora turned. Alfred stood behind her, silent and still, his gaze cold enough to freeze a star. He wore the same blue Space School blazer as she did, his brown eyes steady beneath tousled hair. His Asian features and quiet confidence made it clear—he’d walked these halls more times than he cared to count.
“Were you now?” he said, voice quiet but heavy.
Both girls nodded quickly, their confidence draining.
“Well then,” he said, low and deliberate, “how about you move along—before this gets ugly.”
The hallway seemed to hush around them. The girls didn’t argue. They turned and disappeared into the crowd, their footsteps quick and uneven.
Flora felt the blood drain from her face. “Uh, hi, I don’t—”
Alfred’s expression softened. He smiled, and somehow, she calmed.
“No need to worry,” he said gently. “Come on. I’ll walk you to class. Zara’s sister, right?”
Flora swallowed. The mention of her sister tightened something in her chest, like a string pulled taut. “Yes,” she rasped.
Alfred smiled, not unkindly. “Room 1234, yeah? Let’s get you there.”
He strode through the hallways with the easy grace of a senior student, moving with quiet confidence. Flora followed, keeping pace beside him. Her eyes scanned the unfamiliar halls, trying not to feel too small. Normally, anxiety would grip her, but a sense of peace surrounded her, like a whisper from the Lord in her heart: "I'm with you."
The divine whisper carried such certainty that for a moment, her doubts melted away. She was His child, chosen for a purpose she couldn't yet see. Even if she couldn't understand.
“She always said her little sister would end up here someday,” Alfred told her.
Once they went up the stairs, a window peered through her vision. Her steps slowed, a small smile tugging at her lips as she glanced toward the classroom.
“That’s Mr. Colten’s class.”
Alfred followed her gaze. “I’ve heard he’s one of the best teachers here.” He paused, catching himself. “I mean—from what people have told me since I transferred.”
“He’s my adopted father,” Flora said softly, surprised by how natural the words felt. Saying it aloud grounded her. “After our dad passed away, he took us in—me, Zara, and Nathan. He’s been there ever since.”
Alfred’s eyes widened. “Really? I knew he was close to Zara, but I didn’t realize…” He looked back at Mr. Colten with new respect. “That explains a lot. No wonder she always spoke so highly of him.”
Flora nodded, her throat tightening. Watching him teach made space exploration possible again—like something Zara would still be proud of.


**Alfred P. O. V**
Alfred gestured gently. “Come on. Room 1234’s just around the corner. We don’t want you to be late on your first day.”
Flora nodded and followed him through the winding corridors of Space School. Her steps were slow, deliberate—like each carried more weight than it should.
That glow around her again. He’d seen it once in Zara. Familiar, but not the same.
He blinked it away. Maybe it was just his eyes. Maybe…or was it something else? He trailed back in his mind. Zara's words.
“I see light around you,” Zara said to a woman Alfred did not recognize. The woman looked up and gave a bright smile. “I do. The lord told me to tell you that you are loved by God, that you are not forgotten.”


Alfred shook the memory. Room 1234 came into view. Alfred knew exactly where it was; it was the same room he’d entered on his first day.
Zara, who had been like family to him.
He glanced at Flora. She clutched her books tightly, guarded. She reminded him of the promise he’d made—to protect her and Nathan. Zara had asked him to, just before she boarded the ship.
He intended to keep it.
At the door, he paused. “Here’s your class,” he said, placing a hand on her shoulder. “If you need anything, I’m here. I mean that.”
She hesitated, her blue eyes searching his face for sincerity.
“Flora, you can trust me,” Alfred said, his voice low, steady.
Her eyes flicked away, guarded like she’d heard those words before—and been let down.
But then she nodded and stepped inside.
Alfred watched her go, jaw tight. He wouldn’t let history repeat itself.
He’d find the truth—about Zara, the explosion, and Nathan’s missing sister.
No matter what it costs.
**Letzier P. O. V**
Letzier positioned himself for battle as Blade lunged with a kick. In one swift motion, he caught Blade's foot, yanked him down, and locked him in a chokehold, securing his wrists and keeping him grounded—merciful, but firm.
Coach Andrew’s familiar grin lingered. But something about it felt off. A flicker in his expression gave Letzier a strange vibe.
“Time! Letzier, you win!” the coach called, his smile still fixed in place.
Letzier straightened, breath steady, muscles humming from the match. Questions loomed—about the coach’s expression, about the unease in the room—but he shoved them aside.
“Of course I did,” Letzier said, brushing dust from his sleeve. But his eyes stayed on the coach’s faltering smile.
He walked over to Blade and lifted his hand.
“Thanks,” Blade muttered.
Letzier nodded. “No problem.” He considered offering training help—Blade could use it—but decided against it. His life was too full.
Space School was his focus. And beneath the drills and classes, one mission drove him: finding Zara.
It wasn’t about whether she was dead. That wasn’t the question. It was about the lie. The launch had been rushed. The scientists said everything was fine. But Letzier didn’t believe them.
Zara had been like a sister. She’d brought him and Daisy together. And Daisy—he couldn’t bear the sorrow in her eyes. Every time he thought of Zara, his chest tightened.
She didn’t just vanish. She was stolen by a promise that wasn’t kept.
He sat on the bench, water bottle in hand, but barely tasted it. His mind was elsewhere—racing, aching. He should’ve checked the ship himself. Should’ve asked harder questions. Should’ve stopped her.
The crash hadn’t given him enough proof. Just fragments. Just silence.
He would find out what really happened. And when he does, he will make them pay.
“Hey, Letzier, you good?” Coach Andrew’s voice cut through the haze.
Letzier blinked, then nodded. “Yeah.”
Andrew studied him for a moment, concern flickering behind his usual calm. But he didn’t press.
“Okay. Tell Alfred I said hi, would ya?”
Letzier gave him a questioning look. But nodded.
“I will. I’m heading to my next class. See you next week.”
Letzier stood, the weight of his promise pressing against his chest. He’d made it to Daisy. To himself. To Zara.
He wouldn’t let her story end in a lie.
Class 87 was next.


The halls leading there were quieter, the air heavier. Fewer students walked this path—only those willing to confront what others ignored. It wasn’t just a class. It was a threshold. A place built for those who had lost someone, or suspected the truth had been buried beneath protocol and polished reports.


He and Alfred had chosen it together. Not for credits. Not for prestige. But for answers.
Class 87 was confidential. A course designed for those investigating failed missions, vanished crew, and the shadows left behind. It was where whispers became data, where grief met resolve, where Letzier hoped to find the thread that would lead him back to Zara—or at least to the truth of what stole her.
He walked toward the door, pulse steady, heart braced. Whatever Class 87 held, he was ready to face it.


Chapter
**Nathan P. O. V**
Nathan sat quietly as Mr. Colten spoke, but his attention had already drifted. He wasn’t really listening—not the way he should’ve been. His gaze wandered to the window, and there she was. His sister.
A small smile tugged at Nathan’s lips. She didn’t notice him, but that was okay. He was proud of her—whether she knew it or not. He breathed, remembering how hard this was for her. He knew how it felt, having been there himself, having missed his own sister, not knowing if she was alive, and now Zara. How much more could he lose? He sighed. A sharp snap broke the moment.
“Nathan, are you listening?” Mr. Colten asked, his voice gentle, a faint smile playing at the corners of his mouth.
Nathan turned back, matching the smile. “If I’m being honest... no. Not really.”
Mr. Colten nodded. “we'll, then you’d know we have an upcoming test.”
Nathan nodded out of habit, but his thoughts had already slipped away once more.
He remembered the day Flora’s parents adopted him and Reanna. He’d been nine—too young to grasp the full weight of loss, but old enough to feel its shape. Flora and Zara’s parents had died, and Colten had stepped in, gathering them all like scattered stars and trying to make a new constellation. Back then, it felt like healing. Like hope.
But now… Zara was gone, and Reanna was missing. And the cold truth settled in his chest like frost. He hadn’t realized how much he’d lost until it was too late.
The silence around it all was the worst part. No answers. Just absence. And the ache that came with knowing he couldn’t protect the people he loved.


He couldn't remember the last time they all smiled. The last time they could breathe. Even if he could breathe, it felt more like pain.


**Alfred P. O. V**
Alfred marched toward Class 87, his mind racing with questions about Zara. The hallway buzzed—chatter, lockers slamming, sneakers squeaking—but he barely registered it. His thoughts were elsewhere. Back to the first day he saw Zara.
He’d walked into Space School, full of dreams he couldn’t afford. Studying there had always felt out of reach. Still, he waited for Letzier, hoping they’d hang out, maybe play Minecraft, and forget the weight of reality.
Then Letzier appeared—mid-conversation with a somewhat short girl, her brown hair tucked behind one ear. Beside her stood another girl, her hair a fiery mix of orange and red. Letzier smiled. “Hey, Alfred. This is Daisy and Zara.” Alfred smiled back. “Hi.”
The memory echoed through him like a distant song. Emotions swirled—nostalgia, confusion, urgency. He had to see her. He had to find out. Someone had sabotaged it. He could feel it.
Dan popped up beside him, leaning casually against the wall. “You look like you’re about to storm the principal’s office,” he said with a grin. “Relax, man. It’s not a crime to be mysterious.”
Alfred gave a half-smile, stepping out of memory and back into reality. “Depends on the mystery.”
Dan winked. “we'll, if you find out the vending machine’s been rigged, I want in.”
Before Alfred could reply, Stone stepped into view—calm, unreadable, like a shadow that had learned to smile.
“Alfred,” Stone said, voice smooth. “Still chasing ghosts?” Stone said, as if he could read his thoughts.
Alfred stiffened. “Still pretending you’re not one?”
Stone’s smile didn’t falter. “Careful. Some ghosts bite.”
Alfred smiled. “
He walked past, leaving a trail of unease in his wake.
Alfred exhaled, tension still coiled in his chest—until Azreal appeared beside him, backpack slung over one shoulder, radiating calm.
“Don’t let him get in your head,” Azreal said quietly. “God’s light cuts through every shadow.”
Alfred nodded, the words grounding him. He nodded.
“Thanks, I think,” he said.
Azreal offered a small smile. “Let’s head to 87. Letzier’s waiting.”
And just like that, he was moving. Alfred followed, steadier now, the tension from earlier beginning to fade.
As they walked, Azreal glanced over. “I heard Zara’s sister is here now?”
Alfred nodded, a faint smile tugging at his lips. “Yeah. Flora just transferred. I walked her to class. Nalie was already stirring things up.”
Azreal sighed. “Figures. Nalie really needs to back off.”
Alfred nodded. “She’s been extra lately.”
They reached the door to Class 87, where Letzier stood waiting, arms crossed and unimpressed.
“Took y’all long enough,” he said, raising a brow. “You’re usually early, Alfred.”
Alfred shrugged. “Flora just transferred. I was showing her around. And Nalie… we'll, you know.”
Letzier rolled his eyes. “Classic.”
Then he turned to Azreal. “Sup, Azreal.”
Azreal smiled. “Hey. How’s the 87 Crue holding up?”
Letzier sighed. “Slow as always. Everyone’s dragging today.”
Class 87 was quiet—just a few scattered students. Alfred knew them all: Elora, who always showed up like it was her duty; Lunna and Ava, who shared Elora’s quiet resolve but rarely spoke; and Julie, who kept her distance, headphones in, eyes elsewhere.
They weren’t exactly close. Conversations were rare, and when they happened, they felt more like passing shadows than real connections.
Azreal leaned against the wall, scanning the room. “Flora’s not in this class, right?”
Alfred shook his head. “Nah, she’s in 1234. Like I said before.”
Azreal nodded. “Nalie is just… Nalie. Hard to talk to her when her mind’s locked on one thing. You might want to keep an eye on Flora, just in case.”
Alfred nodded. Out of the corner of his eye, he saw Letzier cracking his knuckles, a gleam flickering in his gaze.
Azreal shook his head. “Really? Already planning to stir things up?”
Letzier glanced toward the hallway.
“If Flora’s anything like Zara, she won’t stay quiet for long. And neither will I.”
Azreal smiled faintly. “Everyone knows Zara. Hard not to.”
Alfred settled in his seat, and so did Azreal.
Alfred nodded, the weight of that truth settling between them. Zara had left a mark—and now Flora was walking through the echoes.
He turned to Azreal. “Think you’ll get a chance to meet Flora? Maybe hang out after school?”
Azreal hesitated, then exhaled. “I’d love to, but things are kinda packed right now. Mom and Dad have me on my tiptoes—chores, Bible class, all of it. There’s this new kid, Sileth, in Bible class. He and I were talking about handing out Bibles together. And we’re going camping once summer hits.”
Alfred chuckled. “You’re always doing something.”
Azreal smiled, a quiet warmth in his eyes. Before either of them could say more, the classroom door slid open and the teacher stepped in, clipboard in hand.
“Alright, Class,” he said, voice firm but calm, “here’s what we’re diving into today.”
The room settled. Conversations faded. Alfred shifted in his seat, the weight of everything—Zara, Flora, Stone—still lingering at the edges of his thoughts. But for now, Class 87 demanded his focus.
And somewhere beneath the surface, he hoped today’s lesson might bring him one step closer to the truth.
**Letzier P. O. V**
Letzier pulled out his phone between classes, his fingers hovering over Daisy's name. She was his first thought after that intense training session—she always was.
"How are you?" he texted.
The response came quickly: "Not too good really."
Letzier's jaw tightened, worry settling in his chest. He knew what those words meant—she was probably in the garden again, surrounded by the flowers she and Zara had planted together. These were the days he hated being stuck at Space School, when all he wanted was to be there for her.
"Want me to come over after class? We could grab something to eat, or just talk." He added a heart emoji—something he'd never done before Daisy, but now it felt natural.
While waiting for her response, he leaned against the hallway wall, running a hand through his hair. Sometimes it felt like he was being pulled in two directions—the need to find answers about Zara's disappearance, and the desire to be there for Daisy every moment she needed him. The weight of both responsibilities pressed heavily on his shoulders.
His phone buzzed again. "Please. Dad's been hovering all morning. Could use a rescue."
A small smile crossed his face. Even on her bad days, she still had that spark of humor. "Consider it done. Two more classes and I'm all yours."
He tucked his phone away, straightening his uniform. He remembered the first day he met Daisy…it still feels like it was yesterday.
He had just completed lesson 101 of survival training, and it was time to focus on practice. As he was about to leave, he spotted Zara talking with Zeb and a girl. He stopped, assessing the situation. Zara waved him over, and without hesitation, he approached.
Zeb acknowledged him with a slight nod, but his attention remained on the women. The girl looked up at him with her short, dark brown hair and hazel eyes, prompting him to smile.
Zara smirked confidently and introduced her, saying, “This is Daisy.”
Letzier gave his hand out, “I’m Letzier,” she gave her hand, and he held it for a while. didn't want to let go.
She smiled. “Aren't you busy?”
He swallowed. “Right.”
He'd find Zara—for both of them. But right now, Daisy needed him, and that was all that mattered.
Chapter
**Flora**
Flora stepped into the mechanics lab 45, her eyes adjusting to the cooler lighting and metallic surfaces. It was her first time here, and everything felt foreign—screens emitted a soft hum, wires trailed across the floor, and a faint scent of ozone lingered in the air.
Alfred was already seated near the front, focused on his interface. He didn’t look up.
At the center of the room, a containment orb hovered in a magnetic field. It pulsed with a soft blue light—steady, rhythmic, almost calming.
Flora paused, watching it flicker.
She’d never seen anything like it before. But something about it felt… familiar. Not in memory, but in feeling. Like she’d overheard someone mention it once—Quantum Glow, wasn’t that what they called it?
She didn’t know what it meant. She didn’t even know if it was important. But the way the light moved—it caught her attention.
Miss Rylin turned from the board and noticed her lingering presence.
“You must be Flora,” she said, smiling. “Welcome to Mechanics. Everyone, this is her first day—let’s make her feel at home.”
Flora nodded, cheeks warm. “Thank you.”
She took her seat near the back, trying to focus as the lesson began. The orb continued to pulse, unnoticed by most. But Flora glanced at it again, once.
She didn’t understand it. But she saw it. After finishing Mechanics 45, Flora hurried to her next class, Survival 101. She settled into her seat, eager and focused, as the instructor began to outline critical survival skills. Every explanation captivated her, and she focused on her notes, believing that each detail could be crucial for the future. Flora was determined to soak up all the knowledge she could. Class Survival 101—her final class of the day, before she could finally go home. The shift felt strange, like stepping into a quieter chapter, where even the air seemed to hold its breath. She tried to ignore Nalie, seated just a few rows away. The tension simmered, but Flora kept her focus locked on the lesson. Then the bell rang. Class was over. Then—bam.
Someone slammed into Flora’s shoulder, sending her notebook skidding across the floor. She stumbled, heart racing. “Watch it,” Nalie muttered without looking back. Flora crouched to gather her pages, cheeks burning, but before she could speak, a tall boy stepped forward—blond hair, hazel eyes, sharp and unfamiliar. Without hesitation, he kicked Nalie’s leg out from under her. She hit the floor with a yelp. Gasps from the other students.
“Try that again,” he said, voice low, “and you’ll regret it.”
Nalie scrambled away.
Flora froze. She didn’t know him. But Alfred was beside him now, calm and steady.
“Flora,” Alfred said gently, “you okay?”
She nodded, still shaken. The boy glanced at Alfred. “She’s with you?” Alfred nodded. “She’s Zara’s sister.” The boy’s expression shifted—recognition, maybe guilt. He crouched beside her. “I’m Letzier.” Flora blinked. The name rang a bell; she remembered Zara mentioning him before, but she couldn’t speak. She didn’t know any of Zara’s friends—she’d always been too afraid to meet them.
Alfred knelt to help gather her papers. Letzier joined him. Their quiet presence steadied her.
“Thank you,” she whispered. Alfred nodded. “No problem.”
“I need to get home,” she said softly. “Nathan’s waiting.”
“I’ll walk you,” Alfred offered, standing. Just then, another boy approached—blue eyes, hazel hair, calm presence.
“Is she alright?” he asked. “She is. Thanks, Azreal.” Alfred replied. Azreal looked at Flora and smiled.
“Nice to see you, Flora. I’d stay, but I’ve got Bible class and chores.” He gave a small wave and disappeared into the crowd.
Flora’s fingers trembled. Her breath caught. She just wanted to go home. She wanted Zara, she wanted her Sister, that's all, that's all she wanted.
Alfred noticed her trembling, “Are you sure you're okay?”
He asked in a gentle tone. Flora only nodded. She held her hand up. “It's okay, really. I can go by myself. Nathan, my cousin, will be outside waiting for me.”
Alfred hesitated but nodded. “As you wish.”
He let her leave.
She walked the halls with her head low, the hum of voices fading behind her. Her prayer was silent, but urgent—Lord, give me peace. She started to sing as it had always calmed her down, when the fear gripped her like this. Flora knew, though, it was the feeling of not having her sister by her side, or would ever be by her side. Ever.


**Nathan**
Nathan stood outside the school building, the cool air swirling around him, but it did little to refresh his heavy heart. Colten’s machinery class had left his mind buzzing—reactor systems, override protocols, emergency drills. It was all useful, but none of it touched the ache in his chest.
Zara had promised they would find his sister together. Now that she was gone, the silence she left behind was deafening.
Nathan took a deep breath, feeling the weight of his long-lost sister, Reanna, pressing down on him. She couldn’t just vanish; he had already lost his parents—losing his sister, too, was simply unacceptable.
Nathan sat hunched on the stone steps, elbows on his knees, staring at the ground as if the answers might be carved into the dust. The night pressed close around him, heavy and silent, broken only by the faint rustle of leaves in the wind.
A light tap on his shoulder startled him. He turned, and there was Zara, her face half-lit by the lantern glow. “You alright, cousin?” she asked softly.
His throat tightened. “No, I’m not alright,” Nathan said, the words sharper than he intended.
Zara didn’t flinch. She lowered herself beside him, smoothing her skirt as she sat. “It’s about Reanna, isn’t it?”
Nathan’s jaw worked as he nodded. “She’s still out there. I can feel it.” His voice cracked on the last word, and he hated how fragile it sounded.
For a moment, Zara’s eyes shimmered with her own unspoken fear. Then she drew in a steadying breath and met his gaze with quiet fire. “I believe that too. We will find her—together. It might not happen today, but it will happen.”
The conviction in her tone cut through the fog of despair that had been suffocating him. Nathan blinked, surprised by the sudden warmth in his chest. Hope—small, stubborn, but real—stirred.


He leaned against the railing, watching the students pass by. Then he saw Flora. She stepped out of the building, her red hair catching the light, her steps quick but thoughtful. When her eyes found his, she smiled, but she looked tense.
Nathan straightened and asked, “How was class?”
As he spoke, her shoulders relaxed slightly. She was indeed shy, and he hoped she might be comfortable around the people Zara loved. However, that thought seemed to fade away. Flora rolled her eyes playfully. “Alive. Survival training felt like we were prepping for a crash landing tomorrow.”
Nathan chuckled. “Colten had me in the control room. Reactor shutdown drills. He kept saying, ‘If you hesitate, you die.’ Real motivational.”
Flora laughed softly. “Sounds like him.”
Nathan nodded. “Saw you with Alfred earlier. What do you think of him?”
Flora hesitated, then shrugged. “He’s quiet. Protective. I think he’s very observant when it looks like he's not.”
Nathan smirked. “That’s Alfred.”
They stood together for a moment, the breeze brushing past them. The moment felt normal—almost peaceful. But Nathan could feel the weight behind it. Flora’s smile didn’t reach her eyes. His own thoughts kept circling back to Zara.
“She would have loved the survival class,” Flora said suddenly, her voice softer. Nathan nodded. “She would have aced it and then come to help us if we struggled,” he said. Flora smiled, but it faded quickly.
“Something happened.”
Nathan turned toward her. “What do you mean?”
She looked down at her hands. “Nalie was in my class. She bumped me—hard. Knocked my notebook out of my hands.”
Nathan’s jaw tightened. “Did she say anything?”
“Just ‘watch it,’ like it was my fault.” Flora’s voice was quiet, but steady.
Nathan felt heat rise in his chest. “Did anyone see?”
Flora nodded.
“He didn’t say anything right away,” Flora continued.
Nathan stared at her, trying to read the emotion behind her words. “Are you okay?”
Flora shrugged.
“I’m alright, I didn't expect this to happen on my first day.” Flora hugged herself, but then she looked up.
"I hear it's worth it. The progress and the pain of studying lead you to what you love doing. If God has called you, shouldn't you pursue it?"


Nathan nodded and pondered the idea. Zara, Zeb, and even he shared a passion for the stars and space, all wanting to explore them.

The moment shattered. He was annoyed at himself; he really should have picked a better spot, mostly indoors than outdoors, where everyone could hear him.
The figure stood firm, hood pulled low, mask covering most of the face — but there was something familiar. Letzier's pulse quickened. He knew this person. The way they moved, the way their voice carried just enough weight... But he couldn't place it.
The figure's stance didn't waver. "Get up. Both of you," the voice said.
Letzier's muscles tensed, every instinct screaming at him to fight back — but not yet. Not until he knew. He kept his voice steady. "Or what?"
The masked figure tilted their head slightly. "Or I'll shoot." The quietness of their tone unsettled him more than the gun.
Slowly, Letzier raised his hands, standing. Daisy followed, still shaking.
Then, as if sensing the energy shift, the figure took another step forward, their hood still concealing much of their face, but not the eyes — those purple eyes. The realization crept into his mind like an unspoken warning.
"You've been looking for me?" The words left the figure's lips with a strange finality.
And suddenly, he knew. His breath caught, his gaze narrowing. His voice was steady when he said the name.
**"Nova."**
His muscles relaxed, and a small smile fell on his lips. She was defiant — she wouldn't kill him, but he did wonder: Why here, why now? But he did wonder: Why here, why now?

**Letzier**

But then—another movement.
A woman stepped from the shadows, tapping Stone’s shoulder. Alfred slowed, confusion rippling through him. She wore a jean jacket, and her black hair fell past her shoulders. She leaned in close, whispering something in Stone’s ear. Alfred crept closer, careful not to draw attention. Fragments of their conversation drifted back to him. “Letzier… I know where Daisy is…” Her voice was low and controlled. Alfred couldn’t catch everything, but he heard enough.
Stone smiled, nodded, and walked away. Before the woman could follow, Alfred struck. She was stronger than she looked—he had to fight to restrain her. But before he could demand answers, she twisted free of his grip on her mouth.
“Really?” she said, her tone sharp with confidence. “You should’ve stayed behind, Alfred.”
He blinked, thrown off balance. “How do you know me?” She laughed softly.
“Where’s Letzier?” he demanded, tightening his grip.
“He’s safe. So is Daisy.” Her voice carried a warning. “But you should let me go before you get hurt, Brutal Alfred.”
Alfred growled. That name—he hadn’t heard it since Zara. His arms stayed locked around her, unmoved by the threat.
“Don’t call me that,” he snarled.
She smiled, unfazed. “Your glares don’t scare me, Brutal Alfred. But it was nice to meet you. Give Letzier my regards—and remember your promise to Zara.”
She leaned in, her voice dropping to a whisper.
**“Protect Flora.”**
Alfred’s breath caught. That name—Zara's sister. In that split second of surprise, she moved. Everything blurred. A flash of motion. A sharp impact. Then—darkness.
Chapter
**Alfred**
The world swam back into focus as Alfred turned his head, the dull throb in his skull pulsing with every heartbeat. A girl knelt beside him, dusty blonde hair catching the low light. But it was her eyes that stopped him—one blue, one brown. Too specific, too strange to be a dream.
“Who are—”
“Shh.” Her voice was sharp, edged with annoyance. “I’m Amika.”
Amika. Right. He was probably hallucinating. Attacked by a girl, rescued by another. Not exactly how he’d planned to spend his evening.
Then he heard it—his name, echoing down the hall.
**“Alfred?!”**
Flora’s voice rang out, and Alfred forced himself upright, ignoring the pounding in his head.
“Are you okay?” he asked, concern overriding discomfort.
Flora raised an eyebrow. “Alfred, I’m not the one who just got knocked out.”
Amika shook her head, tension flickering across her face. “Flora, I thought you went to bed.”
“I’m sixteen,” Flora replied, voice sharp. “Give me a break.”
Alfred gave a weak smile. “It’s okay,” he muttered, wincing.
Amika nodded, but her expression didn’t soften.
"Where’s Colten?” Alfred asked, voice low.
Amika’s face hardened. “He’s busy.”
Flora stepped closer, noticing the shift in Amika’s demeanor. “Amika, are you okay?”
She placed a hand on Amika’s shoulder, but Amika shrugged it off.
“I’m fine,” she said quickly, too quickly. “You haven’t been yourself since Dan came by.”
Dan. The name hit Alfred like a jolt. He remembered seeing Stone—Dan’s brother—lurking near Colten’s house. His jaw clenched.
He locked eyes with Amika.
“Amika,” he said, voice steady, “I don’t want to ask again. Where is Colten?”
Just then, Colten appeared through the corridor, a faint smile playing on his lips—too casual for the tension in the room.
“You good, Alfred?” he asked, voice light, almost teasing.
Alfred blinked at him, still seated, head pounding. “Define good,” he muttered, rubbing his temple.
Colten chuckled, but there was something unreadable in his eyes. “You’re conscious. That’s a start.”
Alfred narrowed his gaze. “You knew Stone was nearby. Didn’t you?”
Colten’s smile didn’t fade, but it didn’t reach his eyes either. “I know a lot of things.”
Alfred pushed himself up straighter, ignoring the ache in his skull. “Then start talking.”
Colten nodded, his gaze shifting to Amika, then to Flora. Amika gave a subtle nod.
“Come on, Flora,” she said. “Let’s get something for Alfred’s head.”
Flora looked confused, her expression clearly skeptical. She wasn’t having it.
Alfred caught her hesitation and spoke gently. “Listen to Amika.”
Flora sighed loudly. “Fine.”
As the girls disappeared down the hall, Colten moved to the table and sat. Alfred followed, lowering himself into the chair with a wince.
Colten’s eyes locked onto Alfred’s, his tone suddenly serious. “Have you ever heard of the BNA?”
Alfred blinked, confused. “Um… probably not.”
Colten nodded slowly. “They’re an organization. Ruthless. Focused on taking over the government from the inside.”
Alfred didn’t respond, but his silence spoke volumes.
“Keep talking,” he said, voice low.
Colten leaned forward. “They’re eliminating anyone who still has a conscience. People with heart. People who resist. And they’re growing stronger—day by day.”
He paused, letting the weight of it settle.
“BNA stands for Base Network Assassins.”
Alfred’s stomach tightened.
“I’ve been trying to stop them,” Colten said, his voice low. “But with only a handful of allies, it’s not easy. The agent who knocked you out earlier—she’s one of mine. You don’t know her… but Nathan does. Very we'll.”
Alfred looked up sharply, breath catching in his throat. A name slipped out, barely a whisper.
“Reanna?” The air seemed to shift. Anger surged in his chest, not just at the revelation—but at the truth it confirmed. Nathan—his biological sister—was alive.
Colten saw it. The tension in Alfred’s eyes. The storm behind them.
“It wasn’t a choice, Alfred,” Colten said quietly.
His eyes shimmered with something raw—regret, maybe even pain.
Alfred held his gaze for a long moment. Then, slowly, the fury in his chest began to fade. He gave a single, reluctant nod.
Colten exhaled. “I need you to do something for me.”
Alfred looked at him, curiosity flickering behind his tired eyes.
“Find Letzier,” Colten said. “Tell him… I want to talk Bible.” Alfred frowned slightly. The phrasing was odd. It felt like there was more—something Colten wasn’t saying. But instinctively, he nodded.
That's if he knew where Letzier was?


**Flora**
Flora decided to head to bed, her eyes heavy with exhaustion. Amika had already handed Alfred the medicine, and the house had settled into a quiet lull. She was tired—bone-deep tired—so she slipped away to her room and curled beneath the covers.
But just as sleep began to pull her under, an image flickered in her mind.
**Zara.**
Clear as day. Her face, her voice. The ache in Flora’s chest returned like a wave crashing against the shore.
Then—words. Whispered, distant, but unmistakable.
Flora’s eyes snapped open.
She sat up, heart pounding. Sleep was no longer an option.
Maybe she just needed water. Something to ground her.
Flora swung her legs over the side of the bed and stood, the silence of the house pressing in around her like a blanket too heavy to shake off.
She padded downstairs, grabbed a cup from the cabinet, and filled it slowly. Through the window, she spotted Alfred outside. He still had the bandage on, sitting quietly beneath the porch light.
A small smile tugged at her lips.
She stepped outside, the night air cool against her skin.
“Aren’t you supposed to be in bed?” she asked softly.
Alfred nodded, just barely. “I’m just… thinking.”
Flora nodded back. “Yeah. Me too.”
Alfred glanced up at her. “About what?”
She didn’t answer. Didn’t want to. Some things weren’t meant to be shared with everyone—just God, and maybe her family.
Alfred caught the silence, gave her a look, then nodded. “Alright.”
There was a pause. Then Flora turned to him, her voice soft. “What about you? What are you thinking about?”
He looked up as if pondering, “Complicated.”
They stood there silently, the night wrapping around them like a blanket. Above, the stars shimmered—distant, quiet witnesses.
Flora tilted her head back, eyes tracing constellations. She wondered what it would feel like… when she finally graduated. Would she soar across the sky, free and untethered?
As if Alfred wasn’t beside her, as if the world paused just for her dreams. Her thoughts drifted.
Are you here, God? she whispered inwardly. Are you really? Or is it…
She didn’t want to question Him. But was it wrong if she did? She didn’t think so. She was human. He was God.
And somewhere in that vast difference, she hoped He understood.
And yet, the unforgotten whisper lingered—a voice in the silence. She didn’t dare speak aloud.
The words drifted around her like wind through the trees, soft but undeniable:
You are mine. And I will show you things you never dreamed you’d see…
You will hear what you never imagined you could hear.
You are seen.
Suddenly, Alfred spoke. “The silence feels different.”
Flora nodded, a half smile. And they just stood there.
Until they were tired.


**Letzier**
Letzier sat beside Daisy, her eyes gleaming like gemstones—she sparkled with a quiet brilliance, like the stars themselves. Daisy caught his gaze and gave a half-smile. “You’re staring at me again.” He chuckled.
“I didn’t know that was a bad thing.” She let out a soft laugh, the kind that lingered in the air like music.


“How long do you think Nova will keep me here?” Daisy asked, her voice low. Letzier’s thoughts drifted to the file—still in Nova’s possession. “As long as it takes,” he muttered.


“What do you mean?” He sighed. “I’m worried. The BNA… they killed Zara outright. Or at least tried to.” Daisy nodded, her expression tightening. “We need to find her.”
He looked at her. “We?” He never thought of Daisy joining him to help find Zara. Daisy met his gaze. “She’s up there.”


Letzier shook his head. “Too dangerous, Daisy. I don’t want you getting hurt.” She huffed.


“She’s my friend, Letzier.” “And you’re my girlfriend,” he asserted with conviction. “So no.” Daisy frowned. “Letzier, please. I can help. I went to space school—I know the basics.” Letzier’s mind spun. Now that he knew Zara was alive, the question burned: how to find her?


His thoughts raced.
He could steal a ship. Risky. Illegal. But what other choice did they have? The BNA sought something—not from him, but from every influential person surrounding him.
He looked at Daisy. Her eyes met his, soft but pleading. That look. It broke something in him. And then the anger surfaced.
The image of what the file had said. The fury that they’d tried to kill her. “For your sake, Daisy,” he said, voice tight.
“Stay here. For me.” She stared for a moment, one, two, but she nodded. “Alright,” she said. Letzier eased with those words, realizing that he was tense. He exhaled.
Nova emerged, the same expression on her face that he had after reading the files. Instantly alerted to the situation, they both got up, Daisy's hand in his.
“I’m afraid to send you back, after reading this, but honestly, I have no choice. I need someone in,” Nova said.


Letzier nodded. Daisy looked at him; he felt her strong gaze. “Nova, explain, why are you afraid to send him back? Is he in danger?" Daisy stammered, her voice evident with worry. Nova let out a breath. “Alright, I’ll explain, but in my hub.” Daisy groaned as she removed Letzier’s hand from his own. She was probably irritated; most likely, it was because Nova interrupted their moment. He felt his heart ache with longing as she strode away.


He loved her, and he couldn’t let anything happen to her, even if it cost his life. Nova looked at Letzier. “I need you to get going… And…" Nova gave a long pause, then she said, “Be careful, Letzier… for Daisy’s sake.”
Letzier nodded.
“I wouldn’t disappoint her for the world,”


Nova smiled. “I know," he said, and he meant that. She had dealt with enough by losing Zara. If she lost him—no. He would do everything in his power to live, but if it came down to Daisy or himself? He knew what he would choose.
**Nathan**
Nathan sat near the window and watched, emotions looming over his mind. The looks everyone had were overwhelming him. No one seemed normal or looked normal. They hadn't seen Letzier in days, and Alfred had hurt himself the other night. Everything seemed strange to him. Flora was quieter, Dan… hadn't seemed himself.
“What was going on?” he murmured.
The days in school were quiet. Without Letzier, it felt… strange. Someone tapped on his shoulder; Nathan looked up to see Colten. “You okay, Nathan?” Colten said, worry evident in his voice.
Nathan gave a quick nod, “I'm alright..”
Colten shook his head.
“I know what it is, everyone seems off to you?” Nathann looked up, “they'd do, and it's bothering me, maybe a bit too much.”
Colten tilted his head slightly, “Indeed, they'd do. It might not make sense now, Nathan, but it will soon.”
Nathan felt confused. What does he mean? Just when he was about to ask, Colten spoke.
“How about you go and work on your studies?”
Nathan didn't respond; all that did was make his confusion worse.


Chapter
**Letzier**
He's training back at space school, training for the military, and across multiple countries, there's still war. His mind raced as he was doing sit up Andrue, his trainer, was yelling to move. He was moving all right. he looked over as he saw his mother. His face went pale. He is so grounded; he's eighteen, he can run away. He was glad that training only happened once a week; they wouldn't think anything bad if he skipped one. But not seeing his mom anymore, not calling her, not saying he was alright, he shivered in his boots; he was so dead. Andrue caught his expression and nodded. "Ten-minute break, everyone!"
Letzier nodded to Andruw and smirked. He walked towards his mom. And immediately, he spoke.
"Mom, I can explain—" The words died in his throat as she pulled him into a fierce hug.
"Foolish boy, you nearly gave me a heart attack." She released him, then promptly slapped his arm. "Don't ever scare me like that again."
Letzier stayed silent. He couldn't promise that—not with what Nova had revealed about the BNA, not with what he needed to do. His mother must have read something in his face because she changed the topic.
"Have you seen Alfred?"
Fear gripped him. In the chaos of the past week—Nova's revelations, the training, the search for WTB contacts—he'd nearly forgotten about his best friend. "No, is he okay?"
"He came by the house looking for you the other day. I just texted Alfred's grandma, Amy, that you're here. Alfred wants to see you."
Letzier's chest tightened. He'd left his friend in the dark between Nova's missions and space school training. He knows Alfred can help. Nova had said to find the WTB, and Alfred might know something, but that's if he knew something.
"Okay, Mama, I'll go." He pulled out his phone and called Zeb.
"Letzier! Where in the world have you been?!" Zeb's voice crackled with equal parts relief and frustration.
"Can I get a ride?"
"Of course you would be asking that—you have a lot of explaining to do"
Letzier didn't answer. Instead, he just acted as if nothing had happened. “I do?”
He heard Zeb sigh, “Where to?”
Letzier smiled.
"I'll tell you when you get here." Letzier needed to think. Nova had warned him to be careful who he trusted, but Alfred... Alfred, he could trust. When Zeb's hover vehicle pulled up, Letzier climbed in, his mind racing with possibilities.
"Okay, now can you tell me where we're going?"
"Alfred's house." And hopefully, some answers about the WTB.


**Alfred**
Alfred's head throbbed as he helped his grandma clean. He couldn't sit still with so many questions rattling around his aching skull.
"Alfred, your friends are here," his beloved grandma called out, probably relieved to see him finally getting visitors instead of pacing holes in her carpet.
"Thank you, Grandma," he managed, trying to sound normal despite the marching band in his head.
Opening the door, he saw Letzier and Zeb stepping out of the hover van. The relief hit him so hard he almost forgot to be angry. Almost.
"You made it," he said, fighting the urge to both hug and strangle his best friend. But he made sure to give him the look. Letzier shrugged it off…As if it didn't matter right now.
Letzier walked up the cement stairs, all business. "We need to talk somewhere private."
But Alfred was too annoyed to hear…He didn't even ask if he was ok.
"Yeah, getting knocked out by mysterious women tends to create conversation topics." Alfred's dry tone made Zeb raise an eyebrow. So did Letzier, but his was with the realization that his head was wrapped. It was random, but Alfred was annoyed. He shook his head and sighed.
“Come inside, we’ll talk in my room.”
They headed up to his room, and Alfred's rehearsed speech went out the window. Instead, he blurted, "Colten asked me to tell you that they need to discuss the Bible with you."
Letzier's head snapped up, a smile spreading across his face that made Alfred want to throw something at him.
“Yeah, that doesn't make any sense. I don't know why Colten would tell me that, but, you know,” Alfred said, glaring. “It wasn't like you were gone for an entire week, not like you to do that, while you were off playing secret agent," Alfred continued, gesturing to his bandaged forehead, "I've been getting concussions. You know what prevents concussions? Texting your best friend. Just a thought." He tried to maintain his annoyed expression, but relief at seeing Letzier safe made it difficult. "Seriously, man. A text. Even an emoji would've worked. Just... don't disappear like that again."


“I see you got hurt,” he commented, clearly disregarding the earlier remarks.


“Yeah, I did—by a girl,” Alfred admitted without hesitation.


Letzier giggled. “Dude, you were hitting on a girl. No wonder she hit you hard,” he said, teasingly. Alfred’s face flushed red. “No, I wasn’t! But that's not the point. I need to tell you what has been happening on my side, and how I got hit by a girl…”
He told him what had happened the night before.
And Letzier's eyes widened,
"And you said the women mentioned me and Daisy?" Letzier asked, his tone suddenly sharp with interest.
Alfred nodded. "Yeah. I don't know who she is. Colten's being so mysterious about everything."
"That's comforting," Letzier said, folding his hands and leaning forward. "For a moment I thought Nova was watching me, but now..."
Alfred's head snapped up. "Nova…The girl Zeb mentioned, at his place… The hacker girl who used to hang out with Zara?"
Letzier leaned in, urgency evident in his voice. “You won’t believe what I discovered,” he began, taking a deep breath as he launched into the astonishing tale of Zara’s survival. He detailed everything, including the involvement of Stone and Dan in the unfolding events, as we'll as the file he had found. Alfred's face looked pale as he mentioned Alfred and Flora being intelligent.
“…BNA is the one who made Zara's ship crash, not the Government, sorta….”


Letzier said, with a heaviness to his voice as if he was pondering it for the first time.
Alfred stepped back a few. “Wha-what?” Alfred felt so confused, he and Floar had like, “And the intelligent thing, the ability to read... others? Flora to be like ten steps ahead…And the school is a” Alfred felt a shiver go down his spine. “That's creepy.”
Letzier nodded.
“Yeah, my thought.”
Alfred smiled. “For you, it makes sense, you're always so strong for some reason, but me? Flora? That's kinda random.”


“Ima a kill Dan and Stone,” Zeb suddenly said, with a sound that Alfred never thought could come out of Zeb's mouth. Zeb has always been forgiving, even when it was hard, advising them to love Stone. Alfred and Letzier both looked at him in Shock.
“That's the first.” They both said.
“You're always the religious type,” Alfred said.
Zeb looked up at Letzier. Ignoring Alfred's comment. “What do we need to do?” Zeb said.
“we'll, let me tell you,” Letzier said. As he talked about Nova.
With a furrowed brow, he recounted his desperate search for Nova. “And we'll, I found her, pointing a gun at my date with Daisy,” he said, annoyed.
“But She'did it with a good purpose,” Letzier said. Alfred chuckled,


“Yeah, I bet if she weren't Nova, you probably would kill her with one swift move,” Alfred said, chuckling. Sending a positive mood. “Yeah,” Letzier chuckled with Alfred, then continued about the WTB and why Colten told Alfred to tell him, and just like she said. And finally, many of the questions overwhelming his mind were being answered.


“So that's why,” Alfred said, but the emotion and all the information weighed heavily. Zeb stepped forward,
“So Colten is involved big time. But in a good way,” Zeb said. They both looked at Zeb. “we'll, it looks like that,” Letzier said.


“If he’s the one who made the agency WTB, then we need him and his team,” Letzier stated. Boldness. Letzier continued.
“Cuse what I'm planning, it requires everything we got.”
Zeb looked at him with curiosity. "What are you planning?" The question hung in the air, heavy with suspicion.
Letzier glanced between Zeb and Alfred, then dropped the bomb: "We're going to steal a spaceship to find Zara." He paused, almost sheepish. "It was my idea, since Nova wouldn't agree."
The silence that followed was deafening. Alfred's bandaged head suddenly didn't hurt so much—probably because his brain had short-circuited trying to process his best friend's casual announcement about grand theft spacecraft.


**Nathan**
Nathan decided to take a stroll, letting the morning air invigorate his senses. He felt like he could think again—at least a little—but he preferred to simply enjoy the day without overthinking. As he walked, he watched the sun reflect off the lake beside their house, the trees behind him, and the bushes surrounding their neighborhood. The road ran alongside him, and just a short distance ahead was the park where Flora and Zara used to walk.
**Zara.**
A reminder of his loss. His heart ached again at the memory of their promise. He remembered the loss of his parents, his younger sister Reanna, and now Zara.
“Lord, why is there so much loss?” he whispered.
No answer.
What did he expect? Lately, only silence. When was the last time he felt God's love? Heard his voice? He tried to remind himself of the times he’d seen God move in his life. One memory surfaced—the time his biological mom had spoken to him.
“What is a Christian?” he’d asked.
Her motherly eyes had looked at him, serious and steady.
“A Christian is a religion,” she said. “People call themselves Christians, worshiping their god, but not really knowing what true worship is.”
Nathan had pondered. “Then what is true worship?”
His mom smiled. “Spirit and in truth. We are lovers of Jesus—we keep him first, not other things, not tech, not stuff, or people. We love through the eyes of God. We are His bride. And that, my dear, is true worship.”
The memory felt real, maybe too real. He looked up. My god, this…is hard. He tried loving him, and all he got was pain. Pain from his past, pain of losing the people he cared most about, Nathan walked as if a tree appeared and he kicked it. Mad.
How can a God do that? Why would he do that? Suddenly, Flora appeared in front of him, causing him to take a step back.
“Flora, hi,” he said. She gave a slight smile. “Are you okay?” Nathan sighed. “Honestly, I’m not.” Flora nodded and replied, “Here,” as she wrapped her arms around him.
His sister, “Promise me something,” Nathan said.
Flora looked up. “Yeah?”
“Promise me that nothing will happen to you, and that—”
She interrupted him. “I cannot promise that; no one can promise that.”
He closed his eyes for a moment, “your right,”
She smiled, “Come, Colten sent me to get you, Alfred found Letzier, and they are coming over.”

**Flora**
Flora and Nathan both step inside, Colten staring out the window, Amika standing beside the door.
She looked at both of them and smiled.
“Good, you got him.”
Suddenly, the atmosphere changed when Flora'saw Colten look.
Amika gathered Nathan and Flora in the living room. Flora looked up, confused, while Nathan asked from behind them, "What's going on?"
Colten studied Flora, his expression unreadable, yet something about the way he held himself made her stomach tighten. He was holding back—something big.
The silence grew heavy as Nathan and Flora'settled onto the sofa. Colten's face carried a weight Flora had never seen before. Amika turned to Colten and nodded her head to him.
"We've held back long enough, Colten," Amika said gently. "They should know."
Colten gave a quick nod, then turned to Flora. His voice came quietly but firmly.
"Zara... she's alive."
The words hit Flora like a tidal wave. Everything around her seemed to shrink, the air growing thick with disbelief. Her breath hitched, red curls slipping from behind her ear as she stared, frozen in place.
No. That couldn't be right.
Her fingers clenched around the fabric of her sleeve, gripping tighter as the weight of those words sank in.

Letzier smiled. "One thing at a time. We'll go as soon as possible, but first," Letzier looked towards Flora and Nathan, then back at Colten.
Colten nodded; understanding flowed between them.
Flora couldn't move, couldn't think, couldn't understand. Who's Nova, and was Zara alive? How?? Alfred looked at her. "Flora, you ok? You look pale," he said. When Flora didn't say anything, he went to grab some water and handed it to her.
She reached for it. "How? This can't be possible, she was dead?" she said, opening the water bottle.
Letzier stepped forward, his jaw tight, his face drawn with something deeper than just concern.
"I heard Stone and Dan talking. They... sabotaged the spaceship, and the worst part is, they had help. Zara's lost somewhere on a planet we can't identify," he said, and even though his words were simple, they carried a heaviness that settled into the room like lead.
Nathan let out a shaky breath. "... Dan, my friend." His voice was hoarse, barely above a whisper. Flora, for a moment, forgot he was in the room. He blinked once, twice—then something in him shut down. His face paled, and the energy drained from his body as realization took hold.
Colten shifted slightly, eyes flickering toward Nathan, like he knew exactly what was running through his mind. Like he was keeping something else. Was there something more he was hiding? Amika, seated beside Flora, gave Colten a sharp look. A knowing look. That silent language between them, the unspoken understanding.
Colten exhaled deeply, shoulders sinking under the weight of the truth. "Yeah..." His voice was barely audible.
Flora felt her throat tighten. She could barely process anything beyond the pounding in her chest. Hope. Fear. Was it possible to feel both at the same time?
Colten stepped closer. "We need you both to help find her," he said, steady despite the turmoil swirling in the air. "Nathan. Flora. We need you. We're going to do something different—we're visiting a friend who can give us a download."
Letzier and Alfred shifted where they stood, and Flora noticed how ready they looked. They stood firm, side by side, the tension rolling off them like soldiers before battle.
For a moment, they almost looked like brothers—though Alfred's skin was darker, there was an undeniable presence between them. A silent understanding. A readiness.
Colten took a measured breath. "Get your things. We leave now." Flora'swallowed past the knot in her throat and gave a small nod. "Okay," Flora'said, though she couldn't believe him.
"I-I can't."
Nathan's voice cracked, raw and broken.
"I'm staying." Silence stretched, thick and suffocating. Colten studied him carefully, eyes flickering with something like knowing. After a beat, he simply nodded. "Okay, Nathan. That's your decision," he stated. Colten looked at her. "Flora, your sister is alive, but your face says you don't believe me," Colten said, sighing. Alfred gazed at Flora, watching.
Then Flora took a deep breath, releasing all the anxiety and shakiness, letting it all go. Something else replaced it—determination? Peace? She wasn't sure, but she looked up at him with newfound clarity. "What do you want me to do?" she said.
Alfred smiled, and he spoke, "we'll, from what Letzier has told me, we need to convince Nova to steal a spaceship." Flora nodded. "You all do that. I'm going to pack up everything."


**Letzier**

Letzier's
