Let them think he was just another friend feeling deceived. They didn't need to know the real betrayal came from above—from the government, from Dan, and from Stone, that snake.
He stepped outside. "Let's go," he said to Nathan. Nathan nodded, understanding the weight of the situation without words.
After calling Zeb for pickup, they climbed the stairs, Alfred's head low with the burden of knowledge. When Flora opened the door, her eyes widened, and the defeat in her expression shocked everyone into silence.
But this wasn't like a death. No—Letzier was out there, fighting to survive. And that's what made it so shocking. Letzier was their best fighter, undefeated, unstoppable. How could he have been captured unless they somehow outsmarted him? He wasn't sure; he just hoped.
**Nathan**
Nathan sat on his bed replaying the moments in his mind. Dan's betrayal, Zara was alive…Reanna. A mixture of Hope and Betrayal repeated.
Zara's warm face loomed in his mind as his friend's words haunted him, “Dan, why?” Now, Letzier was captured. He didn't make it in time.
He gritted his teeth, turning his hands to fists, as he punched the wall so hard that it cracked, his fist driving straight through the drywall. “I can’t believe this,” he growled. He looked at his hands; his hands were bleeding; he didn't care that it was; he was hurt. Colten didn't trust Nathan enough to tell him that his sister was alive, that they were agents, and didn't bother to tell him that Dan would ruin his life.
Slammed his hand against the table, then dropped to his knees, his gaze locked on the floor. His shoulders trembled.
He was done pretending. Done holding it in. Done acting like everything was okay.
“’Cause it wasn’t anymore,” he breathed. “I’m not okay.”
Tears streamed down his face. It was never okay. He had tried—tried reaching for God, tried holding on—and this is where it got him.
Just then, the door creaked open. Flora stepped in, her eyes mirroring his pain.
She didn’t say much. She didn’t have to.
She knelt beside him, and they wrapped their arms around each other. And together, they sobbed.
Chapter
**Flora**
Flora looked at Alfred, who leaned against the wall with his head down. Her heart shattered at the sight. She hoped he didn't blame himself.
Her instincts kicked in.
She approached him. “Alfred, it's not your fault.” But as the words came out, another thought formed in her mind: It’s not his fault; it would be hers…
He shook his head. “I never did blame myself… but…” He held out a phone, handing it to Flora, and she instinctively grabbed it. She looked at the message and felt confused; nothing seemed wrong with it, and her mind whirled. Then it struck her.
“Daisy went to her house because her ex-boyfriend was there,” Alfred had said, voicing her thoughts out loud. Flora felt her legs give way. “It was a trap,” she murmured as emotions swirled around her.
Alfred affirmed, “Flora, it’s more than your sister. Letzier found two files—one that revealed a plan to exterminate people, one of those people being Daisy.”
Flora staggered back. “Why would they want to kill Daisy?” Alfred shrugged.
Flora exclaimed, “And the second one... what was that one about?”
Alfred took a breath and said, “The second one is... about superhuman intelligence. It includes Letzier, you, and me—and some other people.”
Alfred told her what the file had said, what Letzier had told him, and what abilities they might have. Alfred paused. “I wasn't going to tell you, but for your safety, it's best if I do.”
Confusion overwhelmed Flora's mind. One thought struck her the hardest: she realized she had made a mistake. She should have thought ahead. They wouldn’t have lost Letzier if she had.
“Flora, it’s not your fault. You didn’t have enough information to think ahead.”
Flora looked up in surprise, but nodded.
Alfred then gave out a loud sigh.
“I think I need time to process,” Flora said.
Alfred gave a slight nod. “You do that.”


**Nathan**
He decided to take another walk—not just for the fresh air, but because he wanted to find his sister. It was time. He returned to the spot where he had last seen her. As he waited, she approached with her arms folded and her head down.
Nathan spoke. “So, you’re another one of Colten’s agents.” Reanna nodded. “Yeah. Come—let’s talk somewhere private.” Her voice wasn’t how he remembered it from when they were children.
They walked together until they reached a quiet park. No people. Just them. She looked around, and when she spoke, it was soft. “I’m with the WTB. A double agent. I work undercover under the BNA.”
Nathan felt speechless. “And Colten decided to lie to me, saying you were kidnapped?” Reanna sighed, a wave of emotion sweeping across her face. “Yes. It’s complicated.”
Nathan gave a slight nod, his mind whirling with questions. “I see.”
Reanna gazed at him. She took her hood off—black hair, blue eyes. She had definitely grown.
“You’ve grown,” Nathan said.
She smiled. “Same to you.” But then her smile faded.
“I’ll be staying and helping the… BNA longer.” Reanna was gazing past him now, her eyes narrowed.
Nathan’s stomach tightened. He whispered; he could barely hear himself. “They’re behind me, aren’t they?”
She gave a slight nod. “Enough talk. You should go,” Reanna urged him in the same hushed tone.
Nathan nodded, then spoke aloud. “It’s nice to meet you, Reanna. I hope we’ll see each other again.”
Nathan knew this would be the last time he saw his sister. He glanced back. It wasn’t much of a conversation—but at least he knew she was alive.


**Letzier**
Letzier woke up chained against a wall, his head swimming in fog. No door in sight—just walls. No windows. His head pounded with each heartbeat. Daisy. The memory of her hurt stabbed through him. He tried to stand but looked down to find his feet chained as we'll. As consciousness fully returned, fury exploded through him.
"Hey!! Where is she? Tell me where she is or you're all dead!" he barked, rage burning through his veins. Their answering laughter only stoked his anger higher.
"She's safe, we'll taken care of," Coach Andrew's voice echoed through hidden speakers. The familiar voice made Letzier's stomach turn.
Suddenly, a door materialized in the wall, sliding open to reveal a vast white room. The chains released, and Letzier stumbled forward, his muscles tense.
"What is this?" Letzier demanded, scanning the space.
"You showed us something fascinating yesterday." Andrew's voice held that same pleased tone from training, but now it sent chills down Letzier's spine. "That robot you destroyed? One punch. Just one punch, and it went straight through."
The memory flashed in Letzier's mind: the training room, the robot attacking, his fist tearing through metal like paper. His shock at his strength.
"I've been watching you grow stronger," Andrew continued. "But today... Today proved what I've suspected all along. You're special, Letzier. And now?"
Multiple doors opened along the walls, revealing robots similar to the one he'd destroyed. "Now we're going to see exactly how special."
Letzier's heart raced as understanding dawned. They had been testing him all along—every training session, every match. Coach Andrew hadn't been preparing him for Space Military—he had been studying him.
"Fight them," Andrew commanded. "Or Daisy suffers the consequences."
As they stepped forward, the robots' eyes glowed red, and Letzier clenched his fists. He had played right into their hands, and now Daisy was paying the price.
"Fine, I’ll play your game," he said.
Robots started coming at him. He fought, and he wondered how long this would last before they tired him out.


**Nathan**
His eyes gazed out the window as Colten drove the hover bus. It was crazy—they were doing this. Colten had decided to take Elora, who had passed with all A's. She was the only student on the bus to do so, and that was why she was coming. Still, Nathan told himself, they would make sure nothing happened to her. Colten had promised to take her home if anything went wrong. He said he'd use the latest tech: teleportation. Nathan thought that sounded crazy—but then again, AI in general was crazy.
Colten stopped the hover bus, and suddenly a cold surge of fear gripped Nathan’s chest. The building loomed ahead—massive and imposing, it's cylindrical structure rising into storm-thick clouds. The walls didn’t reflect light—they seemed to absorb it, casting an eerie, unnatural shade over the scene.
This wasn’t the gleaming space center he had imagined. It looked more like a fortress—shadowed, soulless, like something meant to keep people in, not welcome them.
Flora stood quietly beside him. Her expression mirrored his fear.
“Are y’all excited?” Colten asked, his voice far too cheerful for the setting.
“Of course,” Alfred replied, too quickly.
“Once in a lifetime,” Alfred said, though he sounded a bit sarcastic as they stepped out with a breezy smile, playing it cool for Elora’s sake. Nathan knew better. Alfred was walking into a building twice his size to steal a ship and possibly trigger chaos across galaxies.
As the girls passed, Alfred gave Nathan a subtle nod. Nathan nodded back. And then, silently, he prayed as they got off the bus. They were doing this, he told himself, and gulped.
**Flora**
At the entrance, guards emerged from the shadows. “What are you doing here? No civilian tours until next year,” one of them snapped.
Colten didn’t flinch. He calmly handed over a folded paper from his jacket. The guard scanned it, frowning. Flora’s heart pounded. She whispered silent prayers—for herself, for her friends. That God would be with them through all of it. “You can enter,” the guard finally said, though his tone had shifted.
His eyes landed on Flora—and stayed there. A chill crept up her spine. Helmeted, he whispered something to another guard. Just as she stepped forward, he reached out and grabbed her arm. Alfred stiffened, ready to defend her, but Colten gave a small shake of his head.
“She’s fine,” the guard said to the others. “I just need to ask her a few questions.” Flora’s heart thudded, but somehow… she believed him. She let herself be led away until he pulled off his helmet. “Zerak?” Her breath caught. He looked away.
“What I told you before—it was true. I was a student. I did have a sister. She was popular.” His words were strained, heavy with half-truths. He glanced at the cameras, then back at her. “But you shouldn’t be here.”
Flora frowned. “What do you mean?” He leaned in, voice hushed. “The government—it’s not what you think. There are layers upon layers. Secrets within secrets. They’re watching, Flora. And they’re planning things you don’t want to be part of.”
Her stomach dropped. She already knew that, but he didn’t. There was a strange familiarity between them. A connection. She steadied her breath.
“Zerak, you're bold to do something like this, warning a girl you just met…” She pondered a moment, remembering what Alfred had said to her a few days before about Intelgents. “If they take me…” She smiled faintly. “I have God with me.”
Zerak scoffed, frustrated. “You’re kidding, right? Flora—He’s not real. This isn’t about faith. It’s about survival.” She didn’t flinch; she waited. Zerak gave a loud sigh.
“There’s a reason they’re letting students tour. They’re not just observing anymore. They’re testing.” He met her eyes. “When they look at you, they see something they want. And once they want something…” He didn’t finish. Flora’s response was soft but steady. “It’s okay,” she said.
“I need to get back,” Flora said. Zerak nodded hesitantly. “Alright.”
She stepped back in line with the group. Alfred gave her a questioning look. She shook her head—not now. The facility’s interior was cold metal and white light. But to Flora’s enhanced vision, it was far more: invisible grids lined the corridors, data streams pulsed through walls, and codes were woven into the air.
Then, a woman in a lab coat emerged. Flora stepped back on instinct. Something in the woman’s eye screamed: trap. The woman’s eyes collided with Flora. Her instincts were tuned.
Alfred moved before she could react, positioning himself between Flora and the woman. Alfred saw it. What surprised Flora was that as soon as she saw Alfred, her eyes winced.
Nathan took Flora’s hand, and he noticed the way Flora felt uncomfortable. Everyone noticed how the woman screamed Bad.
In the corner of her eye, four shadows loomed—Nova, Zeb, Sileth, and Amika.
“I’m Dr. Chen,” the woman said coolly, “and I’ll be your guide on today’s... special tour.” No one spoke. No one breathed. Flora’s pulse quickened. This is happening. Outer space. The mission. Everything. She let out a shaky breath and chuckled to herself.
“Something funny?” Dr. Chen asked. Flora shook her head. She stepped a little closer to Alfred, remembering his promise. Elora smiled—blissfully unaware of what was about to happen.


Chapter
**Zeb**
He could barely contain the hope slamming against his ribs. Zara’s alive. After everything—after the silence, the doubt, the months of clawing through scraps of intel—she’s alive. The thought burned through him like fire in his veins.
Beside him, Nova worked in tense silence. The pale blue glow from her tablet flickered across her face, casting her expression in cold light. Lines of code flew by, her fingers a blur. Sileth stood watch behind them, still as a blade before a strike. Everything had led to this. “All right,” Nova muttered. “Almost there...”
Click. The ship’s access panel hissed open. Zeb exhaled. They were in.
He slipped through the hatch, every nerve on alert. Shadows hugged the hallway. His eyes swept for movement. Amika ghosted in behind him, silent, her hand hovering near her sidearm. Every line of her posture screamed readiness. Step by step. Just a little further. Then—
The alarm. A mechanical shriek tore through the silence, followed by a woman's scream—short, sharp, and real.
Red lights exploded overhead, pulsing like an exposed heart. The corridor became a strobe-lit battlefield. Zeb’s stomach flipped.
Nova’s voice rang in his head like a commandment etched in steel: “If we’re compromised—Plan B. No hesitation. Get in and fight.”
No cover. No shadows. No backup. Just three of them and a hundred ways this could fall apart.
Zeb spun toward the hatch, jaw clenched. The sound of boots—too many boots—echoed down the corridor. So much for slipping out quietly. This wasn’t a mission anymore. It was survival. And it was going to cost blood to get to Zara.


**Alfred**
The sirens hit like a blade. Alfred’s heart slammed against his ribs. Nathan and Colten were moving, shouting, reacting—but all he saw was Flora. Her hand, small and tense in his, tethered him to reality. He gripped it tighter, like holding on could shield her.
He had promised Zara. Before she left—before her ship vanished into silence—she’d pulled him aside, eyes fierce with love and worry. "Take care of her, Alfred. No matter what." He had said yes. Sworn it. And now, Flora was slipping away.
Guards swarmed the corridor like shadows made solid. Shouts ricocheted off the walls. Weapons raised. Chaos bloomed. He saw Amika move through it like lightning—pivot, parry, disarm—each motion precise, devastating. Colten pulled the emergency coin from his coat. One press—and Elora vanished in a flash of gold.
Suddenly, a scream. His mind ran cold. Flora… Her hand was torn from his. Alfred spun, heart crashing into his ribs. She was being dragged across the floor—boots scraping, eyes wide, voice raw with panic.
"Lord..." The word tore from him, unfiltered and desperate. "Please. Please get us all on that ship. I can’t lose her. Not after everything. Not after Zara." The words were random; he hadn't prayed in a long time. What else was he supposed to do?
He lunged—too slow. Someone else was faster. Another guard collided with her captor, slamming him into the wall with brutal force. A helmet clattered to the ground and spun in slow circles, revealing the face beneath. Alfred froze. That face. The Observation Dome. That day. That silent warning. He had seen him before.
His breath caught, but not in relief. Fury surged in his chest—why now? Why here? He rushed forward and pulled Flora back without a word, the weight of his promise to Zara pressing hard on his shoulders.
Then—a low hum. Soft. Steady. Alive. The ship powered on. Lights flickered. Systems stirred awake. Hope crackled back to life. Alfred exhaled, just once. A smile broke through the panic—thin, shaken... but real. They had a chance.


**Letzier**
The alarms pierced through the stark white room, interrupting his latest "test." The robots froze mid-attack, their red eyes dimming as new protocols took priority. Letzier's muscles ached, but he stayed alert, listening.
"What's happening?" Coach Andrew's voice had lost it's usual smugness, replaced by sharp tension. Through the hidden speakers, Letzier caught fragments of urgent reports: "...breach in hangar three..." "... TWB agents..." "...they're stealing the ship!"
A faint smile crossed his exhausted face. He knew exactly what this was—another move in this endless game between organizations. Not a rescue mission for him, no, it was a rescue mission for Zara. He wasn't naive. Heck, he was the one who planned it. This was about something bigger. The BNA had plans, and clearly, they weren't the only ones making moves.
The robots reactivated, their eyes glowing red once more. Whatever was happening up there didn't change his situation down here. As he raised his fists to continue fighting, one thought kept him going: at least his team was causing trouble for the BNA, even if they didn't know he was here. Even if they couldn't help him or Daisy.
One move at a time. That's all he could manage now. This was getting to him—had it been a week? Days? Time blurred in this white room. His fists connected with metal again and again, but with each robot he destroyed, another emerged stronger than the last. They were learning, he realized grimly. Copying his moves.
Punch. Dodge. Destroy. Repeat. The pattern was maddening. Each new robot adapted to his technique, forcing him to fight harder, think faster. It was beyond irritating—it was exhausting. Just when he thought he couldn't take another round...
They stopped. The alarm that had been blaring finally fell silent.
"I need a break," Andrew's voice crackled through the speaker. "If you're wondering, it's dark out."
Letzier's legs trembled with fatigue as he breathed a sigh of relief. But his moment of rest was short-lived. Cold metal suddenly gripped his ankles—the chains. The floor beneath him began to move, sliding him back toward his holding cell. At this point, he was too tired to resist. He barely registered the wall sealing shut behind him as he slumped against it, letting exhaustion drag him into sleep.


**Flora**
Zerak had saved her—just in time. His movements were sharp, practiced. Before she could even process what had happened, Alfred was pulling her to safety. Then Zerak followed.


He caught up fast, stepping into their path. “Whatever you’re doing,” he said, urgent but level, “let me come with you.” The words landed with weight. Heavy. Unavoidable. Alfred turned, ready to shut it down with a single look—but Flora stepped in. “Yes,” she said quickly, already pulling Zerak’s sleeve. “Come. Hurry.” Alfred didn’t argue. He just grunted and kept moving. There was no time for questions anymore. Only trust and forward.
The sharp click of weapons sounded around them as guards raised their guns. But Sileth was faster—his MP11 already in hand. He fired with unnerving calmness, his movements fluid and exact. With a subtle gesture, he motioned for them to hurry. Zerak didn’t hesitate, drawing his weapon with the same calm urgency. Flora could feel it in her gut—bringing him along would complicate things. She could already picture the suspicion on the others’ faces. But something about Zerak’s resolve—his willingness to risk everything in that moment—told her this was right. Right now, there was no turning back.
She bolted for the ship as Colten drew his pistol in one smooth motion. Then a scream split the air—not terror. Pain. Nathan. Her heart stopped. “No, no—” The words slipped out as she spun around.
Everything was chaos. Shouts, gunfire, alarm klaxons. But through her enhanced vision, she saw him—blood pooling around his leg. Without thinking, she ran back, her gift allowing her to track each missile’s trajectory. She weaved through the barrage, watching bullet paths before they struck. Ahead of her, Colten and Sileth provided cover fire, dropping guards with precise shots. Amika moved like a dancer, every motion a lethal calculation.
Zerak was already at Nathan’s side, tearing a strip of cloth with practiced hands. He wrapped the makeshift bandage swiftly and efficiently. “Let’s move,” he said. Together, they lifted Nathan, each taking a side. The sprint to the ship felt like a lifetime.
Alfred was already at the entrance. He grabbed Nathan’s arm, pulling him in as Zerak followed. Flora’s heart pounded as they crossed the threshold. Relief. Fear. Gratitude.
She dropped into a seat, glancing at the ship’s supplies—enough food and water to last for years. A small comfort in the storm. Colten, Sileth, and Amika boarded last, their movements quick and deliberate. “Are we ready?” Zeb’s voice called from the cockpit. Nova was already stationed near the systems—there wasn’t much she could do now except wait. Amika knelt beside Nathan, tending to his wound with calm precision. “We’re all accounted for,” Flora said, breathless. Zeb’s smile was steady. Determined. “Then let’s find Zara.”
**Letzier**
A knock pulled him from sleep. His eyes cracked open to find Andrew's face peering at him—how had he gotten in here? The coach held out a water bottle, and before Letzier could voice his suspicion, Andrew took a long drink.
"No, it's not poisoned. See?" He offered the bottle again. Letzier grabbed it, his thirst overriding his caution. For a moment, embarrassment washed over him—here he was, supposedly the strongest fighter, captured and accepting water from his captor. The awkwardness of it all hit him, but he pushed the feeling aside. His own fate wasn't what mattered most.
"How is Daisy?" The question came out between gulps of water, his heart pounding with fear of the answer. Andrew's expression shifted, almost amused. "Why is she the one on your mind right now?" He shook his head. "But to answer your question—she's alive, and no one has hurt her." The words hit him like a physical force. Letzier's shoulders sagged as waves of relief crashed through him, nearly overwhelming in their intensity.


His eyes burned with unexpected tears that he quickly blinked away. Daisy was safe. She wasn't being tortured. She wasn't hurt. The knot of fear that had been twisting in his gut since his capture finally loosened, if only slightly. He nodded, not trusting his voice, afraid it might break with the emotion threatening to spill over. At least she was safe. That one thought echoed in his mind, giving him strength. That was all that mattered.
Andrew came nearer. “We saw your friend—Alfred, was it? Where did they go?” Letzier shook his head. He did know, but he wouldn't tell him. Even if it meant his life. Andrew growled, “Did I stutter?” “Even if I knew, why would I tell you?” Letzier said, shrugging it off. Andrew sneered. “They took my spaceship. Why? Why would the WTB take my spaceship for no reason? You were with them, right? That girl—Nova, was it?”
He wanted to punch Andrew so badly. Play dumb, Letzier. Play dumb. “Who is the WTB?” But Letzier's gaze caught Stone. “Stone?”
Andrew looked annoyed by his appearance. Letzier, in that moment, recognized the teleportation device—he had seen Stone use it. “Son, what are you doing here?” Andrew yelled. And in that moment, Letzier realized. And all he could think was one thing: how stupid he had been. Dan, Stone, Andrew… They were a family. In that moment, Letzier wanted to stab them in the back—just like they had done to him. Let’s see how it felt.
“Dad, we had them—if it weren’t for your stubbornness to not attack our cousin…” Andrew glared at him and shook his head. Stone sighed. “The Commander wants to see you. He said it’s not worth entrapping our prisoner.”
Letzier gave Andrew a questioning look. Cousin… what does he mean by cousin? Andrew gestured sharply toward the door, his posture laced with disapproval. Letzier didn’t flinch. He barely noticed. His mind spun, sickened by the realization: He’d been trained under a family of traitors. All along.
Stone walked out. Andrew lingered.
“We’ll be after them—the WTB, Flora, all of them. And you’ll be joining us. We will find them.” Then he left, his words echoing off the walls like a sentence passed.
Letzier stood still, muscles rigid. His mind clawed for a plan—anything. But nothing came. Every option blurred into silence. This was the worst situation he'd ever been trapped in.
He dropped his gaze, voice barely a whisper. Suddenly, his mind thought—maybe… maybe God would help. It was worth a try. “God, if you're here, save me.” The words scratched through the room, soft but aching. His fists shook. He hadn’t just prayed. He pleaded.
And then—just like before… the chains dissolved. The door opened. Letzier didn’t flinch. He didn’t run. He refused to let the floor claim him like last time.
But pain still gripped him. The ache of betrayal. The sting of lost trust. Then the hiss of metal echoed through the corridor. The robots were activated. Letzier exhaled once, clenched his fists, and stepped forward. It was time to fight.
**Zara.**
The days blurred together in this endless purple twilight. Food supplies remained steady enough for a few more months if rationed carefully. The ship's emergency stores were at least intact after the crash, even if everything else was twisted beyond repair. "Thank you, Lord, for this provision," she whispered, a habit kept even here in the vastness of space.
Zara pressed her hand against the crystalline ground, feeling the slow, steady pulse beneath. At first, the living planet had terrified her - the way it breathed, the way it moved, how the very surface seemed alive beneath her feet. Now, after so long, it felt like evidence of God's incredible creativity. Who else could design an entire planet that lived and breathed like some cosmic flower?
The signal beacon blinked steadily from it's perch on the highest crystal formation. Every day, the same message: Here. Alive. Help. Her daily act of faith - believing that someone would hear it and come.
Her helmet's display flickered - the filtration system struggling again. The planet's "breath" was breathable, but something in it made her head fuzzy if inhaled too much directly. Like being drunk on air. The spores, maybe, or whatever those floating purple particles were.
"Flora would love this," she whispered, imagining her sister's face lit up with wonder at the bioluminescent crystals. "She'd probably have figured out why the whole planet's one giant plant by now." A smile crossed her face, thinking of Letzier, too. He wouldn't give up looking - that wasn't in his nature. His stubborn faith was one of the things she'd always admired about him.
A tremor ran through the ground - the planet taking another breath. She'd learned to time them now. Inhale: the crystals dim slightly, the air grows heavier. Exhale: everything glows brighter, fresh oxygen flooding the atmosphere. Like clockwork, every six hours. Even in isolation, God had given her this rhythm to hold onto.
The worn Bible in her hands - somehow still intact after the crash. Another miracle. The pages fell open to Psalm 139: "If I rise on the wings of the dawn, if I settle on the far side of the sea, even there your hand will guide me..." Her fingers traced the familiar words, finding comfort in their truth. Even here, on this strange breathing planet, she wasn't beyond His reach.
"They'll come," she prayed softly, watching the purple horizon. "Letzier won't stop until he finds me. Flora won't let them give up." The planet breathed beneath her, a reminder that even in the furthest reaches of space, life persisted. And where there was life, there was hope.
Her mind trailed off with Zeb, his kind features, how he loved the lord, and how he loved her. She missed him. Her heart squeezed. From her ship, she heard a beep noise. She rushed to it. Coming.. Me.. Zeb…On…our…way.
She looked up, and finally she cried. Her hand was over her mouth. His voice. She missed him so. She looked up and prayed Thanks.


Chapter
**Zeb**
He put the ship on autopilot, and they would be heading straight forward. He looked at everyone, and they were all on the ground sleeping. He smiled; he didn't blame them. He sat at the table and thought about the message. He heard her, her voice, that desperate cry for help. She was indeed out there. He started praying and thanking God over and over again, and then led him into worship and praise. For a while now, still seeking his face. And by the time he was finished, he felt satisfied.
Turning, he saw Zerak watching.
“You love her, don't you? Zara,” Zerak asked.
Zeb nodded. Zeb did not fully trust Zerak, but Zeb could still get to know Zerak better.
Zerak settled into the chair across from Zeb, his eyes distant. "I had someone once, too," he said quietly. "Before the BNA, before all of this…”
Zeb looked at him, “Who?”
Zerak looked down, “Her name was Claire."
"Your sister?" Zeb asked, remembering the name from earlier conversations.
Zerak nodded his head. "Yes, Claire. She was..." he paused, searching for words. "She was like Zara in some ways. Brilliant, fearless. Too smart for her good." His fingers traced invisible patterns on the table. "We were both in the early space program. Back when the BNA was just starting to show up, basically taking over the school."
"What happened?"
"They wanted her research. She'd discovered something about planetary atmospheres - something they could weaponize. She refused to hand it over." Zerak's voice grew heavy. "I found her lab destroyed one morning. They made it look like an accident."
"That's why you joined them," Zeb realized. "To find out what happened."
"And to stop it from happening to anyone else." Zerak looked at Flora's sleeping form. "When I saw what they were planning for Zara... I couldn't watch history repeat itself. That's why I helped Flora. Why I'm here."
Zeb studied him. Zeb didn't trust him, but at the same time, he felt like he could believe him. For now.
"Does anyone else know? The truth about what happened?"
"No. My family thinks I joined the BNA for the career opportunity. It's safer that way." Zerak's smile was bitter.
The ship hummed around them, it's steady rhythm filling the silence.
"We'll find her," Zerak said finally. "Zara. We'll get there in time."
Zeb nodded, understanding now why Zerak had chosen to help them. Some wounds never heal - they just become reasons to save others from the same pain.
But still, the uneasy feeling with Zerak was there. Despite his love for his sister, he saved Flora. Zeb still didn't trust him.
**Letzier**
They were getting stronger. He dodged each of their blows. They were getting quicker, smarter. This was not going so we'll, but that wouldn't stop him.
Through it all, he kept asking the man above for help. "Jesus, don't leave me behind in your plans," he whispered as he destroyed robot after robot. He'd killed a few using different move patterns, but soon those patterns would fail. He wanted to be in the real action, not whatever this was. And to keep Daisy safe. He prayed for the group, hoping they were out there finding Zara, and how badly he wanted to join them.
He remembered Andrew's threat about dragging him along. Was everyone up there now, lost in the endless cosmos? Nova wouldn't leave him behind - of that he was certain. But neither would she stop the mission, or at least she better not.
Suddenly, a blade flashed past his face - too close, too fast. Pain bloomed across his cheek as warm blood trickled down. He touched the wound, stunned. He hadn't bled like this since... since that day two years old. The robots should have stopped at the first sign of blood - that was always the protocol. But they kept coming, their red eyes gleaming with artificial intelligence.
Then, without warning, they froze. Letzier stood in the silence, blood dripping steadily onto the stark white floor. Something had changed. Andrew appeared from the corridor, not carrying water this time but flanked by guards - lots of guards.


Their black uniforms made the white room feel smaller, more suffocating. They swarmed around him as chains materialized again, the cold metal familiar against his skin, but the floor remained still.


Instead, the guards raised their weapons, the red targeting lights dancing across his chest like deadly fireflies.
Was this it? Not now. Not when his girl and the others needed him. The thought of leaving everyone behind scared him more than death itself - what would happen to Daisy? Who would protect her from these people? The faces of his friends flashed through his mind: Alfred's determined smile, Flora's fierce loyalty, Zeb's unwavering faith. The thought of never seeing them again, of leaving them to face whatever was coming alone... His heart pounded against his ribs, but he kept his expression neutral. He wouldn't give Andrew the satisfaction of seeing his fear.
But the guns didn't fire. Instead, Andrew spoke with unsettling calm, his voice echoing in the sterile room. Each word dripped with barely contained hatred.
"No, we won't kill you. That's one of the reasons we turned the robots off. We've gotten enough data, and now the robots are stronger thanks to you. But we have one problem - TWB has our ship now, and trust me, if I could kill you right now, I would." Andrew's eyes glittered with malice, a stark contrast to his controlled tone.
Letzier inhaled and exhaled just as his training taught him. The cut on his face stung, a reminder of how quickly things could change. What more could they want from him? They'd already gotten what they needed - his fighting patterns, his techniques, everything that made him unique as a fighter. The robots would now be nearly unbeatable.
Andrew circled him slowly, like a predator savoring the moment. "You see, Letzier, while you've been playing hero with our robots, your friends have caused quite a mess. Not just stealing our most advanced ship, but causing chaos in our systems." He stopped in front of Letzier, his smile cold. "And now they're searching for that girl - Zara, isn't it?"
The name sent a jolt through Letzier's chest, but he kept his face carefully blank. Don't react, don't give them anything.
"The funny thing is," Andrew continued, "we need that ship back. And you're going to help us get it." He gestured to Stone, who stepped forward with something in his hands - a sleek, black device Letzier had never seen before.
"You see, while you were fighting our robots, we weren't just collecting combat data." Andrew's voice took on an almost scholarly tone. "We were mapping your neural patterns, your decision-making process, your very instincts. And this..." he tapped the device in Stone's hands, "this will ensure you cooperate."
Letzier pulled against the chains, the metal biting into his wrists. "If you think I'll help you hurt them-"
"Oh, you won't have a choice." Andrew's smile widened. "And the best part? When we find them, they'll never see the betrayal coming. Not from their trusted friend."
The guards moved closer, their weapons never wavering. Through the fear and anger coursing through him, one thought burned bright in Letzier's mind: he had to warn them somehow. Had to find a way to let them know what was coming.
"And Daisy?" Letzier managed to keep his voice steady. "What happens to her?"
Andrew's laugh echoed off the white walls. "That depends entirely on how we'll you perform."
The device in Stone's hands hummed to life, emitting a soft blue glow that reminded Letzier of the stolen ship's engines. Dan appeared from behind, holding what looked like neural connectors - thin, spider-like wires that made Letzier's skin crawl.
"Father," Stone's voice carried an edge of uncertainty. "Are you sure this won't damage his combat abilities? We need him to be functional."
Andrew's face hardened. "The neural mapping is precise. We're not destroying his skills - we're... redirecting them." He turned to Letzier, his voice dropping to a whisper. "Think of it as a leash. You'll still be you, just... more compliant."
Letzier's mind raced. The robots, the constant battles - it hadn't just been about making them stronger. They'd been studying him, preparing for this moment. Every punch, every dodge, every strategy he'd used had given them data they needed.
"No, I won't let you win!" Letzier growled, straining against the chains. "They'll know something's wrong. Nova will-"
"Nova?" Andrew cut him off with a laugh. "The girl who left you here? Who chose to go searching for Zara instead of rescuing you?" He leaned closer. "Face it, Letzier. Your friends have bigger concerns than you right now."
Dan stepped forward with the neural connectors.
"Hold still," he commanded.
"This will hurt less if you don't resist."
But Letzier knew - this was his last chance. His last moment of true free will. He closed his eyes, sending up one final desperate prayer. "Jesus, rescue me, please," he whispered. Then his eyes snapped open, muscles tensing for whatever came next. As they came closer, he stepped back, but the chains stopped him from moving closer. He prayed over and over, surely God wouldn't let these men win. They merely forced the connector to touch his neck, cold and sharp. His training kicked in - every muscle tensed, ready to fight, but the chains held firm. The guards' weapons clicked in warning. The shock wave converged through him. But he stilled. Focusing on Daisy and friends, Alfred, Flora Face, when she smiled, when the mechon of his sister. He heard Andrew speak. A man he thought was his friend. “Turn it up! Break through him.”
But it didn't break his mind, now, to focus on the very one, the only one, Jesus.
“Lord, let them know, somehow let them know. Please”
Suddenly, just as the darkness started to claim him, a surge of power, peace, and protection flooded through him, and an image of a man smiling appeared. A voice telling him. Trust, trust, trust, trust my Love. The voice over baring his heart, flowing, and now he felt like no matter what happens, God was with him, and in that image, he saw an unthinkable thing, not a thing, a place. Heaven.
The device sparked violently, it's blue glow turning to angry red before dying completely.
"What's happening?" Andrew demanded, grabbing the smoking device from Stone's hands. "The neural patterns were perfect!"
Stone stared at his readings in disbelief. "It's like... like something's blocking us. The connection was there and then... it just wasn't."
Letzier sagged in his chains, exhausted but conscious. A small smile touched his lips - he knew exactly what, or rather who, had intervened. “You failed,” Letzier told him.
Andrew's face contorted with rage before smoothing into something more calculated. "Fine. We do this the hard way." He nodded to Dan. "Get the sedatives ready. We'll keep him subdued during transport if we can't control him."
"The ship leaves in an hour," Stone added, still eyeing Letzier with confusion.
"Perfect." Andrew grabbed Letzier's jaw, forcing eye contact. "You may have resisted our device, but you're still coming with us. And when we find your friends... I will make sure you watch them die!" He left the threat hanging. All Letzier could do was smile. “You think you will win, hah, you're fighting something bigger than me.”
Andrew stormed off like a child. Such a baby, Letzier thought.
As the guards approached with the sedative, Letzier felt a strange peace. They could drug him, chain him, take him into space - but they couldn't touch what protected him. His last thought before the sedative took hold was a prayer of thanks.


**Zeb**
He put the ship on autopilot, and they would be heading straight forward. He looked at everyone, and they were all on the ground sleeping. He smiled; he didn't blame them. He sat at the table and thought about the message. He heard her, her voice, that desperate cry for help. She was indeed out there. He started praying and thanking God over and over again. Then leading him into worship and praise. For a while now, still seeking his face. And by the time he was finished, he felt satisfied. Turning, he saw Zerak watching.
“You love her, don't you? Zara,” Zerak asked.
Zeb nodded.


Zerak settled into the chair across from Zeb, his eyes distant. "I had someone once, too," he said quietly. "Before the BNA, before all of this…”
Zeb looked at him, “Who was she?”
Zerak looked down, “Her name was Claire."
"Your sister?" Zeb asked, remembering the name from earlier conversations.
Zerak nodded his head. "Yes, Claire. She was..." he paused, searching for words. "She was like Zara in some ways. Brilliant, fearless. Too smart for her good." His fingers traced invisible patterns on the table. "We were both in the early space program. Back when the BNA was just starting to show up, basically taking over the school."
"What happened?"
"They wanted her research. She'd discovered something about planetary atmospheres - something they could weaponize. She refused to hand it over." Zerak's voice grew heavy. "I found her lab destroyed one morning. They made it look like an accident."
"That's why you joined them," Zeb realized. "To find out what happened."
"And to stop it from happening to anyone else." Zerak looked at Flora's sleeping form. "When I saw what they were planning for Zara... I couldn't watch history repeat itself. That's why I helped Flora. Why I'm here."
Zeb studied him. Zeb didn't trust him, but at the same time, he felt like he could believe him. For now.
"Does anyone else know? The truth about what happened?"
"No. My family thinks I joined the BNA for the career opportunity. It's safer that way." Zerak's smile was bitter.
The ship hummed around them, it's steady rhythm filling the silence.
"We'll find her," Zerak said finally. "Zara. We'll get there in time." Zeb nodded, understanding now why Zerak had chosen to help them. Some wounds never heal - they just become reasons to save others from the same pain. The ship was calm.
Chapter
**Letzier**
They were getting stronger. He dodged each of their blows. They were getting quicker, smarter. This was not going so we'll, but that wouldn't stop him.
Through it all, he kept asking the man above for help. "Jesus, don't leave me behind in your plans," he whispered as he destroyed robot after robot. He'd killed a few using different move patterns, but soon those patterns would fail. He wanted to be in the real action, not whatever this was. And to keep Daisy safe. He prayed for the group, hoping they were out there finding Zara, and how badly he wanted to join them.
He remembered Andrew's threat about dragging him along. Was everyone up there now, lost in the endless cosmos? Nova wouldn't leave him behind - of that he was certain. But neither would she stop the mission, or at least she better not.
Suddenly, a blade flashed past his face - too close, too fast. Pain bloomed across his cheek as warm blood trickled down. He touched the wound, stunned. He hadn't bled like this since... since that day two years old. The robots should have stopped at the first sign of blood - that was always the protocol. But they kept coming, their red eyes gleaming with artificial intelligence.
Then, without warning, they froze. Letzier stood in the silence, blood dripping steadily onto the stark white floor. Something had changed. Andrew appeared from the corridor, not carrying water this time but flanked by guards - lots of guards.

Instead, the guards raised their weapons, the red targeting lights dancing across his chest like deadly fireflies.

But we have one problem - TWB has our ship now, and trust me, if I could kill you right now, I would." Andrew's eyes glittered with malice, a stark contrast to his controlled tone.

Not just stealing our most advanced ship, but causing chaos in our systems." He stopped in front of Letzier, his smile cold. "And now they're searching for that girl - Zara, isn't it?"

"Oh, you won't have a choice." Andrew's smile widened. "And the best part? When we find them, they'll never see the betrayal coming. Not from their trusted friend."
The guards moved closer, their weapons never wavering. Through the fear and anger coursing through him, one thought burned bright in Letzier's mind: he had to warn them somehow. Had to find a way to let them know what was coming.
"And Daisy?" Letzier managed to keep his voice steady. "What happens to her?"
Andrew's laugh echoed off the white walls. "That depends entirely on how we'll you perform."

"Nova?" Andrew cut him off with a laugh. "The girl who left you here? Who chose to go searching for Zara instead of rescuing you?" He leaned closer. "Face it, Letzier. Your friends have bigger concerns than you right now."
Dan stepped forward with the neural connectors.
"Hold still," he commanded.
"This will hurt less if you don't resist."
But Letzier knew - this was his last chance. His last moment of true free will. He closed his eyes, sending up one final desperate prayer. "Jesus, rescue me, please," he whispered. Then his eyes snapped open, muscles tensing for whatever came next. As they came closer, he stepped back, but the chains stopped him from moving closer. He prayed over and over, surely God wouldn't let these men win. They merely forced the connector to touch his neck, cold and sharp. His training kicked in - every muscle tensed, ready to fight, but the chains held firm. The guards' weapons clicked in warning. The shock wave converged through him. But he stilled. Focusing on Daisy and friends, Alfred, Flora Face, when she smiled, when the mechon of his sister. He heard Andrew speak. A man he thought was his friend. “Turn it up! Break through him.”
But it didn't break his mind, now, to focus on the very one, the only one, Jesus.
“Lord, let them know, somehow let them know. Please”
Suddenly, just as the darkness started to claim him, a surge of power, peace, and protection flooded through him, and an image of a man smiling appeared. A voice telling him. Trust, trust, trust, trust my Love. The voice over baring his heart, flowing, and now he felt like no matter what happens, God was with him, and in that image, he saw an unthinkable thing, not a thing, a place. Heaven.
The device sparked violently, it's blue glow turning to angry red before dying completely.
"What's happening?" Andrew demanded, grabbing the smoking device from Stone's hands. "The neural patterns were perfect!"
Stone stared at his readings in disbelief. "It's like... like something's blocking us. The connection was there and then... it just wasn't."

"The ship leaves in an hour," Stone added, still eyeing Letzier with confusion.
"Perfect." Andrew grabbed Letzier's jaw, forcing eye contact. "You may have resisted our device, but you're still coming with us. And when we find your friends... I will make sure you watch them die!" He left the threat hanging. All Letzier could do was smile. “You think you will win, hah, you're fighting something bigger than me.”
Andrew stormed off like a child. Such a baby, Letzier thought.

**Daisy**
Daisy prayed without ceasing for Letzier's protection, the words becoming a rhythm that matched her heartbeat. Through the thin walls, fragments of conversation had reached her—something about neural mapping, about breaking his will. Letzier was strong, but was anyone strong enough for what they had planned?
The cell door opened, revealing familiar guards. Aaron entered first, followed by another she hadn’t seen as often—Ezra. He moved with precision, every step measured, his posture far more rigid than Aaron’s. Daisy had heard his name once in passing, but his silence had always made him harder to read.
"You're coming with us," Aaron said, voice flat but not cruel. Daisy caught his eye—he’d always been different. He listened when she talked. He brought her extra water once without being asked. Small kindnesses, but they mattered.
"Okay," she replied softly. "Where are we going?"
Ezra’s expression didn’t change, but Aaron tilted his head. "You know we can’t say. Protocol." Then, after a pause, he added quietly, "But Letzier’s still alive. He was strong enough, though it... It got rough. Andrew had it dialed high and..." He trailed off, glancing at Ezra, who didn’t flinch.
Relief crashed over her like a wave. God had heard her.
Aaron bound her hands in front instead of behind—another mercy—and gestured for Ezra to apply the blindfold. Surprisingly, Ezra tied it just loose enough to leave a sliver of sight. Maybe that was intentional.
They led her down a winding corridor, metal echoing underfoot. Then she saw him—Letzier, unconscious between two guards. Her breath caught at the angry scar across his face, blood still seeping from it.
She stumbled forward, collapsing against him on purpose. The guards barked at her, but Letzier’s fingers brushed hers in that moment, a faint squeeze—message. I’m still here.
Ezra stepped in, pulling her gently back. “You’re pushing your luck,” he muttered, not cruelly, not unkindly. It was the first time she’d heard him speak.
Aaron raised an eyebrow at him but said nothing.
They reached the ship. Letzier was thrown into a cell, and she was pushed into one opposite his—close enough to see him, far enough that no guard would worry about contact. Ezra adjusted her blindfold one last time before leaving, loosening it more. Aaron just shook his head with a small, resigned smile.
As the doors slammed shut behind them, Daisy let herself breathe. Letzier was here. Bruised, bleeding, maybe broken—but alive. And even in the worst place imaginable... they were together.
**Flora**
Flora stared out the window of the ship. She hadn’t expected space to be this... breathtaking. Vast. Quiet. Almost holy.
Zerak stepped beside her. “Beautiful, isn’t it?”
Her stomach tightened. Oh dear God... why him? Not him. She forced a polite smile. “You know, there are other people you could talk to besides me.”
He nodded, unfazed. “I know. I just prefer staying near you.”
She took a step back, unsure. Was she being cautious? Or... was she playing hard to get? She didn’t even know.
Before she could sort it out, Alfred appeared, his voice sharp. “Hey—stay away from her.”
Zerak raised an eyebrow. “Why? I’m not touching her.”
Alfred gestured toward Flora.
“Can’t you see she’s uncomfortable?”
Flora blinked. “Alfred, I’m fine. He’s not bothering me.”
Alfred didn’t back down. “Then why did you step away?”
She hesitated. She hadn’t thought about it. It was just instinct. “I don’t know,” she admitted. “I guess I felt... awkward.”
Alfred huffed. “Akword? Sounds the same.”
Flora breathed. Calmed steadily.
“It’s okay, Alfred. I’m fine, see? No harm done. He did help save me—why would he turn around and hurt me?”
Alfred crossed his arms. “I don’t trust him. Not around you. Not around Nathan.”
Flora let out a small laugh. “Could we not do this right now? Please? You can fight it out later—after we find my sister. For now, just... try to get along. For me.”
The hum of the ship filled the silence that followed. She slipped away from the others, finding a quiet corner near the observation deck. Stars drifted past like scattered diamonds, and for a moment, she let herself breathe.
Why did I step back? She replayed the moment in her mind. Zerak hadn’t done anything wrong. But something about him unsettled her, not in a bad way—his calmness, his eyes, the way he always seemed to know more than he said. Maybe she liked him. Maybe she didn’t want to like him. He wasn’t someone she’d normally hang around with, and that made it harder to sort through the feelings.
She bowed her head and whispered, barely audible to anyone but God. “Lord, take any desire that’s not of You. I just want to be with You right now.”
Silence. Her thoughts drifted to Alfred—what made him such a good friend. He loved people. He was stubborn, he cared deeply, and he was smart. Even if he doesn't realize it. Maybe a little zealous, definitely protective. Especially between her and Nathan.
She wondered why. Maybe her sister had something to do with it. Maybe. Zara…how she longed to see her again.
Jesus had that way—when nothing else in the world mattered. Not anymore. His way always prevailed. It was what her mother and father had told her before they passed.
Love when it’s hard. Have patience with people. Keep God at the front of your mind. Let Him direct your path.
When she was younger, she hadn’t believed it.
Not really. Not the way her parents did. But she’d watched God move through them—again and again. In their struggles. In their prayers. In the way they kept loving when it was hard.
If he could help them, He could help her. It was real. He was real.
She stood there, remembering when she was five.
Her mother had taught her the fruits of the Spirit like a song: Love, joy, peace, patience, kindness, goodness, and self-control. Self-control was the hardest.
At five, she didn’t understand. At ten, she still didn’t. She thought it meant being quiet, being good, being perfect.
But now—now she saw it.
Self-control wasn’t about pretending. It was about surrender. About letting go of pride, that quiet voice that always whispered, “You’re better than this. You don’t need help. There's nothing wrong with you.”
But even the small things, not being teachable, thinking that you are teachable. It was Flora's struggle, a big struggle. Within the church, within her. She looked up at the stars.
“God, forgive me of pride, take any anger away from me, don't let me falter in things that aren't of you. Let you guide me, teach me, I am yours, and you are mine.”
She needed God. And the joy of admitting that, admitting that you're wrong, even when it hurts.—of releasing the weight— It kept her. Time and time again.
A voice behind her spoke.
“Running from me?” His voice came softly from behind.
She turned, startled. “No. Just... needed air.”
Zerak leaned against the wall, arms crossed. “You’re not used to people like me.”
She frowned. “What’s that supposed to mean?”
“People who don’t hide what they feel.”
Her heart skipped. “And what do you feel?”
He didn’t answer right away. His gaze drifted to the stars. “You remind me of someone.”
She hesitated. “Who?”
“My sister. Before it disappeared.”
That stopped her cold. “I didn’t know you had a sister.”
“Most people don’t.” His voice softened. “She was shy. Gentle. Stubborn in her quiet way. Patient. Always overthinking everything. Smart. Helpful. And somehow... everyone liked her.”
Flora blinked, unsure what to say. She didn’t feel like someone everyone liked. But she knew what it was to overthink, to be patient, to hold back when others rushed in.
“She sounds... nice,” Flora said quietly.
“She was more than nice,” Zerak replied. “She was steady. Like gravity. You remind me of her—not because you’re the same, but because you carry that same kind of quiet strength.”
Flora looked away, her cheeks warm. She didn’t know what to do with that kind of compliment.
They stood in silence, the stars watching.
Chapter


**Zeb**
Zeb examined the spaceship’s controls. Flying it was easy — almost too easy. The interface was clear and responsive, brighter than any craft he’d piloted before. But it wasn’t the ease that mattered. It was the mission. The ship’s features — invisibility, shields, scanning systems — were more than tools. They were lifelines. He was going to find her. His Zara.
Tears threatened, but he held them back. “Hold on, Zeb. We’re not there yet,” he whispered.
Suddenly, the ship jolted violently. A tremor ran through the floor. Alarms flickered.
Amika burst into the room, Flora close behind.
“A massive ship is approaching us,” Amika said, breathless, eyes wide. “They’re coming.”
Zeb’s heart pounded. The moment felt too big, too fast. But something deeper stirred — a pull stronger than fear. A sudden urge to pray rose inside him, overwhelming and insistent.
“Lord, may we not forget You. Keep our focus on Your word. Stay with us as we journey through the stars. Lead us, for You brought us together — we are Your sons and daughters. May we follow You, guided by Your Spirit. Help us speak truth to one another, even when it’s hard to hear. You spoke the world into existence; lead me through the fires. Your truth is what we cling to. Be with Letzier, give him strength.”
The words flowed from his heart. He didn’t care if the others heard — he only hoped God did.
“Be with Daisy, and help them both find their way. Stay strong for Flora. Place boldness inside her. Be with Reanna, Nova, and all who are not here. And Lord… be with Zara. Don’t let her be gone before we arrive. You know my heart, you know what I long for. If it is Your will… may I marry Zara?”
Suddenly, Colten placed a hand on his shoulder. His own prayer spilled out, urgent and unrestrained:
“May we seek You above all things. May we speak love, truth, and hope to one another. Keep us humble before You. Forgive us, Lord — forgive even the enemy who rages against us. If there is any way for you to save them, please do. Let us not fall into pride. May we love You more than the air we breathe, more than the words we speak. Guide our hands to do Your will. Open our eyes to the truth — open them, Lord, open them wide. We are blind to sin, we deny the truth, we spit at Your name, and still You love us. Dear God, hear my cry. Stay with us, protect us. You did it before — do it again.”
Flora Shylee stood nearby, her voice trembling but resolute as she joined them:
“God, have mercy on my mouth. Use it for your truth, even when it’s hard, even when I just want to cry. Fear holds me, but may I sing praise. May I worship You when fear grips me. Help me seek Your face above all others. Hold me to Your word.”
Amika nodded quietly, her eyes glistening.
But not everyone was still.
Alfred stood near Nathen, who lay on the sofa, tense, watching.
Zerak didn’t speak — his jaw clenched, eyes sharp. He looked irritated. Not angry. Not yet.
“You praying won’t help this group,” he muttered.
Alfred turned sharply. Zeb rose from the captain’s chair.
“What was that, Zerak?” Alfred asked, voice low. Not harsh — but his eyes burned.
Zerak didn’t flinch. “It’s a waste of time. You think words are going to stop what’s coming?”
Alfred stepped forward. “You think silence will? You think standing there with your arms crossed makes you useful?”
“I saved Flora,” Zerak snapped. “What have you done besides bark orders and pretend you’re in charge?”
Zeb stepped between them. “Enough.”
But Alfred wasn’t done. “You don’t get to talk about pretending,” Alfred snapped. “You were with the BNA while the rest of us — citizens — suffered. You show up, act like you know everything, and now you want to lead?”
“I don’t want to lead,” Zerak said. “I want to survive.”
Amika stepped in, voice firm. “Calm down, Alfred. Zerak — Alfred’s right. It’s none of your business. Why? If you come close, I can show you.”
Colten moved fast, blocking her. “You don’t want to go near her.”
Zerak scoffed. “And so? I know how to fight.”
Flora’s voice cut through the tension. “Stop! Just stop!”
Zerak turned to her, something shifting in his face. His shoulders dropped. The heat in his eyes faded.
Zeb watched closely. Alfred’s expression changed — uneasy, guarded. Zeb felt it too. That sudden calm unsettled him. Zerak seemed… nice.
But the weight of the mission pressed harder now. The enemy was near. The crew was splintering. And somewhere out there, Zara was waiting.
**Flora**
Flora felt the shift in the atmosphere. The yelling, the bickering — it was like the air itself had thickened. The weight of the BNA ship pressing toward them was undeniable. It wasn’t just approaching. It was watching. Waiting.
“Guys, look,” Amika said softly, her footsteps slowing to a halt. Her eyes locked on the viewport.
Zeb turned in his seat, facing the controls. The vessel glided past them — massive, silent, effortless.
They were momentarily speechless.
“They’re just… flying over us,” Flora whispered.
Amika moved quickly to the computer console. Her fingers flew across the keys. The room was wide, high-ceilinged, spacious enough for all of them — but it suddenly felt too small.
“Guys,” Amika said, “Nova was able to send a message.”
Everyone moved toward her — except Zerak. Nathan remained on the sofa, still healing from the gunshot wound.
Alfred narrowed his eyes. “Really? She did? How?”
Amika pressed a button. The speakers crackled, then Nova’s voice came through — shaky, urgent.
“BNA is… on your way. I was able to place an invisible detection device before you all left. I want to tell you…
Letzier and Daisy are on that ship. Follow them — they’ll lead you to Zara. Once you’re there, that’s when you take action.
Two more ships are coming. Their mission is to make sure you don’t survive.
Stay safe. Nova out.”
Silence fell again.
Flora’s heart pounded. The ship outside wasn’t just passing by. It was bait. It was a signal.
And now they knew: Zara was close. Letzier and Daisy were alive. And death was on it's way.
**Reanna**
She moved quickly through the corridor, her boots barely making a sound against the cold floor. Every step felt heavier than the last. The walls around her were too clean, too quiet — like the BNA had sterilized not just the space, but the soul of the place.
She had to reach Letzier.
Daisy would be alright — if Reanna could place the right guards around her. Not the loyalists. The ones who hesitated. The ones who asked questions when they thought no one was listening.
She didn’t trust them. Not fully. But she didn’t doubt their minds were stirring.
Every day, someone came to her with quiet doubts. “Is this really the way?”
“Why do we silence people who ask questions?”
“What if the BNA isn’t what they say it is?”
Mostly, it was Aaron. He asked the hardest questions. Reanna placed Aaron to watch Daisy.
She reached the door. Her hand hovered over the panel.
Letzier was inside — sedated, restrained, monitored. They said it was for safety. She knew it was for control.
Like normally, Daisy would be across from him. She didn't say anything, just stared at the ground. Aaron was beside the jail cell. She nodded to him, and he nodded back.
They wanted her to extract Letzier's daily logs. His “daly,” as they called it. She didn’t care. Nova had given her a mission. And she would see it through.
She stepped inside the cell.
Letzier lay still, his face pale, his breathing shallow.
She moved to his side and shook him gently.
His eyes fluttered open, barely. “What now…” he rasped. His voice was dry, cracked.
He looked exhausted. Starved.
She wished she could give him something — food, water, comfort. But there wasn’t time. If the plan worked, he’d have all of that soon. She smiled softly, crouching beside him. “Good. You’re up,” she whispered.
She slipped a folded letter into his hand. “Here. Read this. Quickly. I’ll check your restraints.”
Letzier gave her a look — half confusion, half disbelief — but obeyed.
She moved around the room, covering the cameras one by one. Her hands shook slightly, but she kept going.
“You done?” she asked.
Letzier nodded. No smile. Just a flicker of understanding. “Alright. Clear.”
She took the letter back. Reached for the sedative. Injected it — but it was fake.
She leaned close, her voice barely audible.
“It’s fake. So pretend.”


**Alfred**
Alfred stood behind Zeb, watching the ship’s slow pursuit of the BNA vessel. The enemy ship moved with eerie grace, like it knew it was being followed — like it didn’t care.
He couldn’t believe Nova had managed to plant something on their ship. That fast. That's clean. But then again… it was Nova. A hacker, yes — but more than that. She was relentless. Brilliant. She’d gotten them onto this ship when no one else could.
Still, the doubts clawed at him. What if the invisibility fails? What if they detect us? What if this whole mission ends before it begins? The silence of space pressed in. The hum of the ship felt louder than usual.
His gaze drifted toward Zerak.
He sighed.
Flora didn’t need him.
He could feel it — the way Zerak looked at her, the quiet tension between them. Even though Flora had told him, back at the Dome, that she couldn’t be with him before she even knew his name. That God had to decide.
But Alfred remembered that moment. The way she looked at Zerak when they first saw him. The way Zeb hesitated.
Flora wasn’t supposed to be with Zerak.
Alfred felt it like a burn in his chest. Anger. Pure and sharp. He didn’t trust Zerak. Didn’t like him.
And then Flora walked toward him, her steps soft but certain. “You’re upset?” she asked.
Alfred looked at her. Those eyes. That calm.
How could he blame Zerak?
She carried something he couldn’t — a quiet strength. A peace that didn’t shatter, even when everything else did. She stayed hopeful. When life hit her, she stood. When she wanted to quit, she didn’t, even when she didn’t believe it herself.
He wished he could do the same. But the truth was… he was too broken for her.
He’d lost his parents. He clenched his teeth, remembering seventh grade — the silence, the shame, the way grief had hollowed him out and left him pretending to be whole. He would rather not mention it.
But Flora saw it anyway.
She stepped closer, voice soft. “It’s okay. You don’t want to talk about it.”
Alfred opened his mouth. Closed it.
He looked around the room — the hum of the ship, the distant stars, the quiet tension pressing in from all sides.
Then he said, “Is it possible to get a signal to Zara?”
Flora blinked. “Really?” She could tell — he was shifting the conversation. But the question still held weight.
Alfred smiled, thin and tired. “Yeah. I mean… she sent a help signal all the way out here. You’d think we could try sending something back. If I’m right, Zara’s smart. She’d know how to respond. If Nova can do it… maybe she can, too.”
He was deflecting. But he meant it. He’d been thinking about it since the message. Was it possible?
Flora studied him, then lowered her head and shook it. “I’ll leave this for now. But we’ll talk later, alright?”
He nodded, smiling again — this time with something behind it. He was counting on it.


**Zara**
The days blurred together in this endless purple twilight. Food supplies remained steady enough for a few more months if rationed carefully. The ship's emergency stores were at least intact after the crash, even if everything else was twisted beyond repair. "Thank you, Lord, for this provision," she whispered, a habit kept even here in the vastness of space.
Zara pressed her hand against the crystalline ground, feeling the slow, steady pulse beneath. At first, the living planet had terrified her - the way it breathed, the way it moved, how the very surface seemed alive beneath her feet. Now, after so long, it felt like evidence of God's incredible creativity. Who else could design an entire planet that lived and breathed like some cosmic flower?
The signal beacon blinked steadily from it's perch on the highest crystal formation. Every day, the same message: Here. Alive. Help. Her daily act of faith - believing that someone would hear it and come.
Her helmet's display flickered as the filtration system struggled again. The planet's "breath" was breathable, but something in it made her head fuzzy if inhaled too much directly. Like being drunk on air. The spores, maybe, or whatever those floating purple particles were.
"Flora would love this," she whispered, imagining her sister's face lit up with wonder at the bioluminescent crystals. "She'd probably have figured out why the whole planet's one giant plant by now." A smile crossed her face, thinking of Letzier, too. He wouldn't give up looking - that wasn't in his nature. His stubborn faith was one of the things she'd always admired about him.
A tremor ran through the ground - the planet taking another breath. She'd learned to time them now. Inhale: the crystals dim slightly, the air grows heavier. Exhale: everything glows brighter, fresh oxygen flooding the atmosphere. Like clockwork, every six hours. Even in isolation, God had given her this rhythm to hold onto.
The worn Bible in her hands - somehow still intact after the crash. Another miracle. The pages fell open to Psalm 139: "If I rise on the wings of the dawn, if I settle on the far side of the sea, even there your hand will guide me..." Her fingers traced the familiar words, finding comfort in their truth. Even here, on this strange breathing planet, she wasn't beyond His reach.
"They'll come," she prayed softly, watching the purple horizon. "Letzier won't stop until he finds me. Flora won't let them give up." The planet breathed beneath her, a reminder that even in the furthest reaches of space, life persisted. And where there was life, there was hope.
Her mind trailed off, thinking of Zeb, his kind features, how he loved the Lord, and how he loved her. She missed him. Her heart squeezed. From her ship, she heard a beep noise. She rushed to it. Hoping that it was someone who heard her. Coming.. Me.. Zeb…On…our…way.
Her eyes stared at the scene from her broken ship, in shock, words didn't form. Was this real? She looked up, and finally she cried. Her hand was over her mouth. His voice. She missed him so. She looked up and prayed Thanks. This was hope.

**Zeb**
Zebs stomach turned, existed, and was devastated all at the same time.
That was her, her cry for help. He wanted to hold her, keep her safe; he chuckled to himself. She wasn't one for hugs. But in this case, he probably wouldn't let her go; if they survived, he would propose to her.
He slipped out a prayer.


Zeb did hope that all of mankind would see that the government was corrupt, with evil people. If they can prove that Zara was alive, the people will turn against them. Perhaps there was a reason for being here; maybe the main reason the lord is pushing us to do this is to gather evidence. Was it? Colten pushed us all to do this mission, not just because Zara was alive, but because of the lie that they told us they were dead. He began to think. It would make sense. Because why risk your life, not just their life, but everyone's life?

Chapter 26
**Letzier**
Flora and Alfred came uncuffing him, Daisy beside them. Aaron was there too. Keeping an eye out. Letzier flexed his wrists, the blood rushing back into his hands. His muscles coiled, ready, his body screaming for release. “Took y'all long enough,” Letzier said.


Alfred sighed. “We got lost in traffic,”.
Aaron then spoke.
“We don't have time to chit chat, Stone is on his way.”
Letzier stepped out,
“Let's hurry,”
They all started running. “Reanna did tell you the plane, right?!” Alfred asked.
Letzier didn't speak.
He knew the plane. Just then, Letzier heard a cry, Daisy.
Behind them. Letzier tuned. He clenched his teeth. Daisy was caught in Stone's grip, a knife pointed at her throat.
Letzier noticed, Aaron was not here…Did he betray?
Alfred and Flora stood beside him. while the atmosphere was charged, and they were running out of time.


Letzier turned to Alfred and gave him a nod. “Go,”
Alfred responded with a nod of his own. He grabbed Flora's hand and they started running.


Letzier smiled to himself, feeling renewed. determination. He wouldn't make the same mistake.


Daisy suddenly squeezed out of Stone's grip and sprinted to Letzier. Stone hurled his knife at her, but Letzier caught the handle before it struck it's target.
“Daisy, run!”
She didn’t hesitate. She left, leaving him to deal with Stone. Hopefully, she would be able to reach Alfred.
"Come, let us fight fairly. The one who wins gets out alive, the one who loses doesn’t," Stone said, cruelty emanating from his voice.
"Are you sure?" Letzier asked.
Stone smiled, as if this were fun to him. But Letzier wasn’t bothered; he knew how to fight. Better than his father. Stronger even.
"Yes, let us play — where your begging will be my victory," Stone said.
Either Stone was an idiot or plain stupid. Or both. Wasn’t he the one who destroyed basically fifty AI‑intelligent robots with his bare fists and still survived?
Letzier gave a small chuckle to himself. "Let’s go."
Finally, real action.
Stone pursued Letzier relentlessly, but Letzier deftly slid beneath him. In a swift move, he landed a solid punch to Stone’s face.
They exchanged blows until Stone’s hand clamped around Letzier’s neck. Struggling for air, Letzier drove a kick into his chest, forcing him back just as Stone activated a hidden blade. Stone lunged, thrusting the weapon toward Letzier’s chest, but Letzier caught his arm mid‑strike and, with a sharp twist, hurled him over his shoulder. Stone hit the ground hard, groaning, yet pushed himself back up.
Letzier pressed forward, landing several kicks and punches as Stone tried to block and dodge. After about five seconds of this, Letzier spun into a flying kick that smashed into Stone’s face. Stone flew back a few feet, then crumpled down.
Letzier walked up to him and tore the hidden blade off his wrist. Letzier was surprised by how strong Stone was.
Rule one: Never underestimate your opponent.
"You should’ve known the price of evil. And it hurts to know that you belong here," Letzier said, his voice steady, as if he didn’t feel bad. Maybe a little. Maybe for a moment.
He looked Stone in the eye. “No one to call, everybody to fear. Your tragic fate is becoming increasingly obvious."
Letzier spoke.
"Kill me," Stone said. "You won."
Letzier shook his head.
"I’m not going to do that. Leave. Go, before I change my mind. Everyone here won’t survive what we have planned."
Stone hesitated, suddenly paling. But Letzier didn’t bother. Nova’s plan was about to set in motion, and he needed to get to the armory room fast.
Praying Daisy had made it out, he ran. As fast as he could. Just then, he stopped. Aaron was already there.
Letzier then yelled out. “Where were you?”
Aaron then smiled. “Telpotring Coins remember.”
Letzier hesitated, but then nodded. If Reanna trusted him, there had to be a reason.
“Let me get ready for the plane. You make sure Daisy gets to the pods before it's too late.”
Aaron nodded slowly.
“I was able to connect Nova's computer to the AI unit. She's there. Ready.”
Letzier nodded. “That's why you left sooner. Aaron nodded.”
Letzier felt guilty; he should do this, he needed to make sure Daisy was Safe.
Aaron then looked at him. “I will protect Daisy if it means my life, Letzier, you can trust me.”
Letzier gave him a side eye. “As if I can believe that.”
“The WTB needs you right now; they're losing. I will not break my promise to Reanna. I am a man of my word.”
Letzier had no choice but to trust him. “Alright, hurry.”
