Chapter 27
**Alfred**
Alfred stood eye to eye with Andruw — the man who had turned Letzier into a science experiment, imprisoned Daisy, and nearly killed Zara.
“How do you know my name? I mean, I knew of you… But we’ve never met.”
Andruw laughed, too calm, too cordial. A shiver crawled down Alfred’s spine.
“You don’t know, do you?”
Behind him, Flora screamed. “Alfred, come on!”
But Alfred didn’t move. He felt frozen. This man knew something he didn’t — something that mattered.
“Know what?” Alfred demanded.
Andruw chuckled again. “Your grandmother never told you? Figures.”
Alfred’s voice rose, sharp and violent even to his own ears. “Tell me!”
“You’re just like your father,” Andruw said smoothly. “Those same eyes. That same determination.”
Alfred’s grip tightened around his gun. His heart pounded. He wanted to shoot — but he wanted answers more.
Stone appeared suddenly in the corridor. Alfred’s mind raced. Letzier should already be activating. He didn’t know what to do.
Desperation clawed at him. He looked at Andruw, voice breaking. “Tell me, please. I’ll do whatever I can to—” The words caught in his throat. He almost said it. Almost promised to help.
Andruw leaned forward, eyes gleaming. “You what?”
Alfred’s chest tightened. He couldn’t breathe. For a moment, he wanted to give in — to trade freedom for truth. But then Flora’s voice cut through the haze, pulling him back. At least he thought it was her.
**“Alfred!”**
He turned and bolted toward her. Revenge would come later.


But before he could get far, Andruw’s voice thundered after him: “I’m your uncle, Alfred.”
Alfred froze mid‑stride. The words cut like a blade. Slowly, he stopped. Flora was already ahead, calling his name.
He shook his head, forcing his legs to move. He couldn’t give in. Not now.
Andruw’s voice echoed down the corridor, venomous: “I won’t die, Alfred. We’ll find you again. And Flora will die first. You will pay!”
Alfred gritted his teeth. Good. We’ll be waiting.
Finally, they reached the exit — freedom just ahead. But before he could step through, seven guards blocked the way, rifles raised.
“Under arrest,” one barked.
Alfred’s hand tightened around the sword Letzier had given him. His pulse hammered. Now or never. May the Lord be with me.
He moved. Swift, precise. The blade flashed, cutting down the first guard, then another. Gunfire erupted, bullets sparking against the walls. One man fired at him, but Alfred rolled aside, closing the distance. His sword pierced the guard’s chest, dropping him to the floor.
Another lunged, swinging his rifle like a club. Alfred twisted, driving his blade across the man’s throat. He fell, lifeless.
The corridor rang with chaos — shouts, gunfire, steel. Alfred’s breath came hard, but his focus sharpened. He remembered the training, every drill, every lesson. He fought not just for himself, but for Flora, for Letzier, for all of them.
Three guards remained. Alfred raised his sword, eyes blazing. “Come then,” he growled. “I will not fall.”
The three looked at each other, but shook their heads. They ran. And Alfred felt relieved. Flora was there waiting.


Letzier should be in the suit by now. Flora stood waiting for him.
“What took you?” Alfred didn't answer. “Let's go hurry.”
They closed the hatch, heading to the planet, where they will finally find Zara. Alfred looked at Flora. Her face was full of worry; he wasn't sure who was more worried, right now, him or her.
“Did you call for me, Flora?” Alfred asked. She looked at him, confused. “What do you mean?”
He paused, his mind spinning. He was sure it was her voice, right? He trailed back in his mind, now that he thought about it, was it even her?
They finally landed, and Alfred felt anxious. Letzier should already be in the outer void, ready to destroy anything in it's path. He laid down any thoughts.


It was time to find Zara.
**Letzier.**
He gave his all, forcing the BNA back from the WTB spaceship. Every strike, every surge of energy was poured into the fight. He rammed one droid, then another, metal shrieking as they shattered against his suit’s force. For a moment, it reminded him of a movie he’d watched at six years old — heroes standing alone against impossible odds. But this wasn’t a movie. This was real.
Finally, the WTB ship broke through the blockade, streaking toward the planet below. Relief flickered in his chest, but there was no time to savor it.
He turned, power draining fast, his body trembling inside the suit. He told himself he would be alright. He wasn’t planning to die. Not today. Not tomorrow.
Three BNA vessels loomed ahead, massive and merciless. He wouldn’t let them touch the ship. Not while he still had strength.
He surged forward, the suit roaring with energy. Blasts lit the void around him. He dodged one, then another, spinning through the firestorm. A drone clipped his shoulder — sparks flew — but he slammed it aside, tearing through it's frame.
Breath ragged, muscles burning, he pushed harder. Anger flared — at Andruw’s betrayal, at Daisy’s near death — but beneath it, something deeper rose.
This was hope. For the mission. For Zara. For all of them. He prayed for forgiveness. But it had to be done.
He was out of breath, but he wasn't done yet. It was time to use everything he had.
He moved with speed, so much force, he stiffened. His muscles blazing, was it anger? Angry that Andruw betrayed him, angry that they almost killed Daisy. This, this was for them the WTB. For the mission, for Zara. Letzier prayed. And a peace swept through him. This wasn't revenge; it was hope.
**Flora**
Flora held her breath as they sealed their suits. This was an unknown planet; Zeb had said it was alive.
The hatch opened, and they stepped out. Above them, the sky burned — BNA drones clashed with Letzier, buying the WTB time to escape.
“You remember the coordinates, right?” Flora asked.
Alfred nodded. “Yes. This way.” He pointed, steady but tense. Zeb should be on his way now.
“Let’s—” Alfred stopped as a thunderous boom shook the ground. One BNA vessel exploded above. Another blast followed. He gasped.
“Letzier…” Alfred whispered. He grabbed Flora’s hand. “Let’s hurry. We’re running out of time.” His voice was steady, but Flora’s stomach twisted. She knew — Letzier would use the suit to destroy all three vessels.
Flora's breath was shallow under her space helmet. Fear clawed at her emotions. She was tired.
They ran toward Zara’s last known location, praying Letzier would survive.
The sky split as the last BNA vessel collapsed, burning as it plummeted through the clouds.
“Alfred!” Flora cried.
“I see it! Keep running!” he shouted.
Suddenly, the WTB — Zeb’s ship, Redemption, broke through the smoke, it's engines roaring as it cut across the burning sky. Hope surged through Flora’s chest, but it was short‑lived. She stumbled, crashing hard to the ground. Alfred spun toward her instantly.
She bit back a scream, clutching her leg. Pain radiated sharply and hotly. Her space suit torn, Alfred dropped beside her, his hand gripping her arm. “Come on.”
“I… I can’t. It hurts.”
Alfred’s jaw tightened. His eyes flicked upward at the falling wreckage, then back to her. He pulled her close, voice low but firm. “Lean on me. Hurry.”
Flora nodded, breath shaking, and together they pressed forward, step by step.
Above them, the sky split again. A massive section of the destroyed vessel tore downward, glowing red as it fell. Alfred shoved Flora down, shielding her with his body as the wreckage slammed into the earth nearby. The ground quaked, dust and fire exploding outward.
Flora’s heart pounded. She buried her face against his shoulder for a moment, trembling, before forcing herself upright. Alfred steadied her, his grip strong, his focus unshaken.


**Zeb**
Zeb moved carefully, the spaceship. But his inside turned knowing that Letzier would have been killed.
“I can't believe Letzier would do something so recluse. That wasn't the plan.” Reanna huffed. Zeb nodded.


“It's not surprising, though.”
Amika then spoke, “We need to go back!”
Reanna huffed. “Yeah, sure, go back, not realising that The BNA reckige is heading straight to where Flora and Alfred are!”

Through the haze, Flora caught a glimpse — Amika and Reanna, standing on the ship. Relief surged, but it was tangled with fear.
The hatch opened with a hiss. “Come on!” Reanna shouted, waving them in.
Alfred glanced at Flora’s foot, saw the blood and the rip. Without hesitation, he scooped her into his arms. She gasped, pain flaring, but didn’t protest.
The world around them roared — falling debris, Zeb’s ship firing, the living planet trembling beneath their feet. Alfred held her tighter, moving quickly toward the hatch.
Flora pressed her eyes shut, trying to block out the pain. She wanted to cry, but forced it back. She was stronger than this.

**Tab 31**
The night was cold as Zara trudged forward, her back aching with every step. A trickle of blood ran down her right arm, staining the tattered sleeve of her suit. Some flakes, that reminded her of Snow, fell silently from the sky, dusting the ground in a still, unsettling silence.
She had crash-landed on an unknown planet.
Her gaze flicked toward the wreckage—the twisted remains of the ship that was supposed to carry her safely through the stars. Smoke still rose from the debris, curling into the darkness above. How?
There had been no asteroids. No signs of mechanical failure. The engineers had assured her the ship was perfectly intact before launch. And yet…
She was here. Alone.
The air held oxygen—thankfully—but it felt strange. Heavy. Almost alive.
She’d managed to breathe upon impact, but something about the atmosphere felt off. Dense. Pulsing in a way she couldn’t quite place. She didn’t have time to dwell on it now—she needed shelter.
Spotting a darkened cave, she stumbled toward it and collapsed inside. Drawing her knees to her chest, Zara pressed her forehead against them, trying to steady her shaking breath. She wanted to cry, but the tears refused to fall.
Her mind drifted—Flora.
Her sister’s hazel eyes, bright and fearless, paired with that shimmering red hair. How often had Zara imagined the day Flora would finally make it to Space School? How had she seemed when she left—excited? Scared?
And Nathan. Her brother. The quiet observer with piercing blue eyes and black hair. They, but he was family all the same.
Had they heard what happened? Did they know? Were they safe?
Zara squeezed her eyes shut, whispering a silent prayer for their protection.
But as the words left her lips, a thought crept in—an unsettling presence lurking at the edge of her mind.
She had made enemies at Space School. Not everyone had welcomed her plans, her discoveries, her existence.
Would they do something like this? Sabotage the ship?
She hoped—prayed—that wasn’t true.
But deep down, she feared the answer wasn’t the one she wanted.


Chapter 1
**Zara Footsteps**
**Flora P. O. V**
Flora walked down the space school hallway, each step echoing with the weight of Zara’s absence. The scientists’ words still haunted her—no wreckage, no signal, no way to find her sister’s body. Just silence.
Her sister was dead, and her friends vanished, Nova, Amika, everyone.
She clutched her books tighter, steadying her breath. She and Zara had always been different—Flora, quiet and observant, with curly red hair and blue eyes; Zara, taller, bolder, with straight hair and a smile that could melt tension in a room. Opposites, but inseparable.
Colten—her adopted father—had said Zeb, her boyfriend, would pick her up after class. Flora wasn’t sure what to expect. She hadn’t seen him since the crash, and just the thought of facing him made her chest tighten, a wave of emotions threatening to overwhelm her.
In that moment, the memory of Zara pierced through the shadows of her mind, bringing both comfort and heartache.


Zara looked at Flora, her eyes bright yet shadowed with an unspoken understanding as they sat together in their dimly lit room. “One day, you will walk the same halls I walked. You’re going to need to know how to be strong, how to keep your eyes on the Lord, especially when everything feels like it's falling apart," she urged, her voice steady but tinged with urgency.
Flora's heart ached at the thought. “I get it… But you’ll be with me on my first day, right?”
Zara let out a deep sigh, shaking her head slowly as if the weight of the world rested upon her shoulders. “The day I finally get to fly, V78, happens to be the same day you go. Remember that?”
“But why can’t you just... try?” Flora pleaded, fragile hope flickering in her chest.
Zara’s response came soft yet firm, “As much as I long to be there with you, you know I can’t.” The pain in her eyes mirrored Flora’s own, their shared dreams fading like echoes against the stark walls of reality.


The voices around them echoed off the polished surfaces of the space school’s main corridor, low, scattered conversations mingling with the hum of boots against the cold metal flooring. Laughter erupted occasionally from the groups of students, a haunting reminder of what should have been, but Flora’s heart felt heavy as she inhaled the faint smell of ozone and sterilized tech that now seemed to symbolize both hope and loss. Each breath she took was a reminder that Zara would never be there to share that monumental first day, leaving Flora to navigate the halls alone, forever changed by the past.


Flora moved through the crowd like a ghost, clutching her books close. She didn’t know what the whispers were saying—didn’t want to. Her presence felt too loud, too visible, like grief had marked her in a way everyone could see.
Then two girls broke from the flow of students and strode toward her.
“Hey, look who dropped in. A newbie?” said the first, her brown hair pulled tight, dark eyes sharp with something that wasn’t curiosity.
The girl beside her looked similar—same angular features, but paler, more hesitant. She lingered a step behind.
Flora offered a small smile, trying to keep her voice steady. “Nice to meet you. I’m Flora.”
The first girl scoffed. “No one asked for your name.”
The second girl shifted, uneasy. “Nalie, she’s Flora. You know what hap—”
“I don’t care who she is,” Nalie snapped, cutting her off. Her voice was louder now, drawing a few glances from nearby students.
Then her tone changed—sweet, sudden, and false. “Hi, Alfred. We were just talking.”
Flora turned. Alfred stood behind her, silent and still, his gaze cold enough to freeze a star. He wore the same blue Space School blazer as she did, his brown eyes steady beneath tousled hair. His Asian features and quiet confidence made it clear—he’d walked these halls more times than he cared to count.
“Were you now?” he said, voice quiet but heavy.
Both girls nodded quickly, their confidence draining.
“Well then,” he said, low and deliberate, “how about you move along—before this gets ugly.”
The hallway seemed to hush around them. The girls didn’t argue. They turned and disappeared into the crowd, their footsteps quick and uneven.
Flora felt the blood drain from her face. “Uh, hi, I don’t—”
Alfred’s expression softened. He smiled, and somehow, she calmed.
“No need to worry,” he said gently. “Come on. I’ll walk you to class. Zara’s sister, right?”
Flora swallowed. The mention of her sister tightened something in her chest, like a string pulled taut. “Yes,” she rasped.
Alfred smiled, not unkindly. “Room 1234, yeah? Let’s get you there.”
He strode through the hallways with the easy grace of a senior student, moving with quiet confidence. Flora followed, keeping pace beside him. Her eyes scanned the unfamiliar halls, trying not to feel too small. Normally, anxiety would grip her, but a sense of peace surrounded her, like a whisper from the Lord in her heart: "I'm with you."
The divine whisper carried such certainty that for a moment, her doubts melted away. She wasn't just Flora, the quiet sister, the one left behind—she was His child, chosen for a purpose she couldn't yet see.
As they walked, Alfred spoke softly. “We had a few classes together. She talked about you all the time—how good you are at math, how much you love space exploration.”
Flora blinked, surprised. “She always said her little sister would end up here someday.”
She slowed, a small smile tugging at her lips as she glanced toward the classroom. “That’s Mr. Colten’s class.”
Alfred followed her gaze. “I’ve heard he’s one of the best teachers here.” He paused, catching himself. “I mean—from what people have told me since I transferred.”
“He’s my adopted father,” Flora said softly, surprised by how natural the words felt. Saying it aloud grounded her. “After our dad passed away, he took us in—me, Zara, and Nathan. He’s been there ever since.”
Alfred’s eyes widened. “Really? I knew he was close to Zara, but I didn’t realize…” He looked back at Mr. Colten with new respect. “That explains a lot. No wonder she always spoke so highly of him.”
Flora nodded, her throat tightening. Watching him teach made space exploration possible again—like something Zara would still be proud of.


**Alfred P. O. V**
Alfred gestured gently. “Come on. Room 1234’s just around the corner. We don’t want you to be late on your first day.”
Flora nodded and followed him through the winding corridors of Space School. Her steps were slow, deliberate—like each carried more weight than it should.
That glow around her again.
He’d seen it once in Zara. Familiar, but not the same.
He blinked it away. Maybe it was just his eyes. Or maybe not.
Room 1234 came into view. Alfred knew exactly where it was; it was the same room he’d entered on his first day. The same place he’d first met Zara.
Zara, who had been like family to him.
He glanced at Flora. She clutched her books tightly, guarded. She reminded him of the promise he’d made—to protect her and Nathan. Zara had asked him to, just before she boarded the ship.
He intended to keep it.
At the door, he paused. “Here’s your class,” he said, placing a hand on her shoulder. “If you need anything, I’m here. I mean that.”
She hesitated, her blue eyes searching his face for sincerity.
“Flora, you can't trust me,” Alfred said, his voice low, steady.
Her eyes flicked away, guarded. Like she’d heard those words before—and been let down.
But then she nodded and stepped inside.
Alfred watched her go, jaw tight. He wouldn’t let history repeat itself.
He’d find the truth—about Zara, the explosion, and Nathan’s missing sister.
No matter what it costs.
**Letzier P. O. V**
Letzier positioned himself for battle as Blade lunged with a kick. In one swift motion, he caught Amika’s foot, yanked him down, and locked him in a chokehold, securing his wrists and keeping him grounded—merciful, but firm.
Coach Andrew’s familiar grin lingered. But something about it felt off. A flicker in his expression gave Letzier a strange vibe.
“Time! Letzier, you win!” the coach called, his smile still fixed in place.
Letzier straightened, breath steady, muscles humming from the match. Questions loomed—about the coach’s expression, about the unease in the room—but he shoved them aside.
“Of course I did,” Letzier said, brushing dust from his sleeve. But his eyes stayed on the coach’s faltering smile.
He walked over to Blade and lifted his hand.
“Thanks,” Blade muttered.
Letzier nodded. “No problem.” He considered offering training help—Blade could use it—but decided against it. His life was too full.
Now, Space School was his focus. And beneath the drills and classes, one mission drove him: finding Zara.
It wasn’t about whether she was dead. That wasn’t the question. It was about the lie. The launch had been rushed. The scientists said everything was fine. But Letzier didn’t believe them.
Zara had been like a sister. She’d brought him and Daisy together. And Daisy—he couldn’t bear the sorrow in her eyes. Every time he thought of Zara, his chest tightened.
She didn’t just vanish. She was stolen by a promise that wasn’t kept.
He sat on the bench, water bottle in hand, but barely tasted it. His mind was elsewhere—racing, aching. He should’ve checked the ship himself. Should’ve asked harder questions. Should’ve stopped her.
The crash hadn’t given enough proof. Just fragments. Just silence.
And silence wasn’t the truth.
He would find out what really happened.
“Hey, Letzier, you good?” Coach Andrew’s voice cut through the haze.
Letzier blinked, then nodded. “Yeah.”
Andrew studied him for a moment, concern flickering behind his usual calm. But he didn’t press.
“Okay. Tell Alfred I said hi, would ya?”
“I will. I’m heading to my next class now. See you next week.”
Letzier stood, the weight of his promise pressing against his chest. He’d made it to Daisy. To himself. To Zara.
He wouldn’t let her story end in a lie.
Class 87 was next.
The halls leading there were quieter, the air heavier. Fewer students walked this path—only those willing to confront what others ignored. It wasn’t just a class. It was a threshold. A place built for those who had lost someone, or suspected the truth had been buried beneath protocol and polished reports.
He and Alfred had chosen it together. Not for credits. Not for prestige. But for answers.
Class 87 was confidential. A course designed for those investigating failed missions, vanished crew, and the shadows left behind. It was where whispers became data, where grief met resolve, where Letzier hoped to find the thread that would lead him back to Zara—or at least to the truth of what stole her.
He walked toward the door, pulse steady, heart braced. Whatever Class 87 held, he was ready to face it.
Chapter 2
**Nathan P. O. V**
Nathan sat quietly as Mr. Colten spoke, but his attention had already drifted. He wasn’t really listening—not the way he should’ve been. His gaze wandered to the window, and there she was. His sister.
A small smile tugged at Nathan’s lips. She didn’t notice him, but that was okay. He was proud of her—whether she knew it or not. He breathed, remembering how hard this was for her. He knew how it felt, having been there himself, having missed his own sister, not knowing if she was alive, and now Zara. How much more could he lose? He sighed. He wanted to know how to use a
A sharp snap broke the moment.
“Nathan, are you listening?” Mr. Colten asked, his voice gentle, a faint smile playing at the corners of his mouth.
Nathan turned back, matching the smile. “If I’m being honest... no. Not really.”
Mr. Colten nodded. “we'll, then you’d know we have an upcoming test.”
Nathan nodded out of habit, but his thoughts had already slipped away.
He remembered the day Flora’s parents adopted him and Reanna. He’d been nine—too young to grasp the full weight of loss, but old enough to feel its shape. Flora and Zara’s parents had died, and Colten had stepped in, gathering them all like scattered stars and trying to make a new constellation. Back then, it felt like healing. Like hope.
But now… Reanna was missing. Zara was gone. And the cold truth settled in his chest like frost. He hadn’t realized how much he’d lost until it was too late.
The silence around it all was the worst part. No answers. Just absence. And the ache that came with knowing he couldn’t protect the people he loved—not then, not now.


**Alfred P. O. V**
Alfred marched toward Class 87, his mind racing with questions about Zara. The hallway buzzed—chatter, lockers slamming, sneakers squeaking—but he barely registered it. His thoughts were elsewhere. Back to the first day he saw her.
He’d walked into Space School, full of dreams he couldn’t afford. Studying there had always felt out of reach. Still, he waited for Letzier, hoping they’d hang out, maybe play Minecraft, and forget the weight of reality.
Then Letzier appeared—mid-conversation with a somewhat short girl, her brown hair tucked behind one ear. Beside her stood another girl, her hair a fiery mix of orange and red. Letzier smiled. “Hey, Alfred. This is Daisy and Zara.” Alfred smiled back. “Hi.”
The memory echoed through him like a distant song. Emotions swirled—nostalgia, confusion, urgency. He had to see her. He had to find out. Someone had sabotaged it. He could feel it.
Dan popped up beside him, leaning casually against the wall. “You look like you’re about to storm the principal’s office,” he said with a grin. “Relax, man. It’s not a crime to be mysterious.”
Alfred gave a half-smile, stepping out of memory and back into reality. “Depends on the mystery.”
Dan winked. “we'll, if you find out the vending machine’s been rigged, I want in.”
Before Alfred could reply, Stone stepped into view—calm, unreadable, like a shadow that had learned to smile.
“Alfred,” Stone said, voice smooth. “Still chasing ghosts?”
Alfred stiffened. “Still pretending you’re not one?”
Stone’s smile didn’t falter. “Careful. Some ghosts bite.”
He walked past, leaving a trail of unease in his wake.
Alfred exhaled, tension still coiled in his chest—until Azreal appeared beside him, backpack slung over one shoulder, radiating calm.
“Don’t let him get in your head,” Azreal said quietly. “God’s light cuts through every shadow.”
Alfred nodded, the words grounding him. He nodded.
“Thanks, I think,” he said.
Azreal offered a small smile. “Let’s head to 87. Letzier’s waiting.”
And just like that, he was moving. Alfred followed, steadier now, the tension from earlier beginning to fade.
As they walked, Azreal glanced over. “I heard Zara’s sister is here now?”
Alfred nodded, a faint smile tugging at his lips. “Yeah. Flora just transferred. I walked her to class. Nalie was already stirring things up.”
Azreal sighed. “Figures. Nalie really needs to back off.”
Alfred nodded. “She’s been extra lately.”
They reached the door to Class 87, where Letzier stood waiting, arms crossed and unimpressed.
“Took y’all long enough,” he said, raising a brow. “You’re usually early, Alfred.”
Alfred shrugged. “Flora just transferred. I was showing her around. And Nalie… we'll, you know.”
Letzier rolled his eyes. “Classic.”
Then he turned to Azreal. “Sup, Azreal.”
Azreal smiled. “Hey. How’s the 87 Crue holding up?”
Letzier sighed. “Slow as always. Everyone’s dragging today.”
Class 87 was quiet—just a few scattered students. Alfred knew them all: Elora, who always showed up like it was her duty; Lunna and Ava, who shared Elora’s quiet resolve but rarely spoke; and Julie, who kept her distance, headphones in, eyes elsewhere.
They weren’t exactly close. Conversations were rare, and when they happened, they felt more like passing shadows than real connections.
Azreal leaned against the wall, scanning the room. “Flora’s not in this class, right?”
Alfred shook his head. “Nah, she’s in 1234. Like I said before.”
Azreal nodded. “Nalie is just… Nalie. Hard to talk to her when her mind’s locked on one thing. You might want to keep an eye on Flora, just in case.”
Alfred nodded. Out of the corner of his eye, he saw Letzier cracking his knuckles, a gleam flickering in his gaze.
Azreal shook his head. “Really? Already planning to stir things up?”
Letzier glanced toward the hallway.
“If Flora’s anything like Zara, she won’t stay quiet for long. And neither will I.”
Azreal smiled faintly. “Everyone knows Zara. Hard not to.”
Alfred settled in his seat, and so did Azreal.
Alfred nodded, the weight of that truth settling between them. Zara had left a mark—and now Flora was walking through the echoes.
He turned to Azreal. “Think you’ll get a chance to meet Flora? Maybe hang out after school?”
Azreal hesitated, then exhaled. “I’d love to, but things are kinda packed right now. Mom and Dad have me on my tiptoes—chores, Bible class, all of it. There’s this new kid, Sileth, in Bible class. He and I were talking about handing out Bibles together. And we’re going camping once summer hits.”
Alfred chuckled. “You’re always doing something.”
Azreal smiled, a quiet warmth in his eyes. Before either of them could say more, the classroom door slid open and the teacher stepped in, clipboard in hand.
“Alright, Class,” he said, voice firm but calm, “here’s what we’re diving into today.”
The room settled. Conversations faded. Alfred shifted in his seat, the weight of everything—Zara, Flora, Stone—still lingering at the edges of his thoughts. But for now, Class 87 demanded his focus.
And somewhere beneath the surface, he hoped today’s lesson might bring him one step closer to the truth.
**Letzier P. O. V**
Letzier pulled out his phone between classes, his fingers hovering over Daisy's name. She was his first thought after that intense training session—she always was.
"How are you?" he texted.
The response came quickly: "Not too good really."
Letzier's jaw tightened, worry settling in his chest. He knew what those words meant—she was probably in the garden again, surrounded by the flowers she and Zara had planted together. These were the days he hated being stuck at Space School, when all he wanted was to be there for her.
"Want me to come over after class? We could grab something to eat, or just talk." He added a heart emoji—something he'd never done before Daisy, but now it felt natural.
While waiting for her response, he leaned against the hallway wall, running a hand through his hair. Sometimes it felt like he was being pulled in two directions—the need to find answers about Zara's disappearance, and the desire to be there for Daisy every moment she needed him. The weight of both responsibilities pressed heavily on his shoulders.
His phone buzzed again. "Please. Dad's been hovering all morning. Could use a rescue."
A small smile crossed his face. Even on her bad days, she still had that spark of humor. "Consider it done. Two more classes and I'm all yours."
He tucked his phone away, straightening his uniform. He remembered the first day he met Daisy…it still feels like it was yesterday.
He had just completed lesson 101 of survival training, and it was time to focus on practice. As he was about to leave, he spotted Zara talking with Zeb and a girl. He stopped, assessing the situation. Zara waved him over, and without hesitation, he approached.
Zeb acknowledged him with a slight nod, but his attention remained on the women. The girl looked up at him with her short, dark brown hair and hazel eyes, prompting him to smile.
Zara smirked confidently and introduced her, saying, “This is Daisy.”
Letzier gave his hand out, “I’m Letzier,” she gave her hand, and he held it for a while. didn't want to let go.
She smiled. “Aren't you busy?”
He swallowed. “Right.”
He'd find Zara—for both of them. But right now, Daisy needed him, and that was all that mattered.
Chapter 3
**Flora**
Flora stepped into the mechanics lab 45, her eyes adjusting to the cooler lighting and metallic surfaces. It was her first time here, and everything felt foreign—screens emitted a soft hum, wires trailed across the floor, and a faint scent of ozone lingered in the air.
Alfred was already seated near the front, focused on his interface. He didn’t look up.
At the center of the room, a containment orb hovered in a magnetic field. It pulsed with a soft blue light—steady, rhythmic, almost calming.
Flora paused, watching it flicker.
She’d never seen anything like it before. But something about it felt… familiar. Not in memory, but in feeling. Like she’d overheard someone mention it once—Quantum Glow, wasn’t that what they called it?
She didn’t know what it meant. She didn’t even know if it was important. But the way the light moved—it caught her attention.
Miss Rylin turned from the board and noticed her lingering presence.
“You must be Flora,” she said, smiling. “Welcome to Mechanics. Everyone, this is her first day—let’s make her feel at home.”
Flora nodded, cheeks warm. “Thank you.”
She took her seat near the back, trying to focus as the lesson began. The orb continued to pulse, unnoticed by most. But Flora glanced at it again, once.
She didn’t understand it. But she saw it. After finishing Mechanics 45, Flora hurried to her next class, Survival 101. She settled into her seat, eager and focused, as the instructor began to outline critical survival skills. Every explanation captivated her, and she focused on her notes, believing that each detail could be crucial for the future. Flora was determined to soak up all the knowledge she could. Class Survival 101—her final class of the day, before she could finally go home. The shift felt strange, like stepping into a quieter chapter, where even the air seemed to hold its breath. She tried to ignore Nalie, seated just a few rows away. The tension simmered, but Flora kept her focus locked on the lesson. Then the bell rang. Class was over. Then—bam.
Someone bumped her hard, sending her notebook skidding across the floor. Flora blinked, startled. Nalie. “Watch it,” Nalie muttered, barely glancing back. Before Flora could respond, another figure stepped forward—tall, sharp-eyed, and unfamiliar. Blond hair and hazel eyes. Without hesitation, he moved. A swift kick to Nalie’s leg sent her stumbling to the ground. Flora, who was still on the floor, blinked, stunned. She hadn’t expected anyone to step in—let alone with such force.
“Try that again, and you’ll regret it.” He said.
Flora froze, unsure whether to speak or run. She didn’t recognize him, but since Alfred was standing beside him, she assumed that Alfred must know him. Alfred turned towards her, calm and steady. “Flora,” Alfred said, his voice soft as he stepped forward.
"You okay?”
She nodded with hesitation, her eyes flicking between the two boys. "Yeah…" The boy glanced at her, then at Alfred. “She's with you?” Alfred nodded. “She’s Zara’s sister.”
The boy's expression shifted—something like recognition flickered in his eyes. He gave a firm nod. “I’m Letzier,” he said.
Flora wasn’t sure how to respond, her eyes wide in disbelief. The words eluded her, a frantic clawing at her thoughts. Alfred smiled, as if reading her mind, he bent down, starting to pick up the papers that she had dropped., Letzier followed suit. Flora felt her shoulders ease for a bit. “Thank you,” She murmured.
Alfred nodded, “No problem.”
Flora grabbed the last Paper.


“I need to get home,” Flora said in a low voice. Alfred nodded. “I’ll walk you there...”
Just the n another figure approached—blue eyes, hazel hair, calm presence. “Is she alright?” he asked, his gaze steady. Alfred nodded. “She is. Thanks, Azreal.”
Azreal offered a warm smile. “Nice to see you, Flora. I’d stay and chat, but I’ve got a lot on my plate—chores, Bible class, the usual.”
He gave a small wave and turned to go, already moving with purpose.
Flora felt her fingers numb, cold, her breath sharp. The random feeling felt random. She closed her eyes and breathed.
Tears threatened to fall. She wanted to get home. That's all she wanted. Alfred noticed her trembling, “Are you sure you're okay?”
He asked in a gentle tone. Flora only nodded. She held her hand up. “It's okay, I can go by myself. Nathan will be outside waiting for me.”
Alfred nodded. “As you wish.” She walked the halls with her head low, the hum of voices fading behind her. Her prayer was silent, but urgent—Lord, give me peace. She started to sing as it had always calmed her down, when the fear gripped her like this.


**Nathan**
Nathan stood outside the school building, the cool air swirling around him, but it did little to refresh his heavy heart. Colten’s machinery class had left his mind buzzing—reactor systems, override protocols, emergency drills. It was all useful, but none of it touched the ache in his chest.
Zara had promised they would find his sister together. Now that she was gone, the silence she left behind was deafening.
Nathan took a deep breath, feeling the weight of his long-lost sister, Reanna, pressing down on him. She couldn’t just vanish; he had already lost his parents—losing his sister, too, was simply unacceptable.
Nathan sat hunched on the stone steps, elbows on his knees, staring at the ground as if the answers might be carved into the dust. The night pressed close around him, heavy and silent, broken only by the faint rustle of leaves in the wind.
A light tap on his shoulder startled him. He turned, and there was Zara, her face half-lit by the lantern glow. “You alright, cousin?” she asked softly.
His throat tightened. “No, I’m not alright,” Nathan said, the words sharper than he intended.
Zara didn’t flinch. She lowered herself beside him, smoothing her skirt as she sat. “It’s about Reanna, isn’t it?”
Nathan’s jaw worked as he nodded. “She’s still out there. I can feel it.” His voice cracked on the last word, and he hated how fragile it sounded.
For a moment, Zara’s eyes shimmered with her own unspoken fear. Then she drew in a steadying breath and met his gaze with quiet fire. “I believe that too. We will find her—together. It might not happen today, but it will happen.”
The conviction in her tone cut through the fog of despair that had been suffocating him. Nathan blinked, surprised by the sudden warmth in his chest. Hope—small, stubborn, but real—stirred.


He leaned against the railing, watching the students pass by. Then he saw Flora. She stepped out of the building, her red hair catching the light, her steps quick but thoughtful. When her eyes found his, she smiled, but she looked tense.
Nathan straightened and asked, “How was class?”
As he spoke, her shoulders relaxed slightly. She was indeed shy, and he hoped she might be comfortable around the people Zara loved. However, that thought seemed to fade away. Flora rolled her eyes playfully. “Alive. Survival training felt like we were prepping for a crash landing tomorrow.”
Nathan chuckled. “Colten had me in the control room. Reactor shutdown drills. He kept saying, ‘If you hesitate, you die.’ Real motivational.”
Flora laughed softly. “Sounds like him.”
Nathan nodded. “Saw you with Alfred earlier. What do you think of him?”
Flora hesitated, then shrugged. “He’s quiet. Protective. I think he’s very observant when it looks like he's not.”
Nathan smirked. “That’s Alfred.”
They stood together for a moment, the breeze brushing past them. The moment felt normal—almost peaceful. But Nathan could feel the weight behind it. Flora’s smile didn’t reach her eyes. His own thoughts kept circling back to Zara.
“She would have loved the survival class,” Flora said suddenly, her voice softer. Nathan nodded. “She would have aced it and then come to help us if we struggled,” he said. Flora smiled, but it faded quickly.
“Something happened.”
Nathan turned toward her. “What do you mean?”
She looked down at her hands. “Nalie was in my class. She bumped me—hard. Knocked my notebook out of my hands.”
Nathan’s jaw tightened. “Did she say anything?”
“Just ‘watch it,’ like it was my fault.” Flora’s voice was quiet, but steady.
Nathan felt heat rise in his chest. “Did anyone see?”
Flora nodded.
“He didn’t say anything right away,” Flora continued.
Nathan stared at her, trying to read the emotion behind her words. “Are you okay?”
Flora shrugged.
“I’m alright, I didn't expect this to happen on my first day.” Flora hugged herself, but then she looked up.
"I hear it's worth it. The progress and the pain of studying lead you to what you love doing. If God has called you, shouldn't you pursue it?"


Nathan nodded and pondered the idea. Zara, Zeb, and even he shared a passion for the stars and space, all wanting to explore them.
"Running towards the call sounds about right, to explore what God created," he replied.
They both stood in silence, and he could sense that Flora was feeling more at ease, which was a good thing. Just then, Dan walked toward them, his face lit with a full smile.
“Hi Nathan, Flora. It’s nice to see you again.”
Nathan nodded.
“Hi Dan. We’re just waiting for Zeb, but we can't talk while we wait.”


Flora looked at him, stared. “You okay, Dan?”
Dan nodded. “Yeah, why?”
Flora shook her head. “Nothing. You seem pale, that’s all.”
Dan smiled. “I’m just hungry. Can’t wait for Dad to pick us up,” he said.
Nathan paused. Did he say… ‘us’?
Flora apparently heard it too. “What do you mean, ‘us’?”
She asked.
Dan winced. “I have a brother here, too.”
Nathan’s mind trailed off. When did he ever mention having a brother? He couldn’t recall a single time. Not once.
Then it hit him. Nathan staggered back. It couldn’t be… Could it?


Chapter 4
**Flora**
Flora stood beside Nathan, watching his face drain of color. His breath hitched, and his shoulders stiffened like he’d just been struck.
Then the man walked up.
Tall. Sharp-eyed. Smirking like he owned the ground he stepped on.
“Sup, brother,” he said casually.
Flora blinked, her gaze flicking to Nathan. He didn’t answer. Didn’t move. Just stared—like the world had tilted sideways.
The man—Stone, she realized—stood there with the kind of confidence that made her skin crawl. Not loud. Not aggressive. Just… wrong.
Dan stepped forward, awkward now. “This is my brother,” he said, voice quieter than before.
Flora’s breath caught. Stone.
Zara had told her about him—late-night talks, whispered confessions. She’d said he threatened a kid with a gun and then blamed it on her sister. Flora remembered the way Zara’s voice would shake, how tears would slip down her cheeks when she thought no one was looking.
Flora had listened. Had cried with her. And now, standing here, she clenched her fists. Zara was gone, and there was nothing Flora could do. Oh, she prayed Zeb would be here soon.
Her heart sank. Brother? That’s what Dan meant earlier. That’s why Nathan had staggered back.
Nathan finally spoke, voice low and tight. “You never told me.”
Dan looked down. “I didn’t think it mattered.”
Flora glanced between them. The air was growing heavier by the second. Nathan’s silence wasn’t just shock—it was betrayal. The kind that settled deep and didn’t let go.
And Stone? He just stood there. Watching. Waiting. Like he knew exactly what he was doing.
And just then, Flora heard footsteps. Letzier and Alfred, as if they were brothers, were like they had been with Nalie.
Alfred gazed at her, as if he saw straight through, as if he knew. “Were they bothering you?”
Flora grudgingly nodded. Alfred gazes at Letzier. He shook his head. Letzier Spoke, “Brother or not, Dan, you shouldn't be hanging out with him.”
Stone huffed, “All because I messed with a kid.”
Alfred growled, voice low and sharp. “Then, blaming it on Zara. I don’t care—she’s gone now, and it’s your fault she’s gone.”
Flora looked up in surprise. He killed her?
Alfred didn’t look at her. His gaze was locked on Stone—forceful, deadly—the kind of look that could cut through steel. Flora staggered back, her breath catching.
Stone’s smirk faltered. “Alfred, I didn’t kill her. What proof do you have?”
Alfred stepped forward, fists clenched, his body taut with rage.
Letzier raised a hand, calm but firm. “He’s just a waste of time.”
Flora turned, heart pounding, and spotted Zeb walking toward them. Relief surged through her chest.
She mouthed the words: Help me. Please.
Zeb’s eyes instantly scanned the scene—Alfred’s stance, Stone’s presence, Letzier’s tension, Flora’s fear. Nathan's pale expression. He stepped between them like a wall.
“Okay,” Zeb said, voice steady and commanding. “Everyone, back off. This isn’t the time, and it’s definitely not the place.”
Alfred didn’t move at first. His fists stayed clenched. But Zeb’s presence was grounding—like gravity itself had stepped in.
Stone scoffed but didn’t speak.
Letzier lowered his hand, eyes still locked on Stone.
Flora exhaled, her shoulders trembling. Nathan stepped closer to her, silent but protective.
Zeb turned to Flora gently. “You alright?”
She nodded, barely.
Zeb looked at the others. “Dinner’s waiting. Let’s not ruin it with bloodshed.”
They nodded firmly. Alfred’s steely gaze stayed locked on Dan and Stone as the two marched away. Zeb stood resolutely, his silence hinting that he’d encountered this kind of tension before.
After a beat, Zeb spoke. “How about you and Letzier come to my place tonight?”
Alfred looked up and nodded, taking a moment to gather his thoughts. “That sounds great. I’ll inform my grandma.”
Zeb smiled and turned to Letzier for his input. “Are you okay with that, Letzier?”
Letzier nodded in agreement. “Absolutely. Would it be alright if Daisy joins us? I promised her I would pick her up earlier.”
Zeb took a deep breath. “If she’s interested, then that’s fine,” he responded, although his voice quivered slightly.
Flora noticed the change in Zeb’s expression. It seemed that mentioning Daisy made him a bit uncomfortable. She considered asking about it, but ultimately decided it might be best to let it be for now.
As they piled into Zeb’s hover van, Letzier paused before climbing into the front seat. Nathan was already in the back, and Alfred and Flora were settling into the middle.
“We need to pick up Daisy. Alfred, switch with me?”
Alfred raised an eyebrow but shrugged, sliding into the front. “Flora, would you mind…?” Letzier gestured to the back seat beside Nathan.
Flora smiled, catching on, and climbed into the back. Nathan met her gaze—confused at first, then quietly amused. The shift in seating hadn’t gone unnoticed.
“Thanks for driving, Zeb,” Letzier said, trying to sound casual as he fumbled with his seatbelt.
“No problem,” Zeb replied. “It’s been a while since we all hung out. Ever since…” His sigh said the rest.
Silence settled over the van. Nathan glanced around. Without Zara, the space felt hollow.
“I want to find her,” Letzier said suddenly. “Something in me—”
Zeb cut in with a sharp sigh. “You know how I feel about it.”
Letzier turned toward him, but Zeb didn’t look back.
“Let’s just say I don’t have that feeling,” Zeb said flatly. “She’s dead.”
**Zeb**
Everyone stepped inside the house, the heavy silence a stark reminder of Zara's absence. The atmosphere was thick with grief; it simply wasn't the same without her presence. Overwhelmed, he needed to escape the weight of it for a moment. He strode over to Zara's sister, Flora, and decisively told her to make dinner.
"You mean you haven't made anything yet?" Flora shot back, a hint of amusement cutting through the heaviness.
"Just order pizza if that's the case, Nathan can help you if you're too nervous," He said, with an inquisitive look.
“I’d prefer that," she stated firmly. Zeb smiled. Flora’s Favret, Pizza, he should call her that one day.
With that, he stepped outside into the fresh air, seeking relief from the sorrow that hung inside. Daisy was here, and that overwhelmed him.
Zeb leaned against the railing of the observation deck, staring out into the vast expanse of space. The memory of Zara filled his mind, taking him back to a moment they had shared.
It was a tranquil evening, the air crisp and cool, as the sun dipped below the horizon, casting hues of orange and purple across the sky. From their vantage point on a lush, green hill, Zara and Zeb quietly observed the ship below, it's silhouette stark against the fading light. Zara had cleverly managed to steal them away from their mundane duties for this brief interlude of serenity—a treasured escape from the bustle of their everyday lives.
As they stood side by side, the blanket of stars began to emerge, twinkling like distant diamonds scattered across the vast expanse of the universe. Each star pulsed with its light, a reminder of the beauty that lay beyond their small world.
"Do you ever wonder what it's like beyond the stars?" Zara asked, her voice soft and filled with wonder as if she could almost reach out to touch the shimmering cosmos above.
Zeb turned to her, a gentle smile spreading across his face as he wrapped his arm around her shoulders, pulling her close. "All the time. But I know we’ll explore it together someday," he replied, his tone warm and reassuring.
Zara looked up at the sky, her eyes reflecting the twinkling stars. "God's creation is so vast and beautiful. I trust in His plan for me," she said, her voice filled with faith and serenity, though she had doubt. Zeb looked into her eyes and knew she was feeling the loss of her Father, and then the Cruelness Stone's behavior tore her.
“Zara, whatever it is that's bothering you, you know I will protect you,” Zeb said, his voice filled with concern.
Zara shook her head gently, her eyes reflecting the light of the stars above. “Not you, Zeb. God will protect me,” she replied, her voice steady, and still, she had doubt.
Zeb nodded, a small smile forming on his lips. “I am not afraid, Zeb. Stone is merely human,” she continued, her tone unwavering.
Zeb's brow furrowed with worry. “There's more, isn't there? It's not just Stone?” he asked, his voice soft and searching.
Zara glanced back up at the heavens, her eyes filled with a mix of determination and serenity.
"Do you ever wonder what lies beyond the stars?" Zara asked again, her voice barely above a whisper.
Her gaze was fixed on the heavens. Zeb sighed, knowing full we'll she was avoiding the question. "All the time. But I trust that one day, we'll discover it together, guided by God's hand."


“I'm glad God has brought us together, Zara,” he said, a whisper in the ear. “Me too,” she said to him, and he felt his heart flutter.
In that moment, surrounded by the beauty of the night sky, Zeb felt a profound connection to Zara—a love that bound them together amidst the vastness of space.
The memory of that evening remained etched in his heart, a reminder of their bond and the hope that lay ahead.
The memory faded, and Zeb found himself back on the observation deck. The stars pierced the night sky, each one a silent witness to Zeb's turmoil. He stood on the balcony, letting the cool air wash over him as memories of Zara flooded back. These same stars used to look different when she was here—warmer somehow, more alive. Now they felt distant, cold, and accusing.
His fingers curled into fists as the weight of his earlier denials pressed down on him. How many times had he insisted she was gone? But Letzier's conviction, his stubborn refusal to give up... maybe there was something there. The official report said everything was fine, but those words rang hollow now.


Something had to have happened—something they weren't being told.
Taking one last look at the unforgiving stars, Zeb turned from the balcony. His footsteps echoed through the quiet house as he searched for Letzier, his mind already forming plans he'd never thought he'd make. Daisy sat near the corner, her head down, and Zebs heart ached. Why did Zara leave? Why did he let her on that spaceship? He walked towards Letzier, and he was talking to Alfred. And notice him looking back at Daisy.
"Letzier, we need to talk."
Letzier looked up, catching something different in Zeb's tone. He nodded slowly, following as Zeb led the way to his room. Alfred appeared in the doorway behind them, and Zeb felt a flicker of gratitude.
Determination might be exactly what they needed.
Once inside, Letzier broke the tension. "What is it?"
Zeb took a deep breath, knowing these words would change everything. "You're right," he admitted.
"We do need to find Zara." He said.
Letzier nodded.
"I hope you would see things my way. Have an idea, but I need to ask for help from an old friend. Let's go to a different room, where we can't talk."


**Reanna**
She observed them as they enjoyed their meal, a deep longing swelling within her to join in their laughter and camaraderie. However, her mission was critical—too important to overlook. She relied on Sileth to hack into their system, giving her the chance to listen in and delay the BNA, ensuring they couldn't intercept any communications. Though instructed to feed them false information, she was determined to make it seem authentic. For now, she needed to maintain her role as an observer.


As they chatted, Reanna held her ground for several minutes, hoping they'd utter a specific name—but it never came. She quickly messaged the BNA and Colten, stating firmly, “This is a waste of time; I’m leaving.” Yet, before turning away, she glanced through the window one last time, her longing intensifying.

Chapter 5


**Nathan**
They all gathered around as Daisy called out, “Pizza is here!” The delicious aroma of freshly baked crust and melted cheese filled the room, drawing smiles from every corner.

Nathan wasn’t the only one who noticed. The others exchanged subtle glances, their expressions tinged with concern. Some things hadn’t changed since Zara left.
But the longer Daisy stood there, the more her shoulders relaxed. Her eyes softened. The tension began to melt.
Nathan smiled and replied, “Yes, sir!”
Suddenly, the atmosphere shifted. Laughter bubbled up. Smiles spread. The sound of plates clinking and lighthearted chatter filled the room with warmth.
As the pizza was passed around, Flora playfully tossed a slice toward Nathan. He caught it with a grin.
“Nice catch!” she teased, her eyes sparkling with mischief.
He couldn’t help but smile. Flora was finally letting go—comfortable enough to toss pizza without worrying what anyone thought. Nathan saw Alfred notice, too. Not just Flora, but Daisy. She gave a small, genuine smile.
Zeb joined in, making exaggerated faces as he served slices, causing bursts of laughter to ripple through the room.
Stories and jokes followed, each one more ridiculous than the last. Nathan leaned back and shared a memory from school that had Flora laughing so hard she nearly fell off her chair.
“I can’t believe that happened!” she gasped.
Nathan chuckled. “Back in first or second grade—can’t remember which—I used to follow these kids around during recess. One day, we found a smashed watermelon on the playground.”
He paused, suppressing a laugh.
“Suddenly, all the kids started screaming, ‘It’s a DEAD HUMAN!’ Like they’d stumbled onto a crime scene.”
The room erupted.
“I kept saying, ‘It’s a watermelon!’ But they were convinced it was something sinister. They even dragged the teacher over, who came running like it was a real emergency.”
He shook his head, still laughing. “I must’ve been four or five. It was ridiculous—but at the time, it felt like the biggest mystery of my life.”
Everyone was in stitches, wiping away tears of laughter. The joy was contagious. One by one, they shared their own stories, their voices rising like music.
It was a much-needed reprieve from everything they’d been carrying.
Eventually, the laughter faded into soft conversation. Plates were cleared. Daisy quietly helped Zeb tidy up. Letzier and Alfred wore wide grins, their eyes brighter than they’d been in days.
Then Colten stepped in, gently picking up Flora and guiding her out with a quiet smile.
And for a moment, Nathan thought—maybe healing didn’t come all at once. Maybe it came in pizza, laughter, and stories shared between friends.
FloraFlora stood at the edge of the school courtyard, the morning light casting long shadows across the pavement. Her fingers gripped the strap of her bag, knuckles pale. It was only her second day, but the building already felt like a maze of expectations—hallways she hadn’t memorized, faces she hadn’t learned, and memories she hadn’t made.
She took a breath. The air was cooler today. Still, her chest felt tight.
Lord, walk with me, she whispered inwardly. I don’t want to be brave. I just want to be steady.
She stepped inside.
The halls buzzed with quiet energy—students chatting, lockers clanking, the low hum of announcements overhead. Flora moved carefully, trying not to look lost. She remembered Julie’s help yesterday, the warmth in her voice, the way she’d made the school feel less like a fortress.
But Julie wasn’t here this morning.
Flora hesitated at a junction. She could text Alfred again. But something in her resisted. She wanted to find it herself. She wanted to prove she could.
**Room 1234.**
She turned left, then right, then paused. The hallway opened into a familiar corridor. Relief bloomed in her chest.
Miss Lucy greeted her with a smile as she entered. “Welcome back, Flora.”
Flora smiled softly. “It’s nice to see you again.”
She took her seat, brushing her fingers along the desk’s edge. It felt like a small ritual—like the desk remembered her, even if no one else did.
Class 1234 was gentle. Miss Lucy’s voice was calm, her lessons filled with facts about stars and planetary systems. But Flora’s mind wandered. She thought of Zara—how they used to dream together, sketching constellations and whispering about space missions that felt more like prayers than plans.
She missed her.
And yet, sitting here, Flora felt like she was honoring her. Every note she took, every question she asked—it was for both of them.
The bell rang.
Mechanics was next.
She walked slowly to the lab, her steps heavier. The room was colder, filled with metal and math and the quiet hum of machines. Alfred was already there, adjusting a panel. He glanced up as she entered.
“Ready for Class 45?” he asked. Flora nodded. “I think so.”
He smiled faintly. “You’ll be fine.”
She took her seat, eyes drifting to the orb at the center of the room. The Quantum Glow shimmered faintly, pulsing in soft blue waves. It wasn’t just light—it was rhythm. Pattern. Something alive.
She remembered what her teacher had said yesterday. That she’d noticed something no one else had.
She hadn’t meant to.
She just saw it.
Miss Rylin entered, her gaze sweeping the room.
“Good. Let’s begin.”
Flora’s fingers curled around her desk again. She didn’t know why she did that. Maybe it was grounding. Maybe it was prayer.
Rylin turned to the class. “Yesterday, Flora noticed something most of you missed. Where do you think Glow comes from?”
A hand rose. “Outer space?”
Rylin shook her head. “No. It came from a plant.”
Flora blinked. A plant? That didn’t make sense. She whispered, “God… explanation here?”
Rylin continued, “Eighteen years ago, a man discovered a plant with extraordinary properties. It could heal. Restore. Cure sickness. He refined it into a substance we now call Quantum Glow. It’s powerful enough to fuel an entire ship.”
Flora raised her hand. “How did the man know about the plant's power?”
Rylin hesitated. “I can’t go too deep into that. But I will say this—the plant no longer exists.”
He turned toward the orb, its glow steady and quiet.
Flora felt it—not in her mind, but in her spirit. A sorrow. A weight.
As if something sacred had been lost.
She didn’t hear words. But she understood.


**Letzier**
The school day unfolded like any other. Letzier stepped into the classroom just as the bell rang. Mrs. Hamilton stood at the front, substituting for Mr. Coltens. Her reputation preceded her—sharp voice, sharper expectations.
“Take your seats, everyone,” she said, and the room fell into order.
Letzier slid into his desk, eyes scanning the room. Alfred wasn’t here today—probably helping his grandma again. But Elora and Claire were, along with Dan, seated beside Nathan. A few unfamiliar faces dotted the back row.
Mrs. Hamilton began her lecture on advanced astrophysics, her voice sharp and unwavering. Equations filled the board. Letzier's thoughts began to drift to his girlfriend, Daisy, and he felt a deep longing to help her feel better and experience joy again. He also couldn't shake the persistent ache he felt when he thought about Zara. Perhaps she wasn't dead; she had to be out there, alive. Once he found her, he would return, and his girl would run into his arms, reunited with her long-lost friend.
As the lesson dragged on, a quiet resolve settled over him. He had to stay sharp. Stay focused. If he wanted answers, he needed to be ready.
When class ended, Letzier watched Dan slip out. Something about him had been off lately. He’d been hanging around Stone more and more. Letzier didn’t care that Stone was Dan’s brother—he didn’t trust him. Not after what happened.
Letzier followed, keeping his distance. He spotted Dan chatting with Nathan, laughing about video games and old tech mods.
Nathan’s
Nathan leaned against the lockers, chatting casually with Dan. “Hey, Dan,” he said teasingly. “It’s been a while. Want to come over later? We could watch *The Last Survivor.”
Dan shook his head. “Nah, I’ve got homework. Maybe next week.”
Nathan felt his heart sink. “Your brother, I’m guessing,” he said, disappointment evident in his voice. Stone had hurt Zara, but surely he wouldn’t let Stone control Dan.
Dan looked at Nathan. “I’m not going out with Stone, I’m just…”
Just then, Letzier approached.
“Hey, Dan. Hey, Nathan,” he greeted them.
They both responded in unison. Letzier’s tone shifted. “Dan… what did you think about Zara and the crash? I heard she saw you as a brother.”
Nathan blinked. The question came out of nowhere. He glanced at Letzier—his eyes were locked on Dan, intense. Almost like Alfred’s when he was angry. Almost.
Dan checked his watch and winced.
Letzier didn’t usually look like that. Not unless something was wrong. Nathan’s thoughts raced. Was it because Dan had been hanging out with Stone?
Dan cleared his throat. “Yeah… she meant a lot to me. See you, Nathan.”
He turned and walked off quickly.
Nathan looked at Letzier, confused. “Is something wrong with him? Or is it just me?”
Letzier sighed. “It’s just you. Stay here, Nathan.”
He didn’t wait for a reply. His eyes were already following Dan. And Nathan couldn’t shake the feeling—something was about to go wrong.
**Letzier**
Letzier blended into the shadows next to the school, mimicking Dan’s movements with careful precision. Crouched behind a sleek metal structure in the courtyard of Space School, tension coiled inside him like a spring. Out of nowhere, sharp whispers sliced through the cool evening air—Dan’s voice unmistakably among them—prompting him to freeze behind a dense bush.
"I can't believe Zara cared for me. Stupid girl." Dan's voice dripped with contempt. Letzier's jaw tightened; he wasn't sure why, but Dan's words felt forced, and they stung deeply—this was the same Dan Zara he had once called brother.
Letzier's jaw tightened even more as he heard Stone.
Stone's voice sliced through the air, sharp and merciless, leaving a chill in it's wake. "Should've known to keep her mouth shut. Maybe then she wouldn't have gotten hurt." His cruel chuckle echoed like a twisted melody, igniting a firestorm of anger and despair within Letzier.
He felt his nails digging painfully into his skin, grounding himself against the whirlwind of emotions tearing him apart. Alfred had seen it clearly all along; he had warned them. Then a third voice, one Letzier didn't recognize, cold and precise, "She's still alive. Stranded on an unknown planet. No one will help her."
Alive. The word exploded in Letzier's mind like a supernova.
"She should have been out of the picture," Stone growled, frustration evident in his voice. "Not everyone in the government agrees with our motives," Dan had said.
The unknown voice spoke again: "I overheard that they're going to finish the job."
Letzier felt the air thick with uncertainty. The weight of that revelation pressed down on him. As the last remnants of the group—Dan and the two others—drifted away, their voices fading into the distance, he took a steadying breath. Only Stone remained, leaning against the wall, his posture relaxed but an air of indifference masking the gravity of the situation. Letzier stepped forward, determination pushing him past the hesitation that gripped him. “Stone,” he said, his voice flat and measured, hiding the storm that churned within him.
“We need to talk.”
Stone's smirk appeared beneath his cap. "Do we now? About what?"
Letzier stepped closer. "Cut the act. I heard you. What do you know about the crash?"
"I don't know what you're talking about," Stone replied, but his hesitation betrayed him.
Stone chuckled darkly. "Oh, Zara? She was... ambitious. Too ambitious, maybe. Thought she could fix the world. But not every puzzle is meant to be solved."
"Stop talking in riddles," Letzier demanded, fists clenched. "If you had anything to do with what happened to her—"
"Me?" Stone's laugh held no humor. "You think I'm the one who caused her to crash? Come on, soldier boy. Open your eyes. Zara wasn't the target. She was just... collateral damage."
Something's napped. Letzier grabbed Stone's collar, slamming him against the wall. "Tell me what you know!"
Stone didn't resist. Instead, he tilted his head, voice dropping to a whisper. "You might be quick with your fists, but terrible at figuring things out, Letzier. If you want answers, maybe you should ask your precious government. They're the ones with the real secrets."
Stone's grin widened. "Like I told Alfred... I wasn't the one who did it. You might want to thank my brother for that."
Letzier's fist crashed into the wall beside Stone's head, cracking the concrete. Stone's smirk flickered—just for a moment.
Then Letzier felt it. Eyes watching. A presence in the shadows.
The students' approach broke the tension. Stone pushed away from the wall, disappearing into the crowd. His final words floated back: "You're wasting time chasing a ghost. But hey, good luck finding her. You'll need it."
His laughter echoed long after he vanished, leaving Letzier standing there, fists clenched, mind racing, and the shadows of doubt creeping in.
Nova, he needed to find her and fast.
Chapter 6
**Flora**
Flora sat quietly, her heart heavy, as Zeb parked the hovercar in the lot outside the gleaming Observation Dome. Inside, the dome promised breathtaking views of the universe, projected so vividly that it felt like stepping into space itself. But even the beauty of the stars couldn’t eclipse the ache in her heart; she needed Amika now more than ever. Yes, we're here!" Alfred said as he got out of Zeb's van. Zeb shrugged. “I don’t know.”

Alfred's
Flora claimed she had seen Letzier, and Alfred was determined to uncover the truth. He couldn't disregard her intuition—he knew better than that. Letzier's
Letzier wanted to join, but he wanted to see the newer model of the spaceship. He had an idea but would need help, and he knew now wasn't the time to ask them yet. Plus, he liked watching them from afar. He thought it was amusing to have Flora shout his name. It was ridiculous, but it got his friends' attention, and he would believe her; Alfred wouldn't call Zara's sister crazy. No, he was too much of a gentleman to do that. But it worked. And they would probably see each other again after dawn or maybe longer, and he still needed to find Nova. It bothered him that he couldn't find her. He left the building after Alfred saw him. Letzier knew he was too good at his job of camouflaging. After all, he was working in the space military. He shook his head. He needed to talk to Daisy.

He stood at Daisy’s doorstep, heart steady but mind racing. White shirt, blue jeans, her favorite flowers in one hand, the long-awaited book in the other. Blasts Off — the twentieth in the series. He knew what it meant to her.

Stars were already beginning to show in the sky, like they’d been waiting for this reunion.

Chapter 7
**Letzier**
Letzier sat quietly, his fingers laced with Daisy’s, the warmth of her hand grounding him. To anyone else, he probably looked composed. But inside, his mind was a storm. Confusion. Pressure. The weight of everything they’d uncovered was pressing down on him.
Nova paced the room like a caged animal, her shoulders tense, her eyes sharp. He could tell she was holding something back—something heavy. The room felt too large for just the three of them, yet somehow too small for the truth that was about to surface.
Finally, Nova stopped. Her gaze locked onto him.
“You needed me?” she asked, voice clipped.
Letzier nodded. That was all she needed. Without another word, she turned and strode toward a stack of boxes.
He watched her move, remembering the first time they met—her steady grip on that weapon, the fire in her eyes. Nova had always felt like someone who didn’t belong in their world. Too sharp. Too fast. Too… other.
Daisy’s grip tightened slightly. He glanced at her, saw the flicker of memory in her eyes. She was remembering it too—the coin Nova carried, the way it glowed blue before teleporting them. That nauseating lurch in his stomach. He hadn’t forgotten.

Letzier snapped back to the moment.
Nova turned toward us, her purple hair catching the glow of the rising table. “I’m an expert hacker,” she said, a flicker of pride in her voice. “I used to go to Space School—just like you—until I quit. After Zara’s crash…”
Her voice faltered. I felt a sharp ache in my chest.
She looked down, then continued, softer now. “I started digging into what really happened… Apparently, Zara is Alive, she just….stranded. And as much as I want,” She breathed. She took a step back, not looking in their eyes.
I saw Daisy flinch beside him the moment she said that Zara was alive. It was always the same—every person we met seemed to carry a piece of Zara’s story. A memory. A moment. But no one had the full picture. It was like chasing fragments of a shattered truth, scattered across time and people.
And somehow, he knew they were getting closer.
Nova’s voice dropped. “You can’t trust anyone. No one can hear about this.” Her eyes locked with Daisy’s. “Promise me.”
Letzier leaned forward. “Nova, you realize—”
She cut him off with a raised hand. “I know.”
He didn’t like being silenced, but he let it go. For now.
“Zara’s out there,” he said, voice low. “Alone. On some planet. Alive. The government isn’t doing what it should. And how many others like her have been betrayed?”
The room went still.
Daisy whispered, “Alive?”
Letzier turned to her, squeezed her hand. “Yes. Alive. But betrayed.”
He looked back at Nova. With questions.
“Who is the BNA? You still haven’t explained.”
Nova’s face darkened. “The BNA is a manipulative operation—murderers who’ve infiltrated everything. Government. White House. They’ve planted spies everywhere. Even close to the president.”
She started pacing again, her words speeding up. “They’re growing stronger every day. And that’s what terrifies me.”
Letzier stepped closer. “How do we stop them?”
Nova turned, her voice steady. “Find the WTB agency—We Talk Bible. It’s a faith organization.”
She hesitated. “The BNA let Zara fly that sabotaged ship. And Letzier—” her voice cracked when Nova's gaze landed on his. Daisy squeezed his hand. “—Please don’t go charging in. That look in your eyes… I saw the same one in Zara’s.”
He didn’t respond. She was right. That fire was already burning in him.
“I showed her this,” Nova continued. “Told her not to share. I tried everything.”
“But Dan—” Letzier said, the name sharp on his tongue.
Nova’s eyes filled with tears. “Zara told Dan. Of course she did. We all trusted him.”
Letzier felt his jaw tighten. He wanted answers.
“Through my hacking,” Nova said, “I’ll stay and find more of BNA’s weakness. They can’t handle the WTB. They’ve been fighting them for eight years.”
Nova straightened, her expression unreadable. “Go back to Space School,” she said. “There’s a file I need from the principal’s office. I’ll keep Daisy here. And find the WTB.”
Her voice sharpened. “Don’t tell anyone. Not yet.”
Letzier gave a slow nod. “Understood.”
But even as he said it, a dozen questions swirled in his mind. Nothing felt certain. Nothing felt safe.
He turned to leave—but Daisy reached out and grabbed his hand, holding it tight for a moment. Her grip said what her words didn’t: Be careful. There was something in her eyes—steady, calm, full of faith—that told him everything would be okay.
He looked back at Nova. He wanted to believe it.
He really did. But there was no turning back now. He was going in headfirst.
**Flora**
Flora paced near the window, her heart fluttering with anticipation. The late afternoon light spilled across the room in golden streaks, but she barely noticed. She hadn’t seen Amika in years, and the thought of reconnecting made her both nervous and excited. So much had changed. So much had been left unsaid.
The door creaked open.
Colten greeted Amika with a nod, his voice steady. “You made it.”
Flora turned, her breath catching. Amika stood in the doorway, her silhouette framed by the fading light. Her posture was sharp, her eyes scanning the room with practiced precision. She looked different—older, more composed—but it was her presence that struck Flora most. Controlled. Calculated.
“AMIKA!! You’re here!!” Flora cried, unable to hold back.
She rushed forward, arms wide, and embraced her friend tightly. Amika returned the hug, but Flora felt the tension in her shoulders, the way her body remained alert even in the embrace. For a moment, everything felt normal again—but only for a moment.
“Come in,” Flora said, beaming, trying to ignore the unease creeping in.
Amika’s smile was warm, but her eyes betrayed her. There was something beneath the surface—fear, maybe. Or something darker. Colten watched silently, his presence grounding them both, but Flora could tell he sensed it too.
They moved to the living room. Amika sat with her back to the wall, her bag never leaving her lap. Flora noticed the subtle bulge beneath her jacket. Not just a bag. Not just a visit.
“You look good,” Flora said gently. “Different, but good.”
Amika gave a small nod. “It’s been... complicated.”
Her gaze flicked to the window, then back to Flora.
Colten reappeared with tea, setting it down without a word. His eyes met Amika’s. Something passed between them—recognition, maybe. Or warning.
Flora leaned in. “Where have you been?”
Amika’s lips parted, but before she could answer, a faint buzz came from her bag. She silenced it quickly, her expression hardening.
“Let’s go upstairs…”
Flora glanced at Colten, who suddenly seemed distant—his usual fatherly warmth replaced by something unreadable. What was that all about?
Just then, a knock echoed through the room.
Nathan came downstairs, cheerful as he opened the door. “Hi, Dan.”
Flora turned to Amika, who had gone rigid. Her fists clenched. Flora didn’t understand everything, but she knew danger when she saw it. Heck, if it were Dan, then it's most likely.
Amika spoke suddenly, her voice calm but urgent. “Flora, do you remember where we buried that Bible?”
Flora blinked. “We buried a lot of things,” she said, half-laughing at the memory. It had always seemed ridiculous—two children imagining that a hundred years in the future, someone would remember who they were.
Amika’s tone softened, almost nostalgic. “We buried it beside the tree.”
Flora’s face lit up. “Oh yeah, I remember!”
Before she could say more, Amika grabbed her wrist and pulled her toward the back door. Flora didn’t resist. She felt the urgency in Amika’s grip.
They reached the backyard, the old tree standing tall like a sentinel. Flora ran inside briefly and returned with a shovel, handing it to Amika.
“I’m glad to see you, Amika,” Flora said softly.
Amika smiled, the first genuine one Flora had seen. “I remembered you, Flora—and all the fun we had together.”
Flora watched her dig, memories flooding back with each scoop of earth. When the chest surfaced, she felt a strange mix of nostalgia and dread. Something about Amika felt... off. Not wrong, but changed.
Amika opened the chest and pulled out the Bible, brushing dirt from it's cover. She handed it to Flora.
“Here. A reminder that God will forever be here—from the beginning to the end.”
Flora clutched the Bible tightly, her fingers pressing into the worn leather as if it could anchor her in the storm of uncertainty swirling inside her. Her thoughts drifted to Zara—her friend, her sister in spirit, the one who had vanished without a trace. The ache of not knowing had settled deep in her chest, a quiet grief she carried like a shadow.
She didn’t know the truth yet—that Zara was alive. But something in Amika’s eyes, something in the urgency of their escape, whispered that answers were close. Closer than they’d ever been.
The weight of the book in her hands felt heavier now, not just with memory, but with meaning. It had survived the years, buried beneath the tree they once played under, waiting to be unearthed.
Flora stared at the cover, her heart pounding. She could feel it—something was shifting. The past was no longer buried. The silence was cracking. And whatever lay ahead, she knew it would change everything.
She took a breath, steadying herself.
Chapter 8


Alfred's
The next day, Alfred woke to a beautiful morning, but his thoughts were clouded with worry. Letzier hadn’t answered his calls. Something was wrong.
He got ready quickly and headed downstairs. His grandma was in the kitchen, scrubbing the counters.
"Hey, Grandma," he said, kissing her head.
"Have you heard from your friend yet?"
"No. I’m going to check Colten’s house."
She nodded. "Wise idea. You go do that."
Alfred left, heading first to their childhood clubhouse. It was empty. Birds chirped, trees rustled, but no Letzier.
He turned toward Colten’s house, the streets unusually quiet. When he arrived, the door was slightly ajar.
He knocked. "Hello? Colten?"
No answer.
He stepped inside cautiously. "It’s Alfred. I’m looking for Letzier."
From the back room, Colten’s voice emerged. "He’s not here. Haven’t seen him since yesterday."
Alfred stepped closer to Colten. "Do you know where he went?"
Colten rubbed his eyes. "He said he needed space. He looked shaken. I thought he’d be with Daisy."
Alfred nodded. "Thanks. Let me know if you hear anything."
Once outside again, Alfred stared at his phone, still waiting for messages.
"Where are you, Letzier?" he whispered to himself.
Feeling disappointed, he began to walk away when something caught his eye. Up in a tree…he recognized the tree before, Zara, Letzier, and he would climb it.

His eyes scan the letter, his eyes re-reading it.
Letzier was trying to find Nova. He would have to pay a visit to Zeb.


**Zeb**
Zeb passed through the room, calculating his every move. His mind drifted—Zara had to be out there somewhere. He kept his pace steady, though her face haunted him like a mirage, hovering just beyond reach.
He replayed the moment before she left, again and again, questioning whether it had truly happened—or if someone had sabotaged the ship. Nova had disappeared soon after, leaving behind the spacecraft like something out of a movie: sleek, silent, and possibly their first test run... or a trap.
The thought hit Zeb like a punch to the chest. He slammed his fist into the wall.
“Aw, Ship Reck,” he muttered, biting back a curse. Pain radiated through his knuckles, but he sank onto the couch, shoulders heavy with doubt.
“Lord, what am I supposed to do?” he whispered. He knew he should trust Him. But would the Lord still accept him? After all, He was Zeb’s first love—before Zara, wasn’t He?
He closed his eyes and breathed a quiet prayer. “Lord, forgive me if I’ve strayed.”
A knock echoed through the room.
Zeb stood and opened the door. Alfred stood there, half-shadowed in the hallway light.
Zeb managed a smile. “Hey, Alfred. What’s going on?”
Alfred held out a folded letter. “Letzier needs our help.”
Zeb raised an eyebrow. “Help with what?”
Alfred’s lips curled into a knowing smile. “A small mission.”
Zeb crossed his arms. “And that would be...?”

Letzier needs your help—yours and Zeb’s. We have to take out the cameras in Space School. This is for Zara.
