**Flora**
After retrieving the 60-year-old Bible, they stepped inside. The sound of guitar strings filled the air. Colten sat in the corner, fingers moving effortlessly as he sang "Holy Are You Lord."
Both Flora and Amika smiled, caught in a wave of childhood memories. How many times had his voice brought her comfort? But the sweetness of the memory twisted as she thought of Zara, how she wished her sister were here; she would have loved this.
"Wow, Mr. Colten, you have such a beautiful voice, as always," Flora breathed, wonder dancing in her eyes.
Colten's fingers continued their dance across the strings as he transitioned into "Breathe, Oh Breath of God." The melody should have been peaceful, but something felt off. Dan was upstairs. And Amika seemed tense.
Yet Colten sang on, as if to say: God is here. There's nothing to fear.
The thought crept in anyway: What if they banned the Bible? What if everything went wrong? Her heart thundered against her ribs. Like China, so far back in history, a warning they'd ignored. But this time could be worse.
Would she stay strong? Would her faith hold? She didn't know, but hope flickered in her heart like a stubborn flame.
Dan came thundering down the stairs, footsteps echoing through the hall.
Colten didn’t flinch. He turned to Amika with a calm smile and made his announcement. “Amika, you’re having a sleepover.”
“A what?” Flora’s voice cracked with surprise.
Colten’s smile stayed gentle, but there was a knowing glint in his eyes as he looked to Amika. Her face lit up with excitement.
“Amika, you wouldn’t mind, would you?”
She grinned. “Not at all.”
**Alfred**
Alfred moved swiftly through the halls, his footsteps light, calculated. The fluorescent lights above flickered faintly, casting long shadows across the floor. He rounded the corner—and there he was.
The camera guard.
Stationed just outside the security room, arms crossed, half-alert. Alfred’s pulse quickened. He hoped Letzier was making progress. They didn’t have much time.
Behind him, Zeb appeared, quiet as a shadow.
Okay… here we go.
Alfred reached into his coat pocket and pulled out a small, folded cloth. It was soaked in a mild sedative—nothing dangerous, just enough to knock someone out for a few hours. He’d borrowed it from the infirmary. Technically.
From behind, Zeb’s voice came in a sharp whisper. “Where did you get that from?”
Alfred didn’t turn. “Don’t ask,” he murmured. “Just be ready.”
Zeb swallowed hard. “I thought you were the quiet one.”
“I am,” Alfred said, eyes locked on the guard. “But quiet doesn’t mean harmless.”
He stepped forward, cloth in hand, heart pounding.
One… two… three.
Alfred lunged, swift and silent. The cloth pressed against the guard’s face, and within seconds, the man slumped to the floor, unconscious.
Alfred crouched beside him, checking his pulse—steady. No harm done. Just enough to keep him out of the way.
He exhaled, tension draining from his shoulders. “Alright… Letzier is safe,” he whispered. “I hope.”
Zeb peeked around the corner, eyes wide. “You actually did it.”
Alfred nodded, already dragging the guard behind a stack of crates. “We’ve got maybe ten minutes before someone notices.”
Zeb swallowed. “What now?”
Alfred glanced toward the security room. “Now we make sure no one sees what Letzier finds. What he's looking for, the note didn't say much.
**Letzier**
Letzier moved swiftly through the corridors of Space School, his gaze alert, his nerves taut—but not afraid. Not yet. He reached the office. A glance left, then right. Clear.
He slipped inside, lock picks already in hand. The desk drawer clicked open. He was getting faster. Paperwork spilled out—forms, records, nothing useful. Until—
Stone’s words echoed in his mind. He needed answers.
Then he saw it: History of the Intelligent Serum. His breath caught. Fingers trembling, he grabbed it.
Another file: Extermination Protocols. Why would the school have this? He prayed Alfred had reached the cameras. The doorknob turned.
Letzier dove behind a cabinet, clutching the files to his chest. Breath held. Footsteps. Voices.
**Zeb.**
“Um, sir, I have a… a missing lady. Her name is Flora.”
“She should be outside,” the principal replied, voice clipped.
“She’s not there. Would you help me?” Zeb’s voice cracked. A pause. Then, “Let me call—”
“No, I mean… I’d rather you,” Zeb interrupted.
A sigh. Footsteps retreating. The door clicked shut.
Letzier exhaled, heart pounding. He scrambled out, files still in hand. He’d return them later—maybe. Right now, they needed answers. And fast.
He slipped into a nearby closet, shut the door behind him, and flicked on the dim overhead light.
He opened the Exsterminated Files.
His eyes glanced at it, but his heart stopped.
“What… no,” he whispered, eyes scanning the pages.
Names. Nathan. Zeb. Nova. Azreal, names he hadn't heard of, Amika. People who used to go here, he knew.
Then—his breath hitched.
**Daisy.**
His girlfriend.
Letzier clenched his teeth, fingers curling around the paper. Her name was listed under Phase Two strike down.
He felt the floor shift beneath him. This wasn’t just about secrets anymore. It was personal.
They were targeting people he cared about. People he loved.
But why?
Letzier pulled the intelligence file closer, his breath shallow. He flipped it open—and froze. His mouth dropped. He almost cursed, but didn’t.
The pages detailed the school’s origins, it's hidden purpose. A hunt. A history. A reason.
Colten’s name was there.
But that wasn’t what made his stomach twist.
He turned the page.
Alfred — exceptional auditory perception, uncanny ability to read people. Weakness: fear of losing those he loves.
Letzier clenched his jaw. That was true. Too true.
He kept reading.
Letzier — enhanced strength, above-average resilience. Weakness: emotional sensitivity to others’ pain. Anger intensifies under stress.
“That’s not fair,” he muttered. “Most people feel that way.”
But deep down, he knew his empathy wasn’t ordinary. It was a trigger. A weapon. Or a flaw.
Flora — quiet, analytical, always ten steps ahead. Cognitive scores: exceptional. Strategic instinct: high.
They were being studied.
Not taught. Not guided.
Observed. Measured. Cataloged.
By the school. By the teachers.
Letzier’s pulse quickened. Was Colten part of this? Had he known all along?
He scanned the rest of the file. More names. More profiles. Each one was dissected like a lab report.
Did they have powers? Was that what this was?
Abilities masked as personality traits. Weaknesses labeled as threats. Letzier closed the file, his hands trembling. This wasn’t education. It was surveillance.
He swiftly got out of the closet, moving with the shadows. Letzier felt anger raging through his veins; he wanted to stop whoever thought of this sick game.
He saw Nova as he handed her the file. She nodded. “Thank you, we need to move. We’ll get to my base.” Letzier nodded but didn’t say anything. “And Alfred?” Her voice was hard as she said, “Not yet.”
**Alfred**
The afternoon air felt fresh, but Alfred barely noticed. His thoughts were tangled, looping back to the mission with Letzier. They had taken out the cameras—clean, quiet—but something's still gnawed at him. Letzier had vanished again, and Alfred hadn’t heard a word since.


He sighed, scanning the street. He had seen Letzier briefly earlier, just a glimpse; it wasn’t enough to ease his worry. Maybe I’m overthinking, he told himself. But Colten’s house… he might know something.
Then, a movement caught his eye.
A man was up ahead. Alfred's breath caught in his throat. “Stone.”
The name slipped from his lips like poison, bristling with old hatred. That lunatic was heading straight for Colten’s house, his stride sharp and deliberate. Alfred's blood ran cold. He surged forward, every muscle tense for confrontation.
But then—another movement.
A woman stepped from the shadows, tapping Stone’s shoulder. Alfred slowed, confusion rippling through him. She wore a jean jacket, and her black hair fell past her shoulders. She leaned in close, whispering something in Stone’s ear. Alfred crept closer, careful not to draw attention. Fragments of their conversation drifted back to him. “Letzier… I know where Daisy is…” Her voice was low and controlled. Alfred couldn’t catch everything, but he heard enough.
Stone smiled, nodded, and walked away. Before the woman could follow, Alfred struck. She was stronger than she looked—he had to fight to restrain her. But before he could demand answers, she twisted free of his grip on her mouth.
“Really?” she said, her tone sharp with confidence. “You should’ve stayed behind, Alfred.”
He blinked, thrown off balance. “How do you know me?” She laughed softly.
“Where’s Letzier?” he demanded, tightening his grip.
“He’s safe. So is Daisy.” Her voice carried a warning. “But you should let me go before you get hurt, Brutal Alfred.”
Alfred growled. That name—he hadn’t heard it since Zara. His arms stayed locked around her, unmoved by the threat.
“Don’t call me that,” he snarled.
She smiled, unfazed. “Your glares don’t scare me, Brutal Alfred. But it was nice to meet you. Give Letzier my regards—and remember your promise to Zara.”
She leaned in, her voice dropping to a whisper.
**“Protect Flora.”**
Alfred’s breath caught. That name—Zara's sister. In that split second of surprise, she moved. Everything blurred. A flash of motion. A sharp impact. Then—darkness.
Chapter 9
**Alfred**
The world swam back into focus as Alfred turned his head, the dull throb in his skull pulsing with every heartbeat. A girl knelt beside him, dusty blonde hair catching the low light. But it was her eyes that stopped him—one blue, one brown. Too specific, too strange to be a dream.
“Who are—”
“Shh.” Her voice was sharp, edged with annoyance. “I’m Amika.”
Amika. Right. He was probably hallucinating. Attacked by a girl, rescued by another. Not exactly how he’d planned to spend his evening.
Then he heard it—his name, echoing down the hall.
**“Alfred?!”**
Flora’s voice rang out, and Alfred forced himself upright, ignoring the pounding in his head.
“Are you okay?” he asked, concern overriding discomfort.
Flora raised an eyebrow. “Alfred, I’m not the one who just got knocked out.”
Amika shook her head, tension flickering across her face. “Flora, I thought you went to bed.”
“I’m sixteen,” Flora replied, voice sharp. “Give me a break.”
Alfred gave a weak smile. “It’s okay,” he muttered, wincing.
Amika nodded, but her expression didn’t soften.
"Where’s Colten?” Alfred asked, voice low.
Amika’s face hardened. “He’s busy.”
Flora stepped closer, noticing the shift in Amika’s demeanor. “Amika, are you okay?”
She placed a hand on Amika’s shoulder, but Amika shrugged it off.
“I’m fine,” she said quickly, too quickly. “You haven’t been yourself since Dan came by.”
Dan. The name hit Alfred like a jolt. He remembered seeing Stone—Dan’s brother—lurking near Colten’s house. His jaw clenched.
He locked eyes with Amika.
“Amika,” he said, voice steady, “I don’t want to ask again. Where is Colten?”
Just then, Colten appeared through the corridor, a faint smile playing on his lips—too casual for the tension in the room.
“You good, Alfred?” he asked, voice light, almost teasing.
Alfred blinked at him, still seated, head pounding. “Define good,” he muttered, rubbing his temple.

Alfred narrowed his gaze. “You knew Stone was nearby. Didn’t you?”
Colten’s smile didn’t fade, but it didn’t reach his eyes either. “I know a lot of things.”
Alfred pushed himself up straighter, ignoring the ache in his skull. “Then start talking.”
Colten nodded, his gaze shifting to Amika, then to Flora. Amika gave a subtle nod.
“Come on, Flora,” she said. “Let’s get something for Alfred’s head.”
Flora looked confused, her expression clearly skeptical. She wasn’t having it.
Alfred caught her hesitation and spoke gently. “Listen to Amika.”
Flora sighed loudly. “Fine.”
As the girls disappeared down the hall, Colten moved to the table and sat. Alfred followed, lowering himself into the chair with a wince.
Colten’s eyes locked onto Alfred’s, his tone suddenly serious. “Have you ever heard of the BNA?”
Alfred blinked, confused. “Um… probably not.”
Colten nodded slowly. “They’re an organization. Ruthless. Focused on taking over the government from the inside.”
Alfred didn’t respond, but his silence spoke volumes.
“Keep talking,” he said, voice low.
Colten leaned forward. “They’re eliminating anyone who still has a conscience. People with heart. People who resist. And they’re growing stronger—day by day.”
He paused, letting the weight of it settle.
“BNA stands for Base Network Assassins.”
Alfred’s stomach tightened.
“I’ve been trying to stop them,” Colten said, his voice low. “But with only a handful of allies, it’s not easy. The agent who knocked you out earlier—she’s one of mine. You don’t know her… but Nathan does. Very we'll.”
Alfred looked up sharply, breath catching in his throat. A name slipped out, barely a whisper.
“Reanna?” The air seemed to shift. Anger surged in his chest, not just at the revelation—but at the truth it confirmed. Nathan—his biological sister—was alive.
Colten saw it. The tension in Alfred’s eyes. The storm behind them.
“It wasn’t a choice, Alfred,” Colten said quietly.
His eyes shimmered with something raw—regret, maybe even pain.
Alfred held his gaze for a long moment. Then, slowly, the fury in his chest began to fade. He gave a single, reluctant nod.
Colten exhaled. “I need you to do something for me.”

“Find Letzier,” Colten said. “Tell him… I want to talk Bible.” Alfred frowned slightly. The phrasing was odd. It felt like there was more—something Colten wasn’t saying. But instinctively, he nodded.
That's if he knew where Letzier was?


**Flora**
Flora decided to head to bed, her eyes heavy with exhaustion. Amika had already handed Alfred the medicine, and the house had settled into a quiet lull. She was tired—bone-deep tired—so she slipped away to her room and curled beneath the covers.
But just as sleep began to pull her under, an image flickered in her mind.
**Zara.**
Clear as day. Her face, her voice. The ache in Flora’s chest returned like a wave crashing against the shore.
Then—words. Whispered, distant, but unmistakable.
Flora’s eyes snapped open.
She sat up, heart pounding. Sleep was no longer an option.
Maybe she just needed water. Something to ground her.
Flora swung her legs over the side of the bed and stood, the silence of the house pressing in around her like a blanket too heavy to shake off.

A small smile tugged at her lips.

“Aren’t you supposed to be in bed?” she asked softly.
Alfred nodded, just barely. “I’m just… thinking.”
Flora nodded back. “Yeah. Me too.”
Alfred glanced up at her. “About what?”
She didn’t answer. Didn’t want to. Some things weren’t meant to be shared with everyone—just God, and maybe her family.
Alfred caught the silence, gave her a look, then nodded. “Alright.”
There was a pause. Then Flora turned to him, her voice soft. “What about you? What are you thinking about?”
He looked up as if pondering, “Complicated.”
They stood there silently, the night wrapping around them like a blanket. Above, the stars shimmered—distant, quiet witnesses.
Flora tilted her head back, eyes tracing constellations. She wondered what it would feel like… when she finally graduated. Would she soar across the sky, free and untethered?
As if Alfred wasn’t beside her, as if the world paused just for her dreams. Her thoughts drifted.
Are you here, God? she whispered inwardly. Are you really? Or is it…
She didn’t want to question Him. But was it wrong if she did? She didn’t think so. She was human. He was God.
And somewhere in that vast difference, she hoped He understood.
And yet, the unforgotten whisper lingered—a voice in the silence. She didn’t dare speak aloud.
The words drifted around her like wind through the trees, soft but undeniable:
You are mine. And I will show you things you never dreamed you’d see…
You will hear what you never imagined you could hear.
You are seen.
Suddenly, Alfred spoke. “The silence feels different.”
Flora nodded, a half smile. And they just stood there.
Until they were tired.


**Letzier**
Letzier sat beside Daisy, her eyes gleaming like gemstones—she sparkled with a quiet brilliance, like the stars themselves. Daisy caught his gaze and gave a half-smile. “You’re staring at me again.” He chuckled.

She was probably irritated; most likely, it was because Nova interrupted their moment. He felt his heart ache with longing as she strode away.


He loved her, and he couldn’t let anything happen to her, even if it cost his life. Nova looked at Letzier. “I need you to get going… And…" Nova gave a long pause, then she said, “Be careful, Letzier… for Daisy’s sake.”
Letzier nodded.
“I wouldn’t disappoint her for the world,”


Nova smiled. “I know," he said, and he meant that. She had dealt with enough by losing Zara. If she lost him—no. He would do everything in his power to live, but if it came down to Daisy or himself? He knew what he would choose.
**Nathan**
Nathan sat near the window and watched, emotions looming over his mind. The looks everyone had were overwhelming him. No one seemed normal or looked normal. They hadn't seen Letzier in days, and Alfred had hurt himself the other night. Everything seemed strange to him. Flora was quieter, Dan… hadn't seemed himself.
“What was going on?” he murmured.
The days in school were quiet. Without Letzier, it felt… strange. Someone tapped on his shoulder; Nathan looked up to see Colten. “You okay, Nathan?” Colten said, worry evident in his voice.
Nathan gave a quick nod, “I'm alright..”
Colten shook his head.
“I know what it is, everyone seems off to you?” Nathann looked up, “they'd do, and it's bothering me, maybe a bit too much.”
Colten tilted his head slightly, “Indeed, they'd do. It might not make sense now, Nathan, but it will soon.”
Nathan felt confused. What does he mean? Just when he was about to ask, Colten spoke.
“How about you go and work on your studies?”
Nathan didn't respond; all that did was make his confusion worse.
Chapter 10
**Letzier**
He's training back at space school, training for the military, and across multiple countries, there's still war. His mind raced as he was doing sit up Andrue, his trainer, was yelling to move. He was moving all right. he looked over as he saw his mother. His face went pale. He is so grounded; he's eighteen, he can run away. He was glad that training only happened once a week; they wouldn't think anything bad if he skipped one. But not seeing his mom anymore, not calling her, not saying he was alright, he shivered in his boots; he was so dead. Andrue caught his expression and nodded. "Ten-minute break, everyone!"
Letzier nodded to Andruw and smirked. He walked towards his mom. And immediately, he spoke.
"Mom, I can explain—" The words died in his throat as she pulled him into a fierce hug.
"Foolish boy, you nearly gave me a heart attack." She released him, then promptly slapped his arm. "Don't ever scare me like that again."
Letzier stayed silent. He couldn't promise that—not with what Nova had revealed about the BNA, not with what he needed to do. His mother must have read something in his face because she changed the topic.
"Have you seen Alfred?"
Fear gripped him. In the chaos of the past week—Nova's revelations, the training, the search for WTB contacts—he'd nearly forgotten about his best friend. "No, is he okay?"
"He came by the house looking for you the other day. I just texted Alfred's grandma, Amy, that you're here. Alfred wants to see you."
Letzier's chest tightened. He'd left his friend in the dark between Nova's missions and space school training. He knows Alfred can help. Nova had said to find the WTB, and Alfred might know something, but that's if he knew something.
"Okay, Mama, I'll go." He pulled out his phone and called Zeb.
"Letzier! Where in the world have you been?!" Zeb's voice crackled with equal parts relief and frustration.
"Can I get a ride?"
"Of course you would be asking that—you have a lot of explaining to do"
Letzier didn't answer. Instead, he just acted as if nothing had happened. “I do?”
He heard Zeb sigh, “Where to?”
Letzier smiled.
"I'll tell you when you get here." Letzier needed to think. Nova had warned him to be careful who he trusted, but Alfred... Alfred, he could trust. When Zeb's hover vehicle pulled up, Letzier climbed in, his mind racing with possibilities.
"Okay, now can you tell me where we're going?"
"Alfred's house." And hopefully, some answers about the WTB.


**Alfred**
Alfred's head throbbed as he helped his grandma clean. He couldn't sit still with so many questions rattling around his aching skull.
"Alfred, your friends are here," his beloved grandma called out, probably relieved to see him finally getting visitors instead of pacing holes in her carpet.
"Thank you, Grandma," he managed, trying to sound normal despite the marching band in his head.
Opening the door, he saw Letzier and Zeb stepping out of the hover van. The relief hit him so hard he almost forgot to be angry. Almost.
"You made it," he said, fighting the urge to both hug and strangle his best friend. But he made sure to give him the look. Letzier shrugged it off…As if it didn't matter right now.
Letzier walked up the cement stairs, all business. "We need to talk somewhere private."
But Alfred was too annoyed to hear…He didn't even ask if he was ok.
"Yeah, getting knocked out by mysterious women tends to create conversation topics." Alfred's dry tone made Zeb raise an eyebrow. So did Letzier, but his was with the realization that his head was wrapped. It was random, but Alfred was annoyed. He shook his head and sighed.
“Come inside, we’ll talk in my room.”
They headed up to his room, and Alfred's rehearsed speech went out the window. Instead, he blurted, "Colten asked me to tell you that they need to discuss the Bible with you."
Letzier's head snapped up, a smile spreading across his face that made Alfred want to throw something at him.
“Yeah, that doesn't make any sense. I don't know why Colten would tell me that, but, you know,” Alfred said, glaring. “It wasn't like you were gone for an entire week, not like you to do that, while you were off playing secret agent," Alfred continued, gesturing to his bandaged forehead, "I've been getting concussions. You know what prevents concussions? Texting your best friend. Just a thought." He tried to maintain his annoyed expression, but relief at seeing Letzier safe made it difficult. "Seriously, man. A text. Even an emoji would've worked. Just... don't disappear like that again."


“I see you got hurt,” he commented, clearly disregarding the earlier remarks.


“Yeah, I did—by a girl,” Alfred admitted without hesitation.


Letzier giggled. “Dude, you were hitting on a girl. No wonder she hit you hard,” he said, teasingly. Alfred’s face flushed red. “No, I wasn’t! But that's not the point. I need to tell you what has been happening on my side, and how I got hit by a girl…”
He told him what had happened the night before.
And Letzier's eyes widened,
"And you said the women mentioned me and Daisy?" Letzier asked, his tone suddenly sharp with interest.
Alfred nodded. "Yeah. I don't know who she is. Colten's being so mysterious about everything."
"That's comforting," Letzier said, folding his hands and leaning forward. "For a moment I thought Nova was watching me, but now..."
Alfred's head snapped up. "Nova…The girl Zeb mentioned, at his place… The hacker girl who used to hang out with Zara?"
Letzier leaned in, urgency evident in his voice. “You won’t believe what I discovered,” he began, taking a deep breath as he launched into the astonishing tale of Zara’s survival. He detailed everything, including the involvement of Stone and Dan in the unfolding events, as we'll as the file he had found. Alfred's face looked pale as he mentioned Alfred and Flora being intelligent.
“…BNA is the one who made Zara's ship crash, not the Government, sorta….”


Letzier said, with a heaviness to his voice as if he was pondering it for the first time.
Alfred stepped back a few. “Wha-what?” Alfred felt so confused, he and Floar had like, “And the intelligent thing, the ability to read... others? Flora to be like ten steps ahead…And the school is a” Alfred felt a shiver go down his spine. “That's creepy.”
Letzier nodded.
“Yeah, my thought.”
Alfred smiled. “For you, it makes sense, you're always so strong for some reason, but me? Flora? That's kinda random.”


“Ima a kill Dan and Stone,” Zeb suddenly said, with a sound that Alfred never thought could come out of Zeb's mouth. Zeb has always been forgiving, even when it was hard, advising them to love Stone. Alfred and Letzier both looked at him in Shock.
“That's the first.” They both said.
“You're always the religious type,” Alfred said.
Zeb looked up at Letzier. Ignoring Alfred's comment. “What do we need to do?” Zeb said.
“we'll, let me tell you,” Letzier said. As he talked about Nova.
With a furrowed brow, he recounted his desperate search for Nova. “And we'll, I found her, pointing a gun at my date with Daisy,” he said, annoyed.
“But she did it with a good purpose,” Letzier said. Alfred chuckled,


“Yeah, I bet if she weren't Nova, you probably would kill her with one swift move,” Alfred said, chuckling. Sending a positive mood. “Yeah,” Letzier chuckled with Alfred, then continued about the WTB and why Colten told Alfred to tell him, and just like she said. And finally, many of the questions overwhelming his mind were being answered.


“So that's why,” Alfred said, but the emotion and all the information weighed heavily. Zeb stepped forward,
“So Colten is involved big time. But in a good way,” Zeb said. They both looked at Zeb. “we'll, it looks like that,” Letzier said.


“If he’s the one who made the agency WTB, then we need him and his team,” Letzier stated. Boldness. Letzier continued.
“Cuse what I'm planning, it requires everything we got.”
Zeb looked at him with curiosity. "What are you planning?" The question hung in the air, heavy with suspicion.
Letzier glanced between Zeb and Alfred, then dropped the bomb: "We're going to steal a spaceship to find Zara." He paused, almost sheepish. "It was my idea, since Nova wouldn't agree."
The silence that followed was deafening. Alfred's bandaged head suddenly didn't hurt so much—probably because his brain had short-circuited trying to process his best friend's casual announcement about grand theft spacecraft.


**Nathan**
Nathan decided to take a stroll, letting the morning air invigorate his senses. He felt like he could think again—at least a little—but he preferred to simply enjoy the day without overthinking. As he walked, he watched the sun reflect off the lake beside their house, the trees behind him, and the bushes surrounding their neighborhood. The road ran alongside him, and just a short distance ahead was the park where Flora and Zara used to walk.
**Zara.**
A reminder of his loss. His heart ached again at the memory of their promise. He remembered the loss of his parents, his younger sister Reanna, and now Zara.
“Lord, why is there so much loss?” he whispered.
No answer.
What did he expect? Lately, only silence. When was the last time he felt God's love? Heard his voice? He tried to remind himself of the times he’d seen God move in his life. One memory surfaced—the time his biological mom had spoken to him.
“What is a Christian?” he’d asked.
Her motherly eyes had looked at him, serious and steady.
“A Christian is a religion,” she said. “People call themselves Christians, worshiping their god, but not really knowing what true worship is.”
Nathan had pondered. “Then what is true worship?”
His mom smiled. “Spirit and in truth. We are lovers of Jesus—we keep him first, not other things, not tech, not stuff, or people. We love through the eyes of God. We are His bride. And that, my dear, is true worship.”
The memory felt real, maybe too real. He looked up. My god, this…is hard. He tried loving him, and all he got was pain. Pain from his past, pain of losing the people he cared most about, Nathan walked as if a tree appeared and he kicked it. Mad.
How can a God do that? Why would he do that? Suddenly, Flora appeared in front of him, causing him to take a step back.
“Flora, hi,” he said. She gave a slight smile. “Are you okay?” Nathan sighed. “Honestly, I’m not.” Flora nodded and replied, “Here,” as she wrapped her arms around him.
His sister, “Promise me something,” Nathan said.
Flora looked up. “Yeah?”
“Promise me that nothing will happen to you, and that—”
She interrupted him. “I cannot promise that; no one can promise that.”
He closed his eyes for a moment, “your right,”
She smiled, “Come, Colten sent me to get you, Alfred found Letzier, and they are coming over.”


Chapter 11


**Alfred**
Alfred's head throbbed as he helped his grandma clean. He couldn't sit still with so many questions rattling around his aching skull.
"Alfred, your friends are here," his beloved grandma called out, probably relieved to see him finally getting visitors instead of pacing holes in her carpet.
"Thank you, Grandma," he managed, trying to sound normal despite the marching band in his head.

"You made it," he said, fighting the urge to both hug and strangle his best friend. But he made sure to give him the look. Letzier shrugged it off…As if it didn't matter right now.

**Flora**
Flora and Nathan both step inside, Colten staring out the window, Amika standing beside the door.
She looked at both of them and smiled.
“Good, you got him.”
Suddenly, the atmosphere changed when Flora saw Colten look.
Amika gathered Nathan and Flora in the living room. Flora looked up, confused, while Nathan asked from behind them, "What's going on?"
Colten studied Flora, his expression unreadable, yet something about the way he held himself made her stomach tighten. He was holding back—something big.
The silence grew heavy as Nathan and Flora settled onto the sofa. Colten's face carried a weight Flora had never seen before. Amika turned to Colten and nodded her head to him.
"We've held back long enough, Colten," Amika said gently. "They should know."
Colten gave a quick nod, then turned to Flora. His voice came quietly but firmly.
"Zara... she's alive."
The words hit Flora like a tidal wave. Everything around her seemed to shrink, the air growing thick with disbelief. Her breath hitched, red curls slipping from behind her ear as she stared, frozen in place.
No. That couldn't be right.
Her fingers clenched around the fabric of her sleeve, gripping tighter as the weight of those words sank in.
"How do you know this is true?" she whispered, but even as she spoke, her voice trembled—like some part of her already knew Colten wasn't lying.
Letzier, Alfred, and Zeb walked through the door. Letzier looked at her and Nathan as realization hit him. "You told them."
Colten nodded, "I did. I'm glad you can make it, Letzier, Alfred, but where's Nova..." Colten trailed off, and the words echoed.
Letzier smiled. "One thing at a time. We'll go as soon as possible, but first," Letzier looked towards Flora and Nathan, then back at Colten.
Colten nodded; understanding flowed between them.
Flora couldn't move, couldn't think, couldn't understand. Who's Nova, and was Zara alive? How?? Alfred looked at her. "Flora, you ok? You look pale," he said. When Flora didn't say anything, he went to grab some water and handed it to her.
She reached for it. "How? This can't be possible, she was dead?" she said, opening the water bottle.
Letzier stepped forward, his jaw tight, his face drawn with something deeper than just concern.
"I heard Stone and Dan talking. They... sabotaged the spaceship, and the worst part is, they had help. Zara's lost somewhere on a planet we can't identify," he said, and even though his words were simple, they carried a heaviness that settled into the room like lead.
Nathan let out a shaky breath. "... Dan, my friend." His voice was hoarse, barely above a whisper. Flora, for a moment, forgot he was in the room. He blinked once, twice—then something in him shut down. His face paled, and the energy drained from his body as realization took hold.
Colten shifted slightly, eyes flickering toward Nathan, like he knew exactly what was running through his mind. Like he was keeping something else. Was there something more he was hiding? Amika, seated beside Flora, gave Colten a sharp look. A knowing look. That silent language between them, the unspoken understanding.
Colten exhaled deeply, shoulders sinking under the weight of the truth. "Yeah..." His voice was barely audible.
Flora felt her throat tighten. She could barely process anything beyond the pounding in her chest. Hope. Fear. Was it possible to feel both at the same time?
Colten stepped closer. "We need you both to help find her," he said, steady despite the turmoil swirling in the air. "Nathan. Flora. We need you. We're going to do something different—we're visiting a friend who can give us a download."
Letzier and Alfred shifted where they stood, and Flora noticed how ready they looked. They stood firm, side by side, the tension rolling off them like soldiers before battle.
For a moment, they almost looked like brothers—though Alfred's skin was darker, there was an undeniable presence between them. A silent understanding. A readiness.
Colten took a measured breath. "Get your things. We leave now." Flora swallowed past the knot in her throat and gave a small nod. "Okay," Flora said, though she couldn't believe him.
"I-I can't."
Nathan's voice cracked, raw and broken.
"I'm staying." Silence stretched, thick and suffocating. Colten studied him carefully, eyes flickering with something like knowing. After a beat, he simply nodded. "Okay, Nathan. That's your decision," he stated. Colten looked at her. "Flora, your sister is alive, but your face says you don't believe me," Colten said, sighing. Alfred gazed at Flora, watching.
Then Flora took a deep breath, releasing all the anxiety and shakiness, letting it all go. Something else replaced it—determination? Peace? She wasn't sure, but she looked up at him with newfound clarity. "What do you want me to do?" she said.
Alfred smiled, and he spoke, "we'll, from what Letzier has told me, we need to convince Nova to steal a spaceship." Flora nodded. "You all do that. I'm going to pack up everything."


**Letzier**
Letzier waited beside the car when a man walked by—someone he had never seen before. The man wore a white cloak and had a streak of blonde in his hair, while his eyes were hazel. Letzier tensed up, but when he blinked, the man had vanished.
A voice behind him startled Letzier without warning. He spun around and grabbed the person's arm, flipping him down to the ground. “Wow, Tence!” the man exclaimed as he stepped into view.
“Oh, Slieth, it's nice to see you're here,” Colten said, glancing at Letzier and then back toward where Slieth had been. Feeling unsettled, Letzier took a step back. Letzier crossed his arms. But the man, Slieth, smiled. “Colten was right, you are good.” Letzier remained silent, not wanting to speak. "Don't sneak up on me like that," Letzier finally said. Colten stepped between them. He turned to Slieth and asked, “How was Bible study?” Slieth smiled and replied, “It was great! Azreal and I had a good time.” Letzier relaxed, happy to hear his friend's name. Azreal from Class 87. Amika and Flora then finally came out. “Ready to go?” Amika asked. She looked at Slieth, and she smiled. “Hi Slieth," she said. Letzier felt impatient. “Let's go, I don't want to keep Daisy waiting.”


……….


Letzier followed close behind Colten as they entered the room. Nova stepped back from her computer, her shoulders stiffening the moment she saw them.
She recognized the look in their eyes—and she didn’t like it.
“No,” she said, before either of them could speak. “Whatever you’re planning, it’s too dangerous.”
Letzier opened his mouth. “Nova—”
“I already told you where Zara is,” she cut him off, fingers still flying across the keys. “That has to be enough.”
Colten stepped forward, his voice low and steady. “It’s not enough, and you know it.” There was a weight in his tone that Letzier hadn’t heard before. “That’s my daughter out there, Nova. Alone on that ship, thinking no one’s coming for her.”
Nova’s hands froze over the keyboard.
Letzier watched her carefully. “You think I don’t want to save her?” she said, her voice tight. “The BNA has eyes everywhere. One wrong move and—”
“And what?” Letzier snapped, stepping forward. “We let them win? Let Zara rot up there because we’re scared?”
“We’re not equipped for this,” Nova argued, but Letzier could hear the hesitation creeping in. “Even with the WTB’s help—”
“Then we get equipped,” Colten said. “You’re the best hacker we know. The government won’t help, but we can. Together.”
Nova spun in her chair, eyes flicking between them. Letzier held her gaze, letting her see the fire in his. He wasn’t backing down. Not this time.
She studied them both—his determination, Colten’s desperate hope. Letzier saw the shift in her eyes, the moment she remembered Zara. All those nights spent planning to expose the BNA, before everything went wrong.
“Fine,” she said at last, turning back to her screens. “But we do this smart. First, I need to hack deeper into their database. Find their weaknesses.” Letzier exhaled, tension easing just slightly as her fingers resumed their dance across the keys.
“And Colten?” she added.
He stepped closer. “Yes?”
A ghost of a smile touched her lips. “We’re going to need a bigger team.”
Chapter 12


**Flora**
She strode toward the woods with Amika, Zeb, Alfred, Letsier, and Colten—everyone was here except Nathan. The air was thick with tension, each step pressing deeper into uncertainty. Colten and Letzier had led them here separately, keeping their movements controlled, strategic. Flora stayed close to Alfred and Letsier, while Amika followed alongside Colten and Zeb. But what unsettled her most was how, in an instant, Letsier, Colten, and Amika vanished ahead, swallowed by the dense shadows. Her heart pounded. Her breath quickened. This was happening. They were going to find Zara.
The thought sent another wave of panic crashing through her. She hadn't even had time to fully believe it—her sister was alive—and now they were diving straight into the unknown?
Her eyes flicked to Alfred, searching for steadiness, but he only shrugged before gently tugging her hand forward. His grip was firm, reassuring, but it wasn’t enough to stop the whirlwind of emotions racing through her.
She pulled away as they stepped into the hidden passage, every nerve in her body alight with anticipation. Shock coursed through her veins.
This was it. Zara.
Her pulse quickened, her stomach twisting as they entered a dimly lit space filled with the hum of machinery. Screens flickered, casting a cool glow onto the metallic surfaces.
And then—she saw her.
A woman sat at the center of the room, her fingers moving fluidly over a keyboard. Flora stopped cold, eyes widening. She didn’t recognize this woman.
Her hair was a striking shade of violet, almost glowing in the artificial light, cascading down her back in sharp waves. The monitors reflected in her eyes as she studied the data in front of her, completely absorbed in whatever she was doing. Flora’s breath hitched. Was she supposed to know who this was?
Her thoughts scrambled for logic, for meaning, for something to grasp onto. Her chest tightened as realization crashed over her again. Zara was alive, but this stranger held the key to finding her.
Flora could barely summon words. "Who... who is she?" The woman barely glanced up, her fingers never pausing.
“I’m Nova,” she stated flatly, as if that name should mean something. Flora stiffened. Nova.
The hacker. The one Colten and Letzier had trusted to help them find Zara. Her throat tightened, her body frozen with shock. This was real. And it was happening now.
**Letzier**
Letzier leaned against the far wall, arms crossed, watching Nova gather Flora, Zeb, and Amika around the table. The room buzzed with quiet urgency. Finally, everyone was together.
"Here's what we know," Nova said, zooming in on a schematic. "The ship we need is at Space School's restricted hangar—one of their newest models. Security’s tight, but nothing I can’t handle. Our biggest challenge? Timing."
Letzier’s eyes flicked to Colten as Nova continued. "Your status as a former instructor gets us in the door. I’ve already created a field trip authorization under your name."
Letzier tensed. He saw the flicker in Nova’s eyes, the way her thoughts drifted toward Daisy.
"Daisy stays out of this," he said sharply, cutting through the moment.
Nova sighed, clearly frustrated. Letzier didn’t care. Daisy had been through enough. She wasn’t a pawn in this mission.
"We need more students to make this convincing," Nova muttered. "Alfred and Flora won’t be enough, and Nathan’s still on the fence."
"I can bring some of my students from Space School," Colten offered. Letzier caught the glint of strategy in his eyes. "They won’t question why they’re there—it’ll look completely natural."
Nova nodded, visibly relieved. Letzier stayed quiet, scanning the room. Every piece mattered now. Every person had to play their part.
Nova switched displays, highlighting red points on the map. "One of Colten’s agents—undercover intelligence—shows BNA operatives stationed here, here, and here. They’re watching, but they’re not expecting us to be this bold."
She pulled out a handful of glowing blue coins. Letzier recognized them instantly—emergency teleport tokens.
Letzier didn’t respond to Nova’s warning. He didn’t need to. Her words settled over him like a storm cloud, heavy and familiar. He gave a firm nod. “Alright, everyone’s dismissed.”
He knew what came next.
Colten stepped forward. “Nova,” he said. “This is Sileth.”
Letzier’s eyes narrowed as the man entered the room. He recognized him now—the stranger from earlier, the one who’d vanished after walking past the car. The same man, Letzier, had flipped to the ground on instinct. Not strong, but fast. He’d landed like a shadow and barely made a sound.
**Sileth.**
Nova glanced up, setting her tablet down. “You’re with the WTB.”
Sileth nodded once. “And you’re the hacker.”
Nova smirked. “That’s one way to put it.”
Letzier stepped closer, arms crossed, and kept his gaze fixed on Sileth. “He’s fast,” Letzier remarked. “Not much of a tank, but he moves like smoke.”
Sileth glanced at him with an unreadable expression. “You flipped me fast for a soldier. Maybe you could teach me,”
Letzier smiled in response. “I have my reasons.”
Sileth remained with his arms crossed.
“And I, my friend, follow orders.”
“Good,” Nova said, hopping off the desk.
“Because I don’t have time to babysit.”
Colten cleared his throat. “You’ll have plenty of time to get acquainted. For now, focus on the mission.”
Nova shrugged, already turning back to her tablet. “Sure. As long as he keeps up.”
Letzier caught the flicker in Sileth’s eyes—amusement, maybe. The guy was quiet, but not cold. He was watching everything, calculating. Letzier felt respect, but for now, they need to focus.
As Colten left, Letzier lingered by the doorway. He was curious and wanted to observe a bit more before exiting. Nova gestured towards the monitors.
“Once the plan is set, parents and family members, along with friends… it’ll be a lot worse after the ship is stolen. So the plan is that two or three must stay.”
Sileth didn’t move. “Understood. Who will stay then?”
Nova hesitated. Letzier saw it—the way her eyes darted, the way Sileth’s gaze pinned her in place.
“we'll, I told Colten about my worry,” she said, clearing her throat. “And he said you and me, and possibly Agent R.”
Letzier raised an eyebrow. “You and Sileth?”
Nova coughed, clearly bothered by the way Sileth was watching her. “Colten said he’d be suitable. His aim, his persistence, his speed…”
Sileth chuckled. Nova blinked. “What?”
“Nothing,” he said, slipping back into silence.
“Just that your face is extremely red,” he added.


“What!” Nova snapped.
Nova huffed, “I don't know what you're talking about, I'm just nervous about the mission.”
Sileth chuckled again,


“Or you're nervous about my quiet presence.”
Nova glared at him, and Sleth didn't move. Daisy appeared at the corner. Letzier smiled. She was watching too. Letzier watched her carefully. She was usually sharp, composed—but now her voice had a slight tremble.
He wasn’t sure if it was the mission or Sileth’s unnerving calm. Maybe both.


Letzier smirked. “You walked right into that one.”
Sileth chuckled again, but before Nova waved him off, he glanced at Letzier—just briefly. A flicker of acknowledgment. Like he knew Letzier had been watching the whole time, and didn’t mind.
Before leaving, Letzier found Daisy sitting by the window, staring outside.
He smiled at her, but his expression faded when he noticed the distress on her face. “What's wrong, Daisy?” he asked.
“I need to see if Mom's alright,” she replied. Letzier held his breath for a moment; he had forgotten about her parents. “You can’t, not yet,” he said. Daisy looked at him sternly.

Letzier sighed, hoping he wouldn’t regret his decision. “Alright, I get it. You can see them,” he said. Daisy's face lit up with joy.
“Only if you come with me,” he added. Daisy sighed in response. “Alright.”
Alfred


He couldn't believe he'd grabbed one of Colten's agents. He should have read between the lines. The more he replayed that moment on the sidewalk, the less he blamed her—he would've done the same thing, he thought grudgingly, though maybe with less theatrics.
Now he sat here, listening to Colten lecture about the ship's infield and emergency protocols, wondering how the man could look so calm. Like they weren't casually discussing stealing a ship. Meanwhile, Alfred's mind raced through every possible way this could go wrong. Getting caught. Everyone dying. Being by himself, he shivered at the thought.
His mind drifted to sparring with Letzier. He always convinced himself he'd lose before they even started fighting, even though Zara kept insisting he was better than he thought, especially when he was angry. Of course, he never believed her. He was too busy measuring himself against Letzier's standard to see his strength. He thought about Flora, the kindness in her heart; it felt like she saw everything inside, but didn't tell a soul. He felt that way with everyone else, too, though it nagged him about what Letzier had said about the file.


They all agreed not to tell Flora about the files that Letzier discovered. If the mission goes we'll and everyone survives, it would be better this way. She wouldn't be able to handle the worry for everyone like he was. His head started to hurt.

Chapter 13


Flora


Flora sat in the library, pretending to study star charts while her mind raced with mission plans. The afternoon sunlight streamed through tall windows, each tick of the clock bringing Friday closer.
"Earth to Flora!" Amika waved her hand playfully. "Your notes are upside down." Amika was pretending to be a student with a fake I'd and everything. Colten planned so that Amika could be with her for emotional support. And he was right, she was more than afraid, she was terrified. But she wouldn't let her fear have a hold on her.
Flora quickly flipped through her astronomy textbook, her cheeks flushing. "Sorry. I just keep thinking about—"
"Friday," Amika whispered, glancing around to ensure no one was listening. "I know. Me too." Flora noticed that Amika seemed more like herself, perhaps because Flora now knew that Amika was an agent. She wasn't sure.


Flora nodded, fidgeting with her pen. "It feels strange sitting here studying emergency protocols when we're about to..." She trailed off, not wanting to say too much, even in the empty library.

"True." Flora's fingers traced a diagram of spacecraft navigation systems. Hold on, Zara. We're coming.

"Probably worse," Flora smiled slightly, thinking of their friends all scattered around campus, each pretending this was just another normal week. "I bet Letzier's driving everyone crazy with his—"
Flora's heart nearly stopped. There he was—the man from the observation dome, standing in her school like he belonged there. Her mind raced with questions, with possibilities, with that same strange feeling she'd had when they'd first collided.
"Hello?" Amika's voice seemed distant, but Flora barely heard it.
"I'll be right back," she managed, her voice steadier than her racing pulse. Every step toward him felt charged with something he couldn't name.
"Hi! You're the man I bumped into." The words tumbled out before she could stop them.
He looked up, and his eyes widened with recognition. "Hi, yeah, we didn't, we..." His voice trailed off as they stared at each other, the library fading away around them.
"My name is Flora," she offered, a smile spreading across her face despite her nerves.
His answering smile made her heart skip. "I'm Zarek."
They stood there, studying each other, the air between them heavy with unspoken questions. Flora could feel Amika hovering nearby, probably bursting with curiosity, but she couldn't look away from Zarek's face. What was he doing here? Was this just a coincidence, or...?
"So..." Zarek cleared his throat. "You're a student here?"
Flora nodded, suddenly very aware of Amika watching them like a hawk. "Yeah, I am. And you're... A student also?" The question came out more hopeful than she'd intended.
"I'm a student as we'll here, recently joined, my older sister Claire, she comes here too, she is pretty popular," he said, running a hand through his hair. Was he nervous, too? She looked at him, “I don't think I know Claire.” He smiled.
"Small world, huh?"
"Yeah," Flora breathed. "Small." Their eyes met again, and that strange feeling from the observation dome came rushing back. Like they were supposed to meet, like this wasn't just a chance.
Amika chose that moment to not-so-subtly bump into Flora's shoulder. "Oh! Um, this is my friend Amika," Flora said quickly, breaking the spell.
"Nice to meet you," Zarek smiled, but his eyes kept drifting back to Flora. "I should probably get going, but..." He hesitated, like he wanted to say more but couldn't find the words
"But maybe we could..." Zarek started, then seemed to remember he was talking to a student. His face shifted, professional mask sliding back into place. "I mean, if you have any questions about physics..."
"Right, physics," Flora echoed, trying to hide her disappointment. She could feel Amika practically vibrating with contained excitement beside her.
Just then, Flora's phone buzzed. A text from Nova: "Need you here. Now."
The urgency of the message snapped her back to reality. Finding Zara, Betrayal with Stone, and Dan. Everything that was happening. Her world was so much more complicated than an attractive substitute teacher. And pulse, she wouldn't see him again anyway.
"I have to go," she said quickly, gathering her books. "But I'll see you in class?" The hope in her voice betrayed her attempt at casual.
"Yeah," Zarek smiled, and something in his eyes made her wonder if he was fighting the same pull she was. "See you in class."
As Flora hurried away with Amika, she could feel his gaze following her. Her mind spun with possibilities—was this just terrible timing, meeting him now when everything else was falling apart? Or was it exactly the right timing?
"Flora!" Amika whispered urgently once they were in the hallway. "What was that?"
"I don't know," Flora admitted, clutching her books to her chest. "But we need to get to Nova's. Something's happened.


**Nathan**
He was alone, walking on the sidewalk, his head down, like the weight of the world was on him. He kept repeating in his mind, his sister, Zara, was alive, and his best friend, Dan, betrayed him. He couldn't do it. His life was a lie. As he kept walking.
A mysterious young woman approached him, her gaze piercing, like Alfred's, and she wore a hoodie. He stopped, looking forward. But I am your long-lost sister, Reanna,” SHe said. And his whole world fell upside down. He looked at her, her Blue eyes gazed at him. **Letzier**
Letzier faced Amika again in combat, winning as usual. Coach Andrew nodded with his familiar, pleased smile. "Time! Letzier wins again."
Reaching down, Letzier grabbed Amika's hand to help him up. "I could have won," Amika said.
"Yeah, sure—in your dreams," Letzier replied with a smirk.
The weight of emotions pressed down on his shoulders. With all the planning and the ship reservation coming up this Friday... His thoughts were interrupted as he went to grab his things. Just as he was about to grab his last book, an AI Robot burst in through the doorway, firing missiles across the training area. Andrue yelled, “Everyone get down!!” Without hesitation, Letzier sprang into action. He dodged each missile with precision, closing the distance between himself and the robot. With one powerful punch, his fist went straight through the machine's core.
Letzier froze, staring at his hand as the robot crashed to the ground. Everyone, including Coach Andrew, stared at him in stunned silence.
"we'll done, Letzier," Andrew said, clapping his hands slowly, and then everyone started clapping.
Letzier shook his head, trying to process what had just happened. He stood there, taking deep breaths, his mind racing. What did I just do?
He laughed it off. "Oh, it was easy—didn't even graze my hand." Looking down at his unmarked fist, the truth of those words scared him. Memories flooded back: training since he was eight, punching rocks and whatever he could find, all to join the Space military. How had he become strong enough to destroy a Robot with his bare fists?
Amika came beside him. "You okay, you look under the weather?" he asked. He was a good friend.
"Yeah, I'm okay," Letzier replied, but uncertainty gnawed at him. "Anyway, I've got to head out."
As he left, a sense of foreboding settled over him. Whether for the mission or himself, something felt wrong. This strength of his—it could be either a blessing or a curse.
He heard a Ding coming from his phone. It was Daisy.
I need help, my mom is trying to move her stove, and Dad is not here. Please come over and help me.
Reading the message, he froze. He told her not to go without him. Maybe he should text Nova…but then again, she did really want to see him the other day.
He ponders for a moment. Should he. He felt super hesitant, but then. Suddenly, a thought struck him, she went to her Parents' house without him, her mom wasn't home… which made her vulnerable…He dropped his phone and dashed.
Letzier's
His heart was pounding, his ears ringing, his mind a whirlwind of emotions. He knew the BNA was waiting, but all he wanted was to get a hold of their throats. If they hurt her, they would pay.
He got to the house, kicking the door hard enough that it opened with ease. His mind spun.
There she was—his Daisy—with tears streaming down her beautiful face as guards gripped her arms. The terror in her eyes struck him like a physical blow.
His anger held on to him like a fierce grip.
There were at least twenty guards in one room. He went at them with a kick; he had no weapons, just his fists. He moved—one after another.
Anger fumed, and he grabbed the guard, holding him down. At this point, he figured he might not make it. So he pushed harder, killing at least three guards in the process. His raging anger couldn’t think—other than: no mercy.
Then Daisy—his brave, brilliant Daisy—twisted free. The glass jar she hurled caught the evening light like a diamond, and something ancient and protective roared to life inside him. They wouldn't take her. They wouldn't destroy what they'd built together.
He exploded into motion, every strike carrying not just training but love, desperation, and pure fury. Guards flew back as he fought with everything he had, their bodies crashing into walls. Some didn't get up, and the part of him that once cared about holding back was buried beneath the need to protect her, to save their future together.
**"Letzier!"**
Her scream shredded his heart. He spun to see a guard's arm crushing her throat, and the sight of her gasping for air made his world spin with horror. In that split second of pure, blinding terror, something wet hit his face. He couldn't see, with all the chaos.
"Wha—" His body began to betray him even as his mind screamed in rebellion. The exhaustion hit like an avalanche, and panic clawed at his chest as his limbs turned to lead. No, please no—he had to reach her, had to save her, had to tell her one more time that he loved her...
The last thing he saw was Daisy's hand reaching for him, tears glinting on her cheeks as she screamed his name. Her voice followed him into the darkness as he fell, the weight of his failure crushing his heart more than any drug ever could.
I'm sorry, my love. I'm so sorry…
**Nathan**
Nathan ran as hard as he could, an inexplicable urge driving him to reach Colten. How far did he walk, a mile or two? He was pretty sure that whatever was happening, Letzier wouldn't give up without a fight, but he felt as if it were too late. It took him a moment or two to process what his sister said to him. That's if she was even his sister., Every second felt like an hour to him. School had most likely ended, so they should still be there. Once he finally saw his house, he didn't waste a moment. **Alfred**
When they reached Letzier's house, Alfred's heart was already racing. They knocked, each second of waiting feeling like an eternity, until Letzier's mom appeared in the doorway.
"Is Letzier with you?" Alfred tried to keep his voice steady, fighting back the dread building in his chest.
"No, you might find him at Daisy’s house." Her innocent smile made Alfred's stomach turn—she had no idea her son was walking into danger.
Alfred and Nathan shared a look of silent horror, but forced their faces to stay calm. "Okay, thanks," they managed together. The moment the door closed, they ran as if their lives depended on it—because Letzier's might.
When they finally reached Daisy's house, Alfred felt his world tilt sideways. Police cars everywhere, their harsh lights cutting through the evening air. On the lawn, Daisy's parents clung to each other, their sobs tearing through the chaos.
"No, no, no," Alfred's whisper was heavy with despair. His feet carried him toward the door, even as his mind screamed that he wasn't ready for what he might find. A cop stepped into his path.
"I can't let you go in."
"we'll, I'm going. My—" Alfred's voice cracked. Letzier wasn't just his friend—he was his brother in everything but blood.
"I know, but we believe your friend was the one who kidnapped his girlfriend, Daisy. You can't go in there."
Something's napped inside Alfred. Rage blazed through him, hot and fierce. How dare they accuse Letzier? They didn't know him—didn't know how he looked at Daisy like she hung the stars, how he'd rather die than hurt her.
He pushed past the officer, leaving Nathan outside. The house—it was like walking into a nightmare. Shattered glass crunched under his feet, furniture thrown aside like toys. But it was the small details that hit hardest: Daisy's textbook split open on the floor, pages torn and scattered. Letzier's jacket crumpled in the corner, the one he always wore because Daisy had given it to him.
Alfred's trained eye took in every detail, each piece of evidence telling the story the police couldn't see. This wasn't a kidnapping by Letzier—this was an attack. His fists clenched as the truth crystallized: the BNA had taken them both, and he hadn't been there to stop it.
"No, not my friend," he whispered to the empty room, his voice thick with guilt. "I'm so sorry. But I swear, I’ll look for you." The room fell into a silence. He looked around, saw Daisy's phone, and picked it up. And fear told him. Someone messaged her, someone named Jay.
"You can't be in here!" The cop's shout echoed through the destroyed room.
Alfred nodded to the cop, deliberately barking his words: "Understood. I've seen enough." Let them think he believed their lies about Letzier's betrayal. Let them think he was just another friend feeling deceived. They didn't need to know the real betrayal came from above—from the government, from Dan, and from Stone, that snake.
He stepped outside. "Let's go," he said to Nathan. Nathan nodded, understanding the weight of the situation without words.
After calling Zeb for pickup, they climbed the stairs, Alfred's head low with the burden of knowledge. When Flora opened the door, her eyes widened, and the defeat in her expression shocked everyone into silence.
But this wasn't like a death. No—Letzier was out there, fighting to survive. And that's what made it so shocking. Letzier was their best fighter, undefeated, unstoppable. How could he have been captured unless they somehow outsmarted him? He wasn't sure; he just hoped.
**Nathan**
Nathan sat on his bed replaying the moments in his mind. Dan's betrayal, Zara was alive…Reanna. A mixture of Hope and Betrayal repeated.
Zara's warm face loomed in his mind as his friend's words haunted him, “Dan, why?” Now, Letzier was captured. He didn't make it in time.

Colten didn't trust Nathan enough to tell him that his sister was alive, that they were agents, and didn't bother to tell him that Dan would ruin his life.
Slammed his hand against the table, then dropped to his knees, his gaze locked on the floor. His shoulders trembled.
He was done pretending. Done holding it in. Done acting like everything was okay.
“’Cause it wasn’t anymore,” he breathed. “I’m not okay.”
Tears streamed down his face. It was never okay. He had tried—tried reaching for God, tried holding on—and this is where it got him.
Just then, the door creaked open. Flora stepped in, her eyes mirroring his pain.
She didn’t say much. She didn’t have to.
She knelt beside him, and they wrapped their arms around each other. And together, they sobbed.
Chapter 14
**Flora**

Alfred told her what the file had said, what Letzier had told him, and what abilities they might have. Alfred paused. “I wasn't going to tell you, but for your safety, it's best if I do.”

**Letzier**
Letzier woke up chained against a wall, his head swimming in fog. No door in sight—just walls. No windows. His head pounded with each heartbeat. Daisy. The memory of her hurt stabbed through him. "Hey!! Where is she? Tell me where she is or you're all dead!" he barked, rage burning through his veins. Their answering laughter only stoked his anger higher.
"She's safe, we'll taken care of," Coach Andrew's voice echoed through hidden speakers. The familiar voice made Letzier's stomach turn.
Suddenly, a door materialized in the wall, sliding open to reveal a vast white room. The chains released, and Letzier stumbled forward, his muscles tense.

The memory flashed in Letzier's mind: the training room, the robot attacking, his fist tearing through metal like paper. His shock at his strength.
"I've been watching you grow stronger," Andrew continued. "But today... Today proved what I've suspected all along. You're special, Letzier. And now?"
Multiple doors opened along the walls, revealing robots similar to the one he'd destroyed. "Now we're going to see exactly how special."

**Nathan**

The walls didn’t reflect light—they seemed to absorb it, casting an eerie, unnatural shade over the scene.

**Flora**
